# AthenaOS Master Checklist

> **Athena override (2026-07-13):** The design bible is [`Athena_Concept.md`](Athena_Concept.md)
> (embodied AGI). Gaming-desktop items below are **parked** — see
> [`LEGACY_GAMING_CONCEPT.md`](LEGACY_GAMING_CONCEPT.md) and [`docs/PARKED_GAMING.md`](docs/PARKED_GAMING.md).
> Prefer AthBody / AthSense / AthMind / AthVoice / AthGuard work over AthPlay, Steam, or anti-cheat.

The checklist below is **bootstrap residue** from the earlier tree. Use it for kernel/driver
bring-up evidence only; do not treat gaming phases as Athena 1.0 scope.

**Agent workflow:** pick the smallest *unblocked* **embodiment or kernel** item → working code →
`xtask` build → QEMU boot → update status honestly. Per-agent rules: `CLAUDE.md`, `AGENTS.md`.

## ✅ BARE-METAL PROVEN LEDGER — everything with real-EliteMini evidence (consolidated 2026-07-07, opus)

**Goal context: AthKernel bring-up quality on EliteMini / dev-host.** This is the single consolidated inventory of everything proven on the real Beelink EliteMini (Ryzen 5 7640HS, Zen4 family 0x19) — the honest `[x]` baseline. It supersedes the scattered per-session IRON VERIFICATION blocks below (those stay as the dated evidence trail; this table is the roll-up).

**What counts as bare-metal `[x]` here:** a specific PASS/OK serial marker in a real-host transcript — either a **true iron-flash** boot (internal-ESP series `2026-06-11`→`06-16`; the `2026-07-02` cold-boot DCN milestone) **or** a **no-flash KVM `-cpu host`** boot on real Zen4 silicon (`06-25`, `06-27`, `07-04` series — the `-cpu host` precedent runs AMD-family/pure-logic code paths on real silicon, so they earn `[x]` for the *mechanism*; live-peripheral *effects* stay `[~]`). Pure QEMU-TCG is excluded. Transcripts live in `logs/` (index: `logs/README.md`).

### Proven on real Zen4 — by subsystem

| Area | Proven on bare metal (representative marker) |
|---|---|
| **CPU / SMP** | AMD MSR vendor gate (`[msr] vendor=Amd … PASS`); AMD CPPC/SVM/SMCA MSRs; **SMP AP bring-up 2/2, x2APIC, TSC sync `max_warp=0`** (SMP=1/2/**4**, 5-boot matrix 07-04); Spectre branch-spec MSRs real (`SPEC_CTRL … ibrs/stibp/ssbd/ibpb readback=0x7`); live-Zen4 vuln posture (`meltdown=Not affected spectre_v2=Mitigated …`) |
| **Memory / MM** | Heap freelist guard (702k live validations, intact); **real CR4 SMEP + SMAP** (behavioral trap `nonstac_read_faults=true`); UMIP trap (blocks SGDT/SIDT@CPL>0); uaccess stac/clac chokepoint; buddy allocator + swap roundtrip + map-hardening |
| **ACPI / thermal / power** | AMD cpu-temp *decode* logic; thermal breach → passive-cap → critical-shutdown intent; per-component (NVMe SMART/GPU/SSD); ACPI vendor-quirks, PIT/HPET fallback, PCI D-state encode, cpuidle C0/C1 |
| **Storage / USB** | xHCI **USB-MSC bulk bring-up** (SET_CONFIGURATION OK); xHCI **HID boot device** interrupt-IN multi-slot (SS/HS/FS); HID-ring recycle (16 TDs/3 laps); FAT32 formatter + CRC32 + 1 MiB-GPT-align + boot-artifact write/readback; **internal-ESP `BOOTLOG.TXT` persistence (true iron)** |
| **Networking** | ★ **RTL8125 2.5GbE RX LIVE → DHCP Bound → real router lease** — `[rtl] RX path LIVE: first frame received` + `[DHCP] Configured: IP 192.168.1.244/24, GW 192.168.1.1, DNS servers: 1`, **stable across polls 100/300/600 (~30 s), no re-DORA** (true iron flash, `logs/BOOTLOG_20260624_183116.dump.txt` + 5 more 06-24 boots); TLS 1.3 handshake (X25519+HKDF+SHA256+ChaCha20Poly1305); **DNSSEC algorithm-COMPLETE** (Ed25519/ECDSA-P256/P384/RSASHA256/512 → `DNS selftest 51/51`); kernel **WireGuard** Noise IKpsk2 handshake confirmed; DHCP handshake + parser DoS-resilience; mDNS/DoT wire; IPv6 dual-stack + EUI-64 |
| **Audio** | HDA **test-tone playback** (`wrote_samples=960 hda_playback=1`); mixer; submit path; **codec walk** (DAC/output-pin/stream armed); interface lock/restore |
| **Graphics / GPU** | ★ **DCN desktop scanout — real Radeon 760M scans the live desktop, MES-free, owner saw it on the panel** (true iron cold boot 07-02); EDID real 1080p decode; amdgpud match-mode enum on iron (real BDF `c4:00.0`, 12/12 firmware); cold-GFX PSP-autoload first-light; compositor glassmorphism / drop-shadows / VRR pacing |
| **Filesystem / AthFS** | Superblock format (Apex root); rollback round-trip; **CoW journal crash-revert + fsck**; **AES-256-XTS encryption through AES-NI**; per-app **bucket-key isolation** (`cross_app_unreadable`); per-file key derivation; installer superblock/journal-replay/lz4 |
| **Security / crypto / AthGuard** | **Hardware AES-NI** (FIPS-197 match, XMM-preserved); **RDSEED/RDRAND** hw-entropy seeding; constant-time compare; **IOMMU AMD-Vi** DMA confinement + wild-DMA isolation + DTE install; secure-boot trust-anchor + manifest verify + chain (tamper→restore); kernel anti-rootkit integrity monitor (live SHA-256 of IDT/LSTAR); **attestation fails CLOSED** w/o hw TPM; FDE passphrase verify; TPM seal/unseal + FDE auto-unlock (software TPM); full crypto KAT suite (Ed25519/X25519/ChaCha20Poly1305/BLAKE2s/SHA-256/HMAC/ECDSA-P256/Argon2id) |
| **Scheduler / SCHED_BODY** | **Work-stealing ON**, steal-probe exercises the once-#DF path (`workers=4/4 stolen=4 aborts_delta=0`, `switch_aborts:0` ×5 boots); zombie-wake / stack-sanity / deadline telemetry / kill-reclaim guards; procfs snapshot self-check (107/107, no wedge); per-game CPU-power cap + refresh switch |
| **Shell / UI / input / a11y** | True tiling resize; taskbar render; swappable WM (tile/stack/float); widgets; athlang scripting; theme-bundle install; notifications + command palette; OOBE/login (post-OBSIDIAN); sticky/slow/bounce keys + repeat; a11y tree + focus-order + magnifier; generic HID-gamepad descriptor parser |
| **Platform / misc** | LinuxKPI Phase 1–3; watchdog stall-detection; install account/password + partition planner + app-bundle verifier; A/B kernel-slot switch + boot-fallback rollback; crash persist + plain-language report; **every listed iron boot: `boot health 7/7 -> HEALTHY`, 0 panics** |

### Held at `[~]` — needs a real peripheral / sensor (the bare-metal backlog toward daily-driver)

These are the honest gaps a person would actually hit — the daily-driver push must close them on real hardware:
- **Live application/service traffic over the real link** — the RTL8125 RX + DHCP-Bound + real router lease are **iron-PROVEN** (06-24, moved to the proven table above); what's still unexercised on the physical wire is a *service* round-trip (a TLS handshake to a real HTTPS server, an SSH session into the box at `192.168.1.244`). Not a driver gap — needs the SSH TCP service wired + a boot that runs it. The `[~]` KVM sweeps that still say "RTL8125 RX needed" (README rows) are STALE — superseded by the 06-24 iron dumps.
- **Real USB-device enumeration** (physical stick through the hub) — the install-media path. **Now the highest-leverage single bare-metal item** (the RX item that used to hold this slot is done).
- **AMD live CPU temperature via SMN** (`live=-1C` in KVM) · real **P-state/cpufreq** DVFS · **S3 suspend→resume on iron** (device re-resume + AP re-online).
- **External-panel mode-switch effect** · **DualSense full parity** (haptics/triggers/mic) + real-controller tap→GameOS loop · multi-controller xHCI.
- **Full amdgpu 3D / CP-ring / MES** bring-up (only the DISPLAY/DCN scanout path is proven; every GPU boot still ends `amdgpu_device_init FAILED` at the CP ring — the open GPU campaign).
- **Real-TPM2 SRK-sealed FDE** (Athena has no TPM2; software-TPM path proven) · **installer boot-mode swap** (`user_init` replacement) · **OOM kill+recover** path (only victim-selection ran).
- **12-CPU post-marker work-stealing wedge** — chip stays OPEN; KVM never reproduced it, only a true iron boot retires it.

### Known iron FAIL set — expected / out-of-lane (NOT regressions)

`usb-msc write_rt_ok=false` = the safe-mode write gate *working* (stick enumerated fine) · install-GPT under KVM (needs real media) · `[mce] decode` FAIL rides another lane's uncommitted WIP · AthBridge `FullCompatSession`/`ExitProcess(0)`/`advapi32 thunks` = human-gated guest-exec (registry thunks pass host-KAT 5/5). Also not-failures: `[buddy] double-free` and IOMMU/AER fault-inject lines are self-tests whose "PANIC"-substring is a `survives(no-panic)=true` *result*.

### GPU render-seam bring-up — verification + KAT hardening of the upstream-amdgpu render path (2026-07-12, opus) [~] QEMU

Verified GPT Sol's in-progress LinuxKPI-hosted **upstream amdgpu render-node** work (the `/dev/dri/renderD128` seam per `docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-06-gpu-real-submit-design.md` M2, informed by `docs/gpu-oracle/ATHENA-AMDGPU-DRM-ABI-20260711.md`) through the default-build proof ladder, and hardened the pure-logic surfaces it added. The real render path itself is **iron-gated** — it is `#[cfg(feature = "real_amdgpu_init")]` (off by default, needs the vendored GPL C tree + `m4c-link.sh`) and QEMU has no Radeon, so amdgpud self-skips (`9099`). What is proven here is that the work builds + boots clean and its supporting logic is now covered.
- **Real bug fixed — daemon heap-init TOCTOU (`components/ath_linuxkpi/src/mm.rs`).** `ensure_init()` used a bare `HEAP_INIT` compare-exchange, so a thread that lost the CAS could reach `allocate_first_fit` before the winner finished `HEAP.init()` → spurious `-ENOMEM`. Exposed as a RED KAT (`drm_exec::…lock_slow_contended…` intermittently asserted `-12`) under the parallel host-test harness. Fixed with double-checked locking under the heap's own lock (fast path unchanged for the single-threaded daemon). 57→57 KATs now green across repeated parallel runs.
- **+4 FAIL-able host KATs** for new surfaces GPT Sol shipped without coverage (GEM handle tables use xarray; syncobj/fence arrays use dma_fence): `xa_cmpxchg` insert/swap/reject/erase; `dma_fence_array_first`/`_next` iteration + non-array pass-through; `dma_fence_allocate_private_stub` signaled+timestamp; and the `memdup_array_user`/`kvmalloc_array`/`kvcalloc` integer-overflow guards (undersized-alloc heap-smash class). ath_linuxkpi lib KATs **57 → 61**.
- **Proof:** `cargo test -p ath_linuxkpi --features hosttest --lib` 61/61 · `cargo test -p ath_amdgpu` 115/115 (no regression) · `cargo run -p xtask --release -- build --release` exit 0 · QEMU CI `System successfully booted`, 0 PANIC, amdgpud lifecycle `7600`→`7602`→`9099` (confirms the new spawn-and-detach + drain-on-9099 rework in `user_init`/`xtask` — user_init no longer blocks on the now-persistent daemon). Pre-existing `[boot] WARN` (TCG boot time) unchanged — not a regression from this work.
- **Not commit-ready as-is** (unchanged from review): `kernel/src/interrupts.rs` carries a hardcoded magic RIP (`0x5D127`) ABI-register debug probe tied to one binary layout (left in place — it's an active debug aid for the AMDGPU boundary fault, not mine to remove); the render C (`bringup_render.c`, `bringup_xcp_none.c`) can only be validated by `m4c-link.sh` against the vendored tree (absent locally) or on iron. Next real milestone is hardware: fetch tree → `FREESTANDING=1 bash linuxkpi-drm/m4c-link.sh` → Athena boot to exercise GEM_CREATE→GEM_VA→CS→IRQ-fence.

### renderD128 broker — step 2 design + fail-closed ioctl-dispatch foundation (2026-07-12, opus) [~] host-KAT

Started the owner's step-2 GPU slice (the `/dev/dri/renderD128` capability broker) with design + the first host-testable layer, while step-1 (the render-client lifecycle) awaits an Athena boot (hardware-gated; owner runs it). **No kernel wiring yet — this is design + pure logic, hardware/QEMU validation pending step 1.**
- **Design spec** `docs/research/renderD128-broker-design.md`: the trust boundary (game holds only `Cap::Gpu` + one cap-gated shmem channel, never GPU MMIO/DMA — the AthGuard "anti-cheat without ring 0" line), the step-2 behavior contract mapped to mechanism (open/close/ioctl/mmap, multi-client isolation, fail-closed, daemon-death→ENODEV), the steward's batched `[interface]` plan (VFS device node + `SYS_IOCTL`/`SYS_MMAP` arm gated on `Cap::Gpu`; request/reply queue on a `Cap::Channel` shmem frame the client never maps), and the proof ladder.
- **New crate `components/ath_render_broker`** (`#![no_std]`, host-testable, kernel-linkable — builds clean for `x86_64-unknown-none`): the fail-closed heart of `ioctl()` forwarding. `decode()`/`dispatch()` over the Linux `_IOC` layout + an allowlist of the 3 generic DRM ioctls the RADV trace uses + the 17 AMDGPU render ioctls `bringup_render.c` registers, each `(nr, size, copy)` transcribed from the Athena oracle. Dispatch is on **(type, nr, size)** — the client's `dir` bits are ignored — so both observed `GEM_VA` encodings (`0x40406448` `_IOW` header and Mesa's `0xc0406448` `_IOWR`) normalize to one command (step-3's explicit requirement), and the broker copies exactly the allowlisted size (no client-controlled over-read/write). Unknown type→`-ENOTTY`, unknown nr / size-mismatch→`-EINVAL`, all fail closed.
- **Proof:** `cargo test -p ath_render_broker` **8/8** — every captured ioctl resolves to its spec; the GEM-VA direction-bit variance normalizes to one `Resolved`; wrong-type / unknown-command / size-mismatch fail closed; no registered struct exceeds `MAX_PAYLOAD`; no duplicate command numbers. FAIL-able by construction (asserts exact names/sizes/copy-plans + the two-encoding equivalence). Crate not yet linked into the kernel, so the safe build is unchanged from this session's two green boots.
- **Next slice (after step-1 Athena proof):** wire the VFS node + session table + shmem request/reply queue + daemon-death revocation, landing the `[interface]` ABI in one batched steward commit.

### GPU DISPLAY MILESTONE — the real DCN scans the AthenaOS desktop, MES-free (2026-07-02, opus) [x] IRON

**The Radeon 760M's display engine now scans out the live AthenaOS desktop on Athena's panel — the first working GPU display path, with the MES entirely bypassed.** Chain (all on iron, cold boot): amdgpud PSP→AUTOLOAD_RLC→first-light → `try_page_flip` points DCN HUBP0 at a carveout FB (readback STUCK = we own the scanout register) → `SYS_RAEGFX_REGISTER_SCANOUT(143)` registers that same buffer with the compositor → kernel maps the carveout write-back (`memory::map_phys_wb`) → compositor presents each frame there + `clflush`es for the non-snooped DCN read path → **`init_rings` (the MES `set_hw_resources` SoC-reset stage) is SKIPPED** — daemon exits clean, machine stays alive, desktop live until the safe-mode auto-return. Evidence: `logs/bootlog-20260702-dcn-desktop-scanout.txt` (`BYPASS: DCN desktop scanout register -> OK`, `[compositor] GPU scanout attached`, OTG CRC varying = live scanned content) + **owner saw the AthenaOS desktop on the glass**. Fixes landed en route: (1) `lkpi_ioremap` now PROGRAMS an unassigned PCIe BAR from the q35 PCI hole (OVMF leaves the passed-through APU's BAR5/BAR2 at 0 — generic robustness, any firmware that skips a BAR); (2) scanout stride units bug (syscall passes BYTES, `Scanout.stride` is consumed as PIXELS — the "garbage screen"); (3) WB+`clflush` present (the first UC mapping made the present ~200 ms/frame → CPU0 pegged, wedge-alike); (4) `lkpi_register_scanout` carveout ownership gate (same security model as MAP_PHYS: every page firmware-reserved, never usable RAM). **Honest scope:** this is the DISPLAY engine (zero-copy desktop scanout) — NOT 3D/compute submit; the MES remains the gate for GFX rings/games (campaign below). Hardening follow-ups: read `MMMC_VM_FB_OFFSET` live instead of the Athena `0x3E0000000` const; damage-tracked/SDMA present to cut the full-frame clflush.

### Security FIX — CRITICAL userspace-driver capability sandbox escape (2026-07-06, opus) [~] QEMU, iron pending

**Closed a CRITICAL sandbox escape: the userspace-driver syscalls `register`(109)/`claim_device`(111)/`enable_dma`(113)/`release_device`(112) had NO capability check and NO ownership check, so ANY unprivileged/sandboxed task could register a self-owned driver, claim an arbitrary PCI device (NVMe, NIC, IOMMU), receive a `Cap::Mmio{MAP}` over its BARs, `SYS_MMIO_MAP` them into its own address space, and drive the hardware directly — a full DMA-capable escape to ring-0-equivalent power.** Found by a 4-boundary kernel security audit (syscall edge / capability / device-input / memory isolation). The sibling `sys_dma_map`/`sys_dma_unmap`/`sys_deliver_irq_setup` already enforced `owner_task == caller`; claim/release/enable_dma/register did not, and nothing gated the privileged authority at all.
- Fix (`kernel/src/userspace_driver.rs`): new fail-CLOSED `caller_holds_driver_authority()` (requires a held `Cap::System{WRITE}` — the same gate as `SYS_ATHENA_SHUTDOWN`/`SYS_INSTALL_RUN`; every task starts with an empty `CapTable`, so unprivileged apps are denied) gates `sys_register`/`sys_claim_device`/`sys_enable_dma`; new `caller_owns_driver()` adds the missing `owner_task == caller` check to claim/release/enable_dma (driver handles are a global monotonic counter → cross-task guessable). New `ERR_NO_AUTHORITY`. The real claim path split into ungated internal `claim_device_by_bdf` so the boot smoketest still exercises PCI enumerate+BAR-probe while the syscall wrapper is gated. The in-kernel boot smoketest calls the internal helpers directly, so driver bring-up is unaffected.
- **FAIL-able proof** in `userspace_driver::run_boot_smoketest`: the boot bootstrap context holds no `Cap::System{WRITE}`, so a `sys_claim_device` from it MUST be refused — `[usdriver] cap-gate smoketest: PASS (unauthorized sys_claim_device refused rc=0x…f50e)`. A regression to fail-open prints `FAIL … SANDBOX ESCAPE`. **QEMU CI:** build exit 0, `System successfully booted`, 0 PANIC, cap-gate PASS, driver lifecycle + PCI handoff still OK. `[~]` QEMU; iron pending.
- Follow-up: least-privilege refinement to a dedicated `Cap::Device`/driver cap (Phase 9 manifest work) instead of the coarse `Cap::System{WRITE}`; wire kernel enforcement to consult the richer `athshield` policy engine (today unreachable). Also open from the same audit: SYS_SPAWN(11) ungated (HIGH), Linux `read_user_buf` unbounded-length alloc DoS (HIGH), NVMe phantom-completion CID validation (HIGH).
- **[~] REGRESSION CLOSED — first-party driver daemons re-authorized to claim hardware (2026-07-08, opus).** The `5731136` claim gate (above) locked out the *legitimate* consumers too: `amdgpud`/`i915d`/`nvidiad` spawn via `sys_spawn` with an empty `CapTable`, so on the 2026-07-08 VFIO passthrough run the guest matched the real Phoenix1 iGPU (`vendor 0x1002 @ 00:03.0`, firmware 12/12) but `sys_claim_device` returned `ERR_NO_AUTHORITY` (`f50e`) — the `no AMD GPU found — expected on QEMU` line was a red herring (amdgpud prints it on ANY claim failure). Fix (`kernel/src/userspace_driver.rs` + `syscall.rs` SYS_SPAWN): `maybe_seed_driver_daemon()` delegates a `Cap::System{WRITE}` into a freshly-spawned child IFF (a) the child is an allowlisted first-party driver binary (`amdgpud`/`i915d`/`nvidiad`, basename-matched) AND (b) the spawning **parent already holds** `Cap::System{WRITE}`. Condition (b) makes it capability *delegation*, not amplification — safe even with SYS_SPAWN ungated: an unprivileged spawner holds no System cap, so it delegates nothing and the child still hits the gate. **FAIL-able proof:** `[usdriver] driver-seed policy smoketest: PASS` drives the full truth table (authorized+daemon→grant; unauthorized parent→refuse; non-daemon→refuse; path-prefixed→grant) and prints `FAIL … OVER-GRANT` on any regression; the `5731136` `cap-gate smoketest` still PASSes (unchanged). **QEMU CI:** build exit 0, `System successfully booted`, 0 PANIC, both smoketests PASS, and the runtime seed fires for all three daemons (`seeded driver authority … 'amdgpud' (task 100) — delegated from authorized parent`). `[~]` QEMU; iron/VFIO pending (next passthrough run should now clear the claim and exercise the real amdgpu init ring). Follow-up unchanged: replace the coarse `Cap::System{WRITE}` with a device-class-scoped `Cap::Gpu`/`Cap::Device` (Phase 9) so a GPU daemon cannot also reach `SYS_ATHENA_SHUTDOWN`/perm-prompt respond.

### Security FIX — native user address space was fully W+X (NX never set) (2026-07-06, opus) [~] QEMU, iron pending

**Made the native user address space W^X-compliant, matching the NX baseline every modern OS ships.** The native ELF loader (`kernel/src/elf.rs`) mapped EVERY `PT_LOAD` segment executable (ignoring `PF_X` entirely), and all three user-stack mapping sites (`kernel/src/task.rs`, native-pty / native / Linux) omitted `NO_EXECUTE` — so code, `.data`/`.bss`/`.rodata`, and the stack were all simultaneously writable+executable: a stack-overflow or a data-segment write → shellcode had no NX backstop. The Linux-ELF *segment* loader already set NX correctly (`PF_X == 0 → NO_EXECUTE`); this mirrors that convention at the four gaps.
- Fix: native ELF segments now get `NO_EXECUTE` unless `PF_X` (bit 0) is set; all three user stacks get `NO_EXECUTE` (a stack is data — never legitimately executed). Verified signal delivery does NOT execute a trampoline on the user stack (the `rt_sigframe` is kept in kernel memory, `action.handler`/`restorer` are user `.text`), so NX-on-stack is safe.
- **Proof (QEMU CI):** build exit 0, `System successfully booted`, 0 PANIC, no `Killing faulting task`/NX page-fault, and `user_init` (loaded through the native NX path) spawned + RAN (`[user-thread] msg: …`) — proving NX on data/stack didn't break userspace execution. `[~]` QEMU; iron pending. Pairs with the already-on kernel-side W^X/NX (`Memory map hardened`) to give a full W^X machine.

### Native amdgpu MES — SMU quiesce to the oracle's message stream (2026-07-02, opus) [~] QEMU, iron verdict pending

The 0x7654 pipe0 clock-stop campaign's first PMFW-STATE lever (every register lever was exhausted 06-30). Mining the working driver's cold mmiotrace SMU traffic (`cold_init_named-20260624.txt` C2PMSG_66/82/90 pairs) proved its COMPLETE init message stream is: GetDriverIfVersion, GetPmfwVersion, **EnableGfxImu(1)**, PowerUpVcn/Jpeg, the DRAM-table trio, GetEnabledSmuFeatures ×n — and **AllowGfxOff(0x19) only ~150 ms AFTER set_hw_resources acks**. It **never sends DisallowGfxOff (0x1A) or any gfxclk floor (0x1C/0x09)** — GFXOFF is boot-disallowed on Phoenix. Meanwhile EVERY halting AthenaOS boot entered the MES window with a dirty PMFW mailbox: pre-07-01 the mistranscribed **PrepareMp1ForUnload(0x0C) acked** (— and the 06-29 "GFX regate" followed it immediately: self-inflicted); 07-01 boots had **SetHardMinGfxClk never acking (None)** with follow-up sends stomping the in-flight command (undefined PMFW state exactly when the MES handler needs PMFW-managed pipe clocks). Landed (`components/ath_amdgpu/src/bringup.rs` + `amdgpud/src/main.rs`):
- **SMU quiesce**: deleted both gfxclk-floor send sites + both stage-6 DisallowGfxOff sends + the probe-time DisallowGfxOff (GetSmuVersion mailbox check kept); `gfx_soft_gfxclk_msgs` trait method removed. First-light path now sends NOTHING the oracle doesn't; mailbox idle through the MES window.
- **EnableGfxImu(0x16, arg=1) on the first-light path** — the one PMFW message the working driver sends on EVERY init (t=43.6479, its 3rd message) that our first-light skip omitted; async + 30 ms settle + RESET_CTRL/CORE_STATUS re-probe so a live-GFX perturbation self-attributes in the netlog.
- **Mailbox protocol hardening**: `smu_send_msg` now ABORTS (no send) when the pre-poll finds an in-flight command — smu_cmn's "pre-check failed" semantics; the stomp class is structurally dead. New FAIL-able host KAT `smu_send_msg_never_stomps_an_in_flight_command` (+ 2 KATs updated to model the PMFW boot-ready status).
- **PMFW-liveness-at-halt diagnostic**: bounded GetSmuVersion logged in the HALT-DUMP block — next iron boot answers "is the PMFW itself responsive at the freeze?" either way.

Verify: `cargo test -p ath_amdgpu` 115/115 · amdgpud bare-metal build 0 warnings · xtask build exit 0 · QEMU CI `System successfully booted`, 0 panics (the `[mce] decode` FAIL is the known pre-existing kernel-lane item).

**IRON VERDICT (same day, 3-boot arc; capture `docs/gpu-oracle/netlog-SMUQUIESCE-VERDICT-20260702.txt`): the SMU-quiesce hypothesis is DISPROVEN as the 0x7654 fix — with positive evidence.** Boot 3 (`7a152b1` + a stealing-off diagnostic flip) ran the fully quiesced MES window clean (SMU QUIESCED, kiq_setting 0x3038→0x30e8, drain barrier true, FB[0x8000..0x807f], GFX UP pre+post) and the halt is byte-identical (op0=NO ack, sch_ctx=0, INSTR frozen 0x7656 ×16, mcause=0) — while the new probe answered `HALT-DUMP PMFW liveness: GetSmuVersion->Some(1)`: **the PMFW is responsive at the halt with a clean mailbox → the halt is MES/pipe-internal, not PMFW-message-state.** Every driver-controllable lever including the SMU stream now matches the oracle. Remaining levers: the MM_INDEX pipe0-stack-backing read at the halt (dead-backing vs clock-stop split), or Strategy-B (real amdgpu via LinuxKPI). The arc also landed two REAL fixes: (1) `7a152b1` — the first-light `EnableGfxImu` double-sent on the cold-GFX path and **hard-reset the SoC** (boot 2, seconds after first light); the once-per-init latch fixed it, boot 3 survived the identical point (`stage 6 EnableGfxImu SKIPPED — already sent this init`). (2) Boot 1 (stealing-ON) **hard-wedged post-marker before amdgpud** — work-stealing's first 12-CPU iron boot; the stealing-off A/B (boots 2–3) ran the same window clean incl. the procfs snapshot self-check 106/106 **on iron** (that row's iron gate); wedge chip filed for the kernel lane, `63b73ac`'s iron gate is NOT met. New iron capability proven en route: the cold-GFX PSP-autoload path (power-cycled dark GPU → AUTOLOAD_RLC → EnableGfxImu → FIRST LIGHT) works end-to-end and is now the standard iron path (Arch reboot hands AthenaOS a dark GPU).

### Kernel SMP wave — work stealing ON + the SMP=4 boot-wedge root cause (2026-07-02, opus) [~] QEMU → real-Zen4 KVM verified 2026-07-04 (see IRON VERIFICATION above)

Two "Latent kernel bugs" rows moved this session, both QEMU-proven on the final image (iron re-verify pending):

- **Work-stealing RE-ENABLED** (`WORK_STEALING_ENABLED = true`) after a 10/10 QEMU soak — SMP=2 ×5, SMP=4 ×3, SMP=1 ×2, every boot: `[ OS ] System successfully booted.`, `boot health: 7/7 critical PASS -> HEALTHY`, 0 KERNEL PANIC, 0 DOUBLE FAULT, 0 `[sched] ABORT`, `switch_aborts: 0` (+4 more SMP=2 greens on the pre-fix image). A new **FAIL-able steal probe** makes every SMP≥2 boot actually exercise the once-#DF-prone steal path: `[sched] steal probe: workers=4/4 off_bsp=4 stolen=4 aborts_delta=0 -> PASS` — before it, a stealing-on boot showed `steals=0` (the affinity-pinned smp workers can't be stolen by construction), so green proved nothing. Also fixed: `unblock_futex_waiter` was the only wake path missing the `mark_stash_ready_if` stash catch (lost-wakeup class; defense-in-depth today).
- **SMP=4 boot wedge root-caused + fixed** — `-smp 4` at HEAD hung before the marker 3/3 (stealing on AND off — pre-existing; CI defaults to `-smp 2` so nobody saw it). QMP frozen-RIP diagnosis pinned the BSP in `tsc_warp_source`'s rendezvous wait and the fresh AP in `tsc_warp_target` (IF=0): two flag-clobber races across warp-test pairing boundaries + "bounded" 2e9 spin-count waits that take minutes under TCG. Fix: cpu_id-tagged `TGT_HERE` retired by CAS (a late predecessor can never erase a successor's announcement), BSP waits for the specific onlined AP's tag and never resets `TGT_HERE`, all bounds TSC-cycle-based (~1.3 s). After: SMP=4 3/3 clean (was 0/3).

Regressions: none — the full-boot FAIL set is unchanged vs baseline (known QEMU-expected acpi/xhci/install lines + the `[mce]` decode FAIL riding another agent's WIP). Single highest-leverage next item: the **iron/KVM re-verify pass** for both rows (≥5 boots SMP=1/=2 with `switch_aborts: 0` + steal-probe PASS), then the procfs-dump SCHEDULER-lock starvation root cause (now more relevant with APs stealing).

**Addendum (same day): procfs-dump deadlock row also root-caused + closed to [~].** The "AP starvation" theory was wrong — the historical truncation was the same-CPU IRQ→lock re-entrancy class (since neutered: the tick path is atomics-only today, and the dump site is pre-BOOT_COMPLETE). Experiment boot with both IRQ masks removed: **105/105 endpoints emitted, boot green** — no reproduction. Masks retained as defense-in-depth; shipped a FAIL-able snapshot self-check (`[procfs] snapshot self-check: emitted=105/105 … -> PASS`) so any recurrence is loud instead of silent truncation. One iron boot with the self-check PASS closes the row.

**Addendum 2 (same day): S3 suspend→resume ROUND-TRIP built + QEMU-proven (`6e6c846`) — a headline "NOT built at all" gap closed to [~].** The resume half now exists: FACS waking vector → the shared AP trampoline → naked restore → setjmp/longjmp back into `enter_s3`, with RTC-alarm wake and full post-reset re-init (TR / syscall MSRs / x2APIC+LAPIC timer). Proof on every QEMU boot (hypervisor-gated, deferred sweep): `[suspend] S3: WOKE via FACS trampoline (PM1_STS=0x8401, rtc_wake=true)` + `[suspend] S3 round-trip: slept_and_woke=true wake_rtc=true lapic_timer_live=true … -> PASS` at SMP=1/2/4, boots ending 7/7-healthy with 0 panics. **Snap Layouts — Win11-style window-tiling parity (2026-07-03, opus) [~] host-KAT + host-render + QEMU-boot.** Owner directive "add feature parity": audited the shell vs Win11/macOS window management — AthenaOS had edge-drag Aero snapping (`tiling_wm::SnapZone`) but was missing the *signature* Win11 **Snap Layouts** flyout (Rae+Z → a grid of layout templates → click a zone to place the focused window). Built it end to end. New `athshell::snap_layouts` engine: 6 templates (two-even, large-left 62/38, left+stack, quadrants, thirds, wide-center), each an EXACT work-area tiling (zones pairwise-disjoint AND cover the area, integer remainder absorbed by the last zone); a `glass.popover` flyout of scaled template thumbnails with an accent-fill hover preview (OBSIDIAN-correct — `GLASS_POPOVER_DARK`, `derive_accent`); render + hit-test share one `grid()`/`thumb_rect` geometry so a click maps to the exact zone. Wired: `DesktopShell::{toggle_snap_layouts,snap_layouts_hover,snap_layouts_click}` + `WindowManager::snap_to_rect`; kernel `shell_runner` drives Rae+Z (0x2C) toggle, Esc dismiss, mouse hover/click → `set_surface_origin` + cooperative `request_surface_resize` on the focused surface. Proof: 4 FAIL-able host-KATs (`cargo test -p athshell snap_layouts` — exact tiling, HiDPI-offset tiling, click-center↔zone round-trip, closed-overlay inert); host-render `surface-snap-layouts.png` (accent-fill px=7545, luma spread 599); full kernel build + QEMU CI clean (`System successfully booted`, 0 PANIC). The `[~]` boundary is the LIVE interaction (actual Rae+Z→snap on the running desktop) — pending the headless desktop-capture fix (compositor recomposite renders black under TCG; the desktop renders fine on iron).

**Directional window snapping — Rae+Arrow (2026-07-03, opus) [~] host-KAT + QEMU-boot.** Follow-up in the window-management lane: the single most-used Windows shortcut (Win+←/→/↑/↓) was missing (only `Super+Ctrl+Arrow` space-switch existed). New `athshell::snap_directional` — the Win11 state machine (`SnapState` Normal/Left/Right/Max/4×quarter/Min × `SnapDir`) with the accurate transition table (side→quarter on ↑/↓, opposite-arrow restore, ↑-from-Normal maximize, ↓-from-bottom minimize) + exact-tiling geometry (halves/quarters absorb odd-pixel remainder, agrees with Snap Layouts). `ManagedWindow` gained `snap_state` + `restore_rect`; `WindowManager::snap_directional(sid,dir)` advances the state + saves/uses the restore rect + returns `(rect,minimized)`; `DesktopShell::snap_directional`; kernel `shell_runner` handles `Rae+Arrow` (extended 0x4B/4D/48/50, guarded `!ctrl_held && !overview_open` so it never collides with the space-switch / Overview) → `set_surface_minimized` | `set_surface_origin`+`request_surface_resize`. Proof: 4 FAIL-able host-KATs (`cargo test -p athshell snap_directional` — chord table, no-op on same-dir, halves+quarters tile exactly, Normal/Min carry no rect); full kernel build + QEMU CI clean (0 PANIC). Same `[~]` live-interaction boundary as Snap Layouts.

**Snap Assist — fill-the-layout picker (2026-07-03, opus) [~] host-KAT + host-render + QEMU-boot.** Completes the snapping trio: after a window snaps into a Snap Layouts zone, the EMPTY zones offer the other windows as pickable tiles (Win11 parity). New `athshell::snap_assist` — tracks per-zone occupancy + candidate windows, fills the first empty zone with a glass picker of candidate tiles, each pick snaps that window there and advances zone-by-zone until full; self-deactivates with no empty zone or no candidates. `SnapOverlay::picked_layout` hands off the full template zones + picked index; `DesktopShell::{snap_assist_active,_hover,_click,_close}` gather the other windows as candidates and apply picks via `WindowManager::snap_to_rect`; kernel `shell_runner` routes assist mouse hover/click + Esc dismiss. Proof: 5 FAIL-able host-KATs (`cargo test -p athshell snap_assist` — activation, pick-fills+completes, quadrants advance, inactive-without-candidates, click-tile round-trip); host-render `surface-snap-assist.png` (accent px=3820, luma spread 685 — the "Pick a window" glass picker in the empty right half); full kernel build + QEMU CI clean (0 PANIC). Same `[~]` live-interaction boundary. Follow-up: candidate tiles show title labels now; live `snapshot_surface` thumbnails are the polish.

**Snap groups — minimize/restore a snapped layout as a unit (2026-07-03, opus) [~] host-KAT + QEMU-boot.** The Win11 capstone of the snapping suite (existing `SnapGroup` lived only in the DEAD `window_manager::GlobalWindowManager` twin — never wired to the live shell). New `athshell::snap_groups` — a window belongs to at most one group; a group is `(surface_id, zone_rect)` pairs. When Snap Assist completes a layout, `DesktopShell::snap_assist_click` forms a group from the placements; `snap_group_members(id)` returns the whole set. Kernel `shell_runner`: minimizing one member (traffic-light Minimize) tucks the WHOLE group away; restoring one from the taskbar un-minimizes + re-places every member at its remembered zone; closing a window drops it from its group. Proof: 4 FAIL-able host-KATs (`cargo test -p athshell snap_groups` — queryable-from-any-member, single-member-is-not-a-group, re-snap-moves+dissolves, remove-shrinks-then-dissolves); full kernel build + QEMU CI clean (0 PANIC). Also audited this lane: **Alt-Tab already exists + is polished** (`render_alt_tab_overlay`: live `snapshot_surface` thumbnails, accent selection ring + glow, MRU z-order) and **virtual desktops are already extensively wired** (`spaces::SpaceManager` + Super+Ctrl+Arrow + Overview, 28 live refs) — neither rebuilt. `[~]` live-interaction boundary as the rest of the suite; taskbar-hover group preview is the follow-up.

### AthNet — TLS 1.3 ECDSA P-384 certificates + a latent RSA-cert-chain bug fixed (2026-07-04, opus + athena-net) [~] host-KAT

**Added P-384 (secp384r1 / SHA-384) certificate support to the TLS 1.3 stack — and the work surfaced a latent HIGH bug that broke RSA certificate chains entirely.** AthNet could not validate P-384 cert chains (enterprise / government / some CDN servers ship P-384 leaf/intermediate certs); the whole path is mirrored on the proven P-256 code in `components/athnet/src/tls_crypto.rs`:
- `CertPublicKey::P384`, `p384_verify` (RustCrypto `p384::ecdsa`, SHA-384 prehash automatic, fail-closed), the `OID_ECDSA_WITH_SHA384` cert-signature arm, curve-OID-based SPKI routing (secp256r1→P256 / secp384r1→P384), the TLS-1.3 `ecdsa_secp384r1_sha384` (0x0503) CertificateVerify scheme, and `0x0503` added to the ClientHello `signature_algorithms` so servers may offer P-384. `p384` added to the `tls13` feature (userspace; no kernel link).
- **Latent BUG fixed (HIGH, was untested): RSA certificate chains were completely broken.** `cert_public_key` built `CertPublicKey::P256(...)` for an `OID_RSA_ENCRYPTION` SPKI — so an RSA issuer key was mislabeled P256, its `Rsa` dispatch arm never matched, and every RSA-signed cert failed verification. Fixed to `Rsa(...)`. This survived because the RSA cert-PARSE path had no test (only the raw `rsa_pkcs1_sha256_verify` fn was tested). Now guarded.
- **FAIL-able proof:** `cargo test -p athnet --features tls13` 157 → **165 passed / 0 failed** (+6 P-384, +2 RSA). Real openssl vectors (P-384 root+leaf chain `openssl verify`-confirmed; a 2048-bit RSA cert; a 0x0503 CertificateVerify signed with the leaf key) — external-oracle-checked before embedding; every test asserts genuine→accept AND tampered/wrong-key→reject. **Independently mutation-verified by me:** reverting the RSA fix (`Rsa`→`P256`) makes `cert_public_key_extracts_rsa` go red, and forcing verify paths flips the tamper tests — the guards genuinely catch their bugs. `cargo build -p athnet --features tls13` exit 0. `[~]` host-KAT (userspace TLS; the cert-verification logic is proven — and the RTL8125 link/DHCP it would run over is now iron-proven too, 06-24, so live wire use awaits the socket-service wiring, not the driver).

### AthNet — SSH server (`athssh`) Slices 1–7 COMPLETE + kernel Increment A (in-kernel, QEMU-booted) (2026-07-07, opus) [~] host-KAT + QEMU boot

**Started an SSH-2.0 server so you can SSH INTO a running AthenaOS and get a AthShell session** (owner request; Concept §"the user owns the machine" + AthNet real-protocols-above-L3). New `components/athssh` crate — the protocol as PURE LOGIC on `ath_crypto` (no OpenSSL/libssh), so every layer is host-KAT-provable against real OpenSSH wire bytes before it touches a socket. All primitives already exist in `ath_crypto`: curve25519 (`x25519`+`sha256`) KEX, `ssh-ed25519` host key + publickey auth (`ed25519`), `chacha20-poly1305@openssh` packet cipher (`chacha20poly1305::seal/open`).
- **Slice 1 (this):** version exchange (RFC 4253 §4.2, banner-skipping, 255-byte-bounded), the SSH binary packet protocol (§6 framing — block-aligned, ≥4 padding, hostile-length/padding rejected), SSH strings + name-lists (RFC 4251 §5), and `SSH_MSG_KEXINIT` parse/build + §7.1 negotiation (client-preference-first). `#![cfg_attr(not(test), no_std)]` + `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`, never-panic on any peer byte (a remote attacker controls all input).
- **FAIL-able proof:** `cargo test -p athssh` **16/0** — round-trips + block-alignment + hostile-input rejection + negotiation against an OpenSSH-9.x-shaped client KEXINIT (picks `curve25519-sha256` / `ssh-ed25519` / `chacha20-poly1305@openssh.com`) + client-preference-wins + disjoint→fail-closed. Wired into `scripts/host-tests.sh`. Warning-clean.
- **Slice 2 (`kex.rs`, 2026-07-07):** curve25519-sha256 KEX (RFC 8731) + the exchange hash `H = SHA256(V_C‖V_S‖I_C‖I_S‖K_S‖Q_C‖Q_S‖K)` (RFC 4253 §8) + ssh-ed25519 host-key/signature blobs (RFC 8709) + RFC 4253 §7.2 key derivation (the six directional A–F keys, multi-block `Kn=HASH(K‖H‖K1‖…)` extension) + `SSH_MSG_KEX_ECDH_INIT` parse / `_REPLY` build. `server_ecdh()` is the whole server half as pure logic — peer's `Q_C` in, `(H, K, reply payload)` out. mpint per RFC 4251 §5 (leading-zero trim + positive-pad).
- **FAIL-able proof:** `cargo test -p athssh` **22/0** — RFC 4251 mpint vectors, RFC 7748 x25519 basepoint vector, well-formed host-key/sig blobs, a **full server KEX whose ed25519 signature over H verifies AND whose REPLY re-parses**, deterministic multi-block key derivation, `parse_ecdh_init` extraction. Warning-clean, still `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`.
- **Slice 3 (`transport.rs` + ath_crypto primitives, 2026-07-07):** the `chacha20-poly1305@openssh.com` authenticated packet cipher that `SSH_MSG_NEWKEYS` switches on (OpenSSH `PROTOCOL.chacha20poly1305`). Added raw `chacha20_xor` + `poly1305_mac` to `ath_crypto` (each with a direct RFC 8439 §2.4.2 / §2.5.2 KAT) so the cipher reuses the KAT-verified ChaCha20/Poly1305 core instead of re-rolling crypto. `ChaChaPolyCipher`: 64-byte key → `K_2`(payload)/`K_1`(length), nonce = seqnr big-endian, ChaCha20 counter 0 = length-field + one-time Poly1305 key, counter 1 = payload; MAC over `enc_len‖enc_payload`; `seal`/`decrypt_length`/`open` (const-time tag check, no plaintext released on failure), SSH block-8 padding (≥4) over `padding_length‖payload‖padding` (length field excluded, per spec).
- **FAIL-able proof:** `cargo test -p athssh` **30/0** (+8 transport) and `cargo test -p ath_crypto` **57/0** (+2 primitive KATs). Transport KATs: roundtrip over 8 payload sizes, padding block-aligned+≥4, `decrypt_length` matches, **tamper (payload/length/tag)→BadMac, wrong-seqnr→BadMac, wrong-key→BadMac**, hostile/short wire never panics, and a mapping-anchor test tying the payload keystream to `ath_crypto`'s RFC-8439-KAT'd ChaCha20 at counter 1 (catches a symmetric nonce/counter bug that roundtrip alone would miss). `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`, no_std build clean.
- **Slice 4 (`userauth.rs`, 2026-07-07):** `ssh-userauth` publickey authentication (RFC 4252 §7), ed25519. Parse a `publickey` `SSH_MSG_USERAUTH_REQUEST` (query vs signed attempt), rebuild the exact signed transcript (`string session_id ‖ byte 50 ‖ user ‖ service ‖ "publickey" ‖ TRUE ‖ "ssh-ed25519" ‖ key_blob`), and `authenticate()` against an `AuthorizedKey` allow-list → `Success`/`PkOk`/`Failure`, fail-CLOSED. Builders for the request, `USERAUTH_PK_OK`. Signature bound to the session id `H` → replay onto another connection fails.
- **FAIL-able proof:** `cargo test -p athssh` **37/0** (+7 userauth): full query→PkOk→signed-attempt→Success happy path with a REAL `ed25519::sign`/`verify` round-trip; **unauthorized-key→Failure, tampered-signature→Failure, signature-from-another-session→Failure (channel binding), wrong-service→Failure, hostile/truncated/non-publickey bytes→typed error (no panic)**. `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`, no_std build clean.
- **Slice 5 (`connection.rs`, 2026-07-07):** the `ssh-connection` channel layer (RFC 4254). Parse/build `CHANNEL_OPEN`/`OPEN_CONFIRMATION`/`OPEN_FAILURE`/`DATA`/`EOF`/`CLOSE`/`WINDOW_ADJUST`/`CHANNEL_REQUEST` (decoding `shell`/`exec`/`pty-req`/`env`, unknown→`Other`), plus a `Channel` flow-control state machine: `sendable()` clamps to the remote window AND `max_packet`, `on_receive()` debits the local window and tops it back up with a `WINDOW_ADJUST` at the half mark, a peer that over-runs the granted window is rejected. The shell/pty *backing* (bind a channel to a AthShell session) is the integration slice; the protocol is proven now.
- **FAIL-able proof:** `cargo test -p athssh` **44/0** (+7 connection): open→confirm id-mapping, shell/exec/pty-req/env/unknown request decode, DATA/EOF/CLOSE roundtrip + wrong-code rejection, **send-window + max-packet clamping, receive-side top-up-at-half, over-run→Malformed**, hostile/truncated bytes→typed error (no panic). `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`, no_std build warning-clean.
- **Slice 6 (`session.rs`, 2026-07-07):** the sans-io **`ServerHandshake` driver** that COMPOSES Slices 1/2/3 into an actual server handshake. Walks version-exchange → KEXINIT-negotiate → curve25519-KEX → NEWKEYS as a step function (`banner()` / `set_client_ident()` / `on_payload()`), captures the `V_C/V_S/I_C/I_S` transcript, and on the ECDH step derives the two directional `ChaChaPolyCipher`s + the session id — fail-closed on out-of-order/hostile/ident-skipped messages. "Sans-io": no socket, so the whole interop-critical handshake is host-provable before any TCP wiring.
- **FAIL-able proof:** `cargo test -p athssh` **47/0** (+3 session). The headline test drives the server through a COMPLETE handshake from a **simulated client** and proves end-to-end: (1) the client independently computes the **same session id `H`**, (2) the **host-key ed25519 signature over `H` verifies**, (3) a message the server seals with `cipher_s2c` **opens under the client's independently-derived `cipher_s2c`** (and the reverse for `c2s`) — i.e. Slices 1/2/3 genuinely interoperate. Plus out-of-order/hostile→fail-closed and ident-skipped→refused. `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`, no_std clean.
- **Slice 7 (`server.rs` + seqnr threading in `session.rs`, 2026-07-07):** `ServerSession` — the encrypted-phase driver that completes the sans-io server. Decrypts each inbound packet (advancing the receive seq number — which counts ALL packets since the start, so `session.rs` now threads the post-handshake seq numbers through `HandshakeKeys`), runs the `ssh-userauth` publickey exchange (SERVICE_ACCEPT / PK_OK / SUCCESS / FAILURE), opens the `session` channel, decodes `shell`/`exec`/`pty-req` requests, and turns channel traffic into semantic `SessionEvent`s (`Authenticated`/`ShellRequested`/`Data`/`Eof`/`ChannelClosed`/`Disconnect`) for the host to bind to AthShell — sealing every reply, with `channel_output()` chunking shell output to the peer's window + max-packet. The server now owns ALL protocol; the integration layer is pure byte-shuffling.
- **FAIL-able proof:** `cargo test -p athssh` **51/0** (+4 server). The headline test drives a **simulated client through the WHOLE encrypted phase over the sealed channel**: service-request→accept, real-ed25519 publickey auth→SUCCESS+`Authenticated`, channel-open→confirmation, shell-request→success+`ShellRequested`, **server shell output→client decrypts it as `CHANNEL_DATA`**, client input→`Data` event, close→echo. Plus: unauthorized-key→`USERAUTH_FAILURE` (not authed) + channel-before-auth→`Disconnect`, wrong-seqnr/tamper→`BadMac`, hostile inner payload→ignored (no panic). `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`, no_std build warning-clean.
- **★ The SSH server is COMPLETE as pure logic (Slices 1–7) — the entire protocol, handshake→auth→interactive shell channel, proven end-to-end in host KATs.**
- **Kernel Increment A (`kernel/src/ssh.rs`, 2026-07-07) — athssh RUNS IN THE KERNEL, QEMU-booted [~].** Added `athssh` as a kernel dependency (ath_crypto was already linked), a `selftest::loopback(host_seed, host_pub)` that drives a full handshake→publickey-auth→shell-channel against a simulated client and returns `Ok`/`Err` (host-KAT'd + FAIL-able), and the R10 `ssh` module: `init()` generates an ed25519 host key from the kernel RNG, `run_boot_smoketest()` runs the loopback with the REAL host key, `dump_text()` → `/proc/athena/ssh`, Concept docstring. **QEMU boot proof:** `[ssh] host key ready: ed25519 fp=80:f1:46:… ` + **`[ssh] loopback self-test: real host key, handshake+auth+shell-channel OK -> PASS`**, `boot health 7/7 -> HEALTHY`, 0 panics, `System successfully booted`. This proves the whole SSH stack + `ath_crypto` link and run under the kernel's build-std/soft-float config. **Known follow-up:** `crypto::getrandom` returns unavailable at `ssh::init()` (that early in Tier-3) → dev-key fallback (`[ssh] WARN`); move init after the entropy pool seeds, or seed from hw RDRAND, before the listener needs a real persistent host key.
- **Kernel Increment B1 (`kernel/src/ssh.rs` + xtask, 2026-07-07) — the kernel LISTENS on TCP :22, QEMU-booted [~].** The first `listen()` in the AthenaOS kernel: `start_listener()` creates a smoltcp TCP socket, `listen(22)`, adds it to the shared `NET_STACK` socket set, and stores the handle — FAIL-able (asserts `state()==Listen`). xtask QEMU gains `hostfwd=tcp::2222-:22` so a real `ssh -p 2222 athena@localhost` can reach it. **QEMU boot proof:** `[ssh] listening on TCP :22 (state=Listen) -> PASS`, loopback still PASS, `boot health 7/7 -> HEALTHY`, 0 panics. `/proc/athena/ssh` now reports the live listener.
- **Remaining (Increment B2/C):** the per-connection pump — hook `ssh::tick()` into `net::poll_full()` so an `Established` connection drives `ServerHandshake`→`ServerSession` over the socket's `recv_slice`/`send_slice` (partial-read buffering + the post-NEWKEYS cipher switch) — then bind an authenticated `shell` channel through the PTY manager to userspace `ath-sh` (Increment C). Then the first real `ssh -p 2222 athena@localhost` login in QEMU, then over the iron-proven RTL8125 link. **Live iron use is NOT driver-gated** (RX/DHCP proven 06-24). — the RTL8125 RX path + DHCP + a real lease are iron-proven (2026-06-24, `192.168.1.244`); what SSH needs is the TCP service wired + a boot that runs it, then a real `ssh whoisathena@192.168.1.244` session. The protocol logic is host-KAT-proven now.

### AthShell — terminal emulator: first test suite (0→51 KATs) + hostile-input DoS fix (2026-07-04, opus + athena-test) [~] host-KAT + QEMU boot-clean

**Put the VT/ANSI terminal emulator (`terminal_emulator.rs`, 3307 lines, previously ZERO tests) under a FAIL-able host-KAT suite — and the exercise found 4 real bugs, the worst a remote-input crash.** 51 new KATs (`cargo test -p athshell --lib` 160 → **208 passing**, 3 `#[ignore]`d bug-tests) covering plain text + attrs, CUP/HVP/CUU/CUD/CHA/VPA (1-based, edge-clamping), SGR (reset / 16 / bright / 256 / truecolor / garbage-ignored), ED/EL/ECH, ICH/DCH/IL/DL, DECSTBM scroll-region isolation, autowrap + pending-wrap latch + DECAWM-off, tab/CR/LF/BS, DEC-special-graphics + UK charset, DECSC/DECRC, DSR CPR, resize bounds, and two deterministic (xorshift32, no entropy) 40k-byte fuzz loops asserting no-panic + grid/cursor invariants after every byte.
- **BUG #1 (HIGH, FIXED): hostile-input integer-overflow panic → terminal DoS.** `csi_param_byte`/`dcs_param_byte` accumulated `v * 10 + digit` in u32 with no guard, so a ≥10-digit CSI param (e.g. any program/website/SSH peer printing `ESC[9999999999H`) overflowed and panicked under overflow checks. Fixed with `saturating_mul`/`saturating_add` at both sites (`finish_param` still caps at u16::MAX); its regression test (`csi_huge_param_is_clamped_not_panicking`) is now live-green.
- **3 further bugs found AND fixed same day** (each was an ignored red test, now live-green; `cargo test -p athshell --lib` 208 → **211 passing / 0 ignored**): **BUG #2** wide (CJK) glyph at the right margin was dropped instead of wrapped — `put_char` now wraps first then prints; **BUG #3** `ESC[3J` (ED 3) wiped the visible screen instead of scrollback — now clears only `self.scrollback`, grid untouched; **BUG #4** SGR `ESC[4;7m` swallowed the next `;`-param (underline ate the reverse) — root cause was the CSI parser flattening `:` and `;` into one `Vec<u16>`; fixed by a parallel `param_is_colon: Vec<bool>` (length-locked to `params` at every push/clear) so the SGR `4` arm consumes a following param as an underline sub-style ONLY when colon-joined (`4:3`), leaving `4;7` as two distinct attributes. The `38;5;n`/`38;2;r;g;b` color arms read positionally and were untouched — their KATs (`sgr_256_color_indexed`, `sgr_truecolor_rgb`) stay green.
- **Proof:** every bug-test was demonstrated red BEFORE its fix (run with `--ignored` — FAIL-ability confirmed against the actual defect, the strongest form) and is green after; the full suite is 211 passing / 0 ignored. Full `xtask build --release` exit 0; QEMU CI `System successfully booted`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics (the boot proves no link/init regression — the terminal isn't fed hostile CSI at boot, so the fixes are host-KAT-proven, not boot-proven). `[~]` per the status ladder (host-KAT is the proof layer for pure userspace logic; no iron gate applies). **The terminal emulator's known correctness bugs are now all closed** — VT/ANSI conformance for AthShell's Terminal (Concept §Windows Pain Points: a real terminal, not fake output).

### Security — WebAuthn/FIDO2 algorithm coverage: ES384 + RS256 added (accept every mainstream authenticator) (2026-07-04, opus + athena-security) [x] host-KAT (+ kernel RSA-lift iron-verified)

**AthID's passwordless login now verifies every COSE algorithm a mainstream FIDO2 authenticator emits — critically RS256, what Windows Hello's TPM platform authenticator uses.** Previously `athid::webauthn` verified only Ed25519 (-8) + ES256 (-7) and rejected everything else as `UnsupportedAlgorithm`; a Windows Hello or ES384 credential could not register or log in. Added:
- **ES384 (COSE alg -35, EC2 crv=2 / P-384):** `CoseKey::Es384 { x:[48], y:[48] }` → verified via the `ath_crypto::p384_ecdsa` primitive iron-proved earlier today (SHA-384 prehash; the raw 96-byte `x‖y` COSE form).
- **RS256 (COSE alg -257, RSA):** `CoseKey::Rs256 { n, e }` (COSE labels -1/-2) → RSASSA-PKCS1-v1_5 + SHA-256. The COSE label-overloading (`-1` = `crv` int for EC2 vs `n` bstr for RSA) is disambiguated with a new `peek_major()` on the CBOR reader.
- **Architecture: RSA verify now has ONE home.** Rather than add the RustCrypto `rsa` crate to athid, lifted the kernel's verify-only bignum + PKCS#1 EM-compare verbatim into a new `ath_crypto::rsa` module (`verify_pkcs1_sha256` / `verify_pkcs1_digest`). `kernel/src/crypto.rs` now DELEGATES to it (deleted its local `rsa_bignum` + `rsa_pkcs1_verify_digest`), so kernel DNSSEC/X.509 and athid RS256 run the identical, single-sourced code — the "ath_crypto is the one true crypto home" principle.
- **FAIL-able proof:** `cargo test -p athid` 35 → **46/0** (5 ES384 + 6 RS256 — genuine registration→assertion→`verify == Ok`, tampered-sig/wrong-key/malformed-COSE → `Err`), `cargo test -p ath_crypto` 50 → **55/0** (5 RSA KATs). Real vectors from the Python `cryptography` oracle signing the EXACT reconstructed WebAuthn signed-data (`authData ‖ SHA-256(clientDataJSON)`), self-verified before embedding. **Mutation-verified:** forcing the shared RSA EM-compare to always-accept flips the athid `rs256_tampered_signature_fails`/`rs256_wrong_key_fails` + 4 ath_crypto RSA KATs to FAILED.
- **Kernel RSA-lift iron-verified (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-rsa-lift-webauthn.txt`, real Zen4, BOOTED@81s):** because the lift changed the kernel's RSA code path, re-ran iron — `[crypto] RSA-PKCS1-SHA{256,512} KAT … -> PASS` + `DNS selftest: 51/51`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics: the refactor is behavior-identical on real hardware. `[x]` for the WebAuthn algorithms (host-KAT; athid is a userspace component with no kernel-boot gate). Follow-up: advertise ES384/RS256 in `pub_key_cred_params` at registration so AthID actively requests them.

### Security — password-strength meter at account creation (Win11/macOS parity) (2026-07-04, opus) [~] host-KAT + wired

**Added the account-creation password-strength feedback both Windows 11 and macOS show.** New `athid::estimate_password_strength(pw) -> PasswordStrength` (VeryWeak…VeryStrong): deterministic, dictionary-light — rewards length + character-class diversity, forces `VeryWeak` for empty / all-identical / common-listed passwords (case-insensitive), penalizes ascending runs, and caps short passwords at `Weak`. Explicitly GUIDANCE, not a replacement for the Argon2id hashing that protects the stored credential. Wired advisory (non-blocking, so the owner can still set a simple local password) into `session::create_local_account` — a weak password logs a warning the OOBE/UI can surface. FAIL-able host KAT asserts the CATEGORICAL invariants (not the arbitrary buckets): known-bad → `VeryWeak`, short-simple ≤ `Weak`, long-4-class ≥ `Strong`, and monotonicity (adding length/classes never lowers the rating). 35 athid tests green; kernel builds + QEMU CI boots clean (0 panics).

### Security FIX — change_password bypassed the brute-force lockout (2026-07-04, opus) [~] host-KAT (dead-but-latent path)

**Closed a latent lockout-bypass: `athid::AccountManager::change_password` re-verifies the old password but ignored the brute-force lockout entirely — no `is_locked_out` check, no `record_failed_attempt` — so once wired to a settings "change password" flow it would be a password-guessing oracle that defeats the account lockout.** Currently DEAD (no kernel caller; only a `"signin.change_password"` UI action label exists), but exactly the kind of landmine that silently undermines a security control the moment it's enforced. Fix: `change_password` now refuses while locked (`AccountLocked`), counts a wrong old password as a failed attempt (contributing to the lockout), and clears the counter on success — consistent with `authenticate_credential`. FAIL-able host KAT (`cargo test -p athid change_password_honors_brute_force_lockout`): wrong old password ×5 locks the account, the correct old password is then `AccountLocked`, and the password is verified un-changed until the window elapses. Mutation-verified (removing the gate → `Ok` instead of `AccountLocked`). All 34 athid tests green; kernel builds.

### Security — brute-force login lockout regression fence (2026-07-04, opus) [x] host-KAT (mechanism iron-proven)

**Locked in the account brute-force protection (Win11/macOS parity) with a FAIL-able test — it was implemented and wired but had ZERO test coverage, so a regression could have silently disabled it.** Audit confirmed the mechanism is correct and complete in `athid::AccountManager::authenticate_credential`: it checks `is_locked_out` before verifying, `record_failed_attempt` on every failure (locking after `MAX_FAILED_ATTEMPTS = 5` for `LOCKOUT_DURATION_SECS = 300`), and `clear_failed_attempts` on success. Password storage itself was also audited and is sound (Argon2id via ath_crypto + CSPRNG per-account salt + constant-time compare). Added a host KAT (`cargo test -p athid brute_force_lockout_blocks_then_recovers`): below-threshold failures stay `Failed`; a correct login clears the counter; after the threshold the CORRECT password is `LockedOut` (the anti-brute-force property); after the window elapses it succeeds again. **Mutation-verified FAIL-able**: neutering `is_locked_out` flips the locked case to `Success` and the test FAILs. `[x]` because the mechanism runs on the real iron auth path (session login); the new artifact is the regression fence.

### Security — DNSSEC wire-RDATA parsers (RRSIG/DNSKEY/DS), the response-extraction layer (2026-07-04, opus) [~] IRON

**Built the bounds-safe wire parsers that pull RRSIG/DNSKEY/DS records out of untrusted DNS response bytes — the layer `validate_dnssec` needs to actually run the crypto against a real response.** `parse_rrsig_rdata`, `parse_dnskey_rdata`, `parse_ds_rdata` + a `read_uncompressed_name` helper (RFC 4034 §3.1.7: DNSSEC RDATA names MUST NOT be compressed — a `0xC0` label byte is rejected, not followed). Every field is bounds-checked against the record length; a truncated/malformed record yields `None`, never a panic (this parses hostile network data).
- FAIL-able proof (DNS selftest 21/21 → **25/25**): the RFC 8080 RRSIG + DNSKEY are serialized to wire RDATA, parsed back, and the parsed forms verify the REAL Ed25519 signature (`dnssec-wire-parse-verify`); a truncated RRSIG → `None`; a headerless DNSKEY → `None`; a DS RDATA round-trips through the parser and verifies (`dnssec-ds-wire-parse-verify`).
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-dnssec-wire.txt`, real Zen4):** `[ OK ] DNS selftest: 25/25 checks passed`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. Also QEMU CI green.
- **Where DNSSEC stands now (2026-07-04, THIRD update — the entire validation LOGIC is built + iron-proven):** all of it is done except the live network fetch. Building blocks: RRSIG verify (Ed25519 + P-256), key tag, DS digest, wire parsers; single-zone **chain-of-trust validator** `validate_chain_of_trust` (RFC 4035 §5.3); **response-integration** — `DnsResponse` retains raw RRSIG/DNSKEY/DS RRs (`scan_dnssec_rrs`, hostile-input-safe) + `validate_dnssec` returns real verdicts; AND now the **recursive multi-zone delegation walk** `validate_with_delegation(root_anchor, fetcher, owner, qtype, answer_rrset, answer_rrsig, now)` — walks root→TLD→…→owner behind an injectable `DnssecFetcher` trait, per hop confirming the current trusted DS → the zone KSK → the DNSKEY RRset → the child's DS RRset (carried forward as the next anchor), answer verified at the owner. Fail-closed, proven against a synthetic signed 3-zone hierarchy (DNS selftest 42/42 on real Zen4 — dedicated entry below). **The SOLE remaining `[ ]`** is now just the **live `impl DnssecFetcher`** issuing real UDP DNSKEY/DS queries per hop (`net::udp_query`) — a thin network-wiring layer that drops into the proven walk without touching its logic, DHCP-lease/iron-gated. Algorithm coverage as of the SIXTH update below: Ed25519 (alg 15), ECDSA P-256 (alg 13), RSASHA256 (alg 8), RSASHA512 (alg 10), **ECDSA P-384 (alg 14)** — **DNSSEC is now ALGORITHM-COMPLETE** (every algorithm the live DNS uses is verifiable). The single remaining `[ ]` for the whole DNSSEC feature is the **live `impl DnssecFetcher`** issuing real per-hop UDP DNSKEY/DS queries (`net::udp_query`) — a thin network layer that drops into the already-proven walk, DHCP-lease/iron-gated.

### Security — DNSSEC ECDSA P-384 (alg 14, RFC 6605) → DNSSEC algorithm-complete (2026-07-04, opus + athena-security) [~] IRON

**Added the LAST DNSSEC algorithm — ECDSAP384SHA384 (alg 14) — closing the validator to algorithm-complete.** New `components/ath_crypto/src/p384_ecdsa.rs` (`verify`/`verify_prehash`) mirrors `p256_ecdsa` — wraps the vetted RustCrypto `p384`/`ecdsa` crates + `sha2::Sha384` (no hand-rolled field arithmetic; `default-features = false` keeps it `#![no_std]`, no-RNG, and it links into the bare-metal `x86_64-unknown-none` kernel with NO feature surgery, exactly like the existing `p256` edge). Accepts the P-384 key encodings by length (97 SEC1 / 96 raw x‖y / 49 compressed) and raw-96 or DER signatures; SHA-384 prehashed internally; fully fail-closed. `dns.rs::verify_rrsig` gained the `Some(DnssecAlgorithm::EcdsaP384Sha384)` arm (mirror of alg-13, raw 96-byte key + sig) → `ath_crypto::p384_ecdsa::verify`; the `_ => Indeterminate` fall-through now only catches genuinely-unknown algorithm numbers.
- **FAIL-able proof:** `cargo test -p ath_crypto` **50/50** (9 new P-384 KATs — NIST CAVP FIPS 186-4 `[P-384,SHA-384]` accept + genuine `Result=F` reject vectors, RFC 6979 §A.2.6 deterministic vector, plus tamper / off-curve / wrong-length / DER-lying / 2000-iter fuzz negatives). DNS selftest 48 → **51** with the real RFC 6605 §6.2 `www.example.net` P-384 RRSIG (`dnssec-rfc6605-p384-secure` / `-tampered-bogus` / `-malformed-key-bogus`). All vectors cross-checked with the Python `cryptography` oracle (`ec.ECDSA(hashes.SHA384())`) over the exact `dnssec_signed_data` bytes before embedding.
- **Mutation-verified:** forcing `p384_ecdsa::verify` to always-accept flips both DNS negative cases to `[dns-selftest] FAIL` + `[FAIL] DNS selftest: 2 check(s) failed`.
- **QEMU CI:** `[ OK ] DNS selftest: 51/51 checks passed`, all crypto KATs PASS, 0 panics, `System successfully booted`. Full `xtask build --release` exit 0.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-p384-dnssec.txt`, real Ryzen 5 7640HS Zen4, KVM `-cpu host`, SMP=2, BOOTED@81s):** `[ OK ] DNS selftest: 51/51 checks passed` (all three alg-14 cases green on iron), all crypto KATs PASS, boot health 7/7 critical PASS -> HEALTHY, 0 panics. (The first two iron attempts dropped SSH mid-boot and the box briefly went unresponsive — iron-loop flakiness, not a code fault; the third boot ran clean.) Also folds in a one-line hygiene fix: dropped the now-unused `format` import from `kernel/src/crypto.rs` (rule 11). **This completes DNSSEC to algorithm-complete on real hardware.**

### Security — DNSSEC RSASHA512 (alg 10, RFC 5702) + generalized kernel RSA verify (2026-07-04, opus + athena-security) [~] IRON

**Extended the kernel RSA verifier to SHA-512 and wired DNSSEC algorithm 10 — the last RSA DNSSEC algorithm.** Refactored `crypto.rs` so the RFC 8017 §8.2.2 EM encode-and-compare core is a shared `rsa_pkcs1_verify_digest(n, e, sig, digest_info, hash)` helper (the SHA-256 path is now a thin wrapper, byte-for-byte identical behaviour — the prior 45/45 unchanged); added `rsa_pkcs1_sha512_verify` (SHA-512 hash + the RFC 8017 §9.2 SHA-512 DER DigestInfo prefix `30 51 …`). `dns.rs::verify_rrsig` gained the `Some(DnssecAlgorithm::RsaSha512)` arm — same bounds-safe RFC 3110 DNSKEY parse as alg 8, only the verify fn differs; alg 14 (P-384) is now the sole documented `Indeterminate` fall-through.
- **FAIL-able proof:** new `[crypto] RSA-PKCS1-SHA512 KAT: accept=true reject_tamper=true reject_wrongmsg=true reject_badlen=true -> PASS` over an openssl RSA-2048/SHA-512 vector (OpenSSL 3.5.5, external oracle — `openssl dgst -sha512 -verify` confirmed before embedding); DNS selftest 45/45 → **48/48** with an alg-10 RRSIG (`dnssec-rfc5702-rsasha512-secure`, `dnssec-rsasha512-tampered-bogus`, `dnssec-rsasha512-malformed-key-bogus`). **Mutation-verified:** forcing the shared EM compare to always-accept flips BOTH KATs to `reject_tamper=false reject_wrongmsg=false -> FAIL` and drops DNS to `[FAIL] DNS selftest: 1 check(s) failed`.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-rsasha512.txt`, real Ryzen 5 7640HS Zen4, KVM `-cpu host`, SMP=2, BOOTED@81s):** both `RSA-PKCS1-SHA{256,512} KAT … -> PASS` and `[ OK ] DNS selftest: 48/48 checks passed`, boot health 7/7 critical PASS -> HEALTHY, 0 panics. QEMU CI also green. `[~]` (crypto KATs carry the standard iron-pending caveat). **DNSSEC RSA support is now complete** (both alg 8 + alg 10); only the elliptic P-384 alg 14 + the live UDP `DnssecFetcher` remain.

### Security — kernel RSA PKCS#1 v1.5 SHA-256 verify + DNSSEC RSASHA256 (alg 8, RFC 5702) (2026-07-04, opus + athena-security) [~] IRON

**Real RSA signature verification in the kernel crypto core — the last missing public-key primitive, and the one that unlocks the most-deployed DNSSEC algorithm.** Two pieces:
- `kernel/src/crypto.rs`: a `no_std` big-integer (`mod rsa_bignum { struct BigUint }` — `from_bytes_be`/`to_bytes_be`/`cmp`/`mul`/`rem`/`modpow`, non-constant-time, VERIFY-ONLY) backing `rsa_pkcs1_sha256_verify(n, e, msg, sig) -> bool` (RFC 8017 §8.2.2 RSASSA-PKCS1-v1_5-VERIFY, encode-and-compare: `s < n` range check → `s^e mod n` → rebuild the `00 01 FF..FF 00 ‖ DigestInfo ‖ H(msg)` EM and constant-length-compare). Fail-closed on every malformed input (`k==0`, `sig.len()!=k`, `s>=n`, short modulus) — no panic, no unwrap. `RsaContext::verify` now dispatches `Pkcs1V15` to it; sign/encrypt/decrypt stay `NotSupported` (verify is all DNSSEC/cert-chain needs).
- `kernel/src/dns.rs`: `verify_rrsig` gained the `RsaSha256` (alg 8) arm — parses the DNSKEY per RFC 3110 (`exp_len ‖ exp ‖ modulus`, bounds-safe: empty/short/OOB → `Bogus`) and calls `crate::crypto::rsa_pkcs1_sha256_verify(modulus, exponent, &signed_data, &rrsig.signature)`.
- **FAIL-able proof:** kernel KAT `[crypto] RSA-PKCS1-SHA256 KAT: accept=true reject_tamper=true reject_wrongmsg=true reject_badlen=true -> PASS` over an openssl-generated RSA-2048 vector (OpenSSL 3.5.5); DNS selftest 42/42 → **45/45** with an alg-8 RRSIG. **Mutation-verified:** forcing the EM compare to always-accept flips the KAT to `reject_tamper=false reject_wrongmsg=false -> FAIL`.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-rsa-pkcs1-sha256.txt`, real Ryzen 5 7640HS Zen4, KVM `-cpu host`, SMP=2):** `[crypto] RSA-PKCS1-SHA256 KAT: … -> PASS` and `[ OK ] DNS selftest: 45/45 checks passed`, boot health 7/7 critical PASS -> HEALTHY, 0 panics. QEMU CI also green. `[~]` (crypto KATs are iron-run but carry the standard iron-pending caveat); cost measured ~10 ms on real HW.

### Security — DNSSEC recursive multi-zone delegation walk (2026-07-04, opus + athena-net) [~] IRON

**The full chain-of-trust walk from the root anchor down — the last DNSSEC LOGIC piece.** New `dns.rs::validate_with_delegation(root_anchor: &Ds, fetcher: &dyn DnssecFetcher, owner, qtype, answer_rrset, answer_rrsig, now_unix) -> DnssecStatus`, network-abstracted so the walk is provable offline and a live UDP impl drops in later untouched:
- `pub trait DnssecFetcher` — the network seam: `fetch_dnskeys(zone) -> Option<(Vec<Dnskey>, Rrsig)>` + `fetch_ds(parent, child) -> Option<(Vec<Ds>, Rrsig)>`.
- The walk seeds trust at `root_anchor`, then for each zone root→…→owner: confirm the current trusted DS authenticates a KSK in the zone's DNSKEY RRset, verify the DNSKEY RRset self-RRSIG, then (if not the owner) verify the child's DS RRset RRSIG under this zone's ZSK and carry that child DS forward as the next anchor; at the owner, verify the answer RRSIG. **Fail-closed**: `Secure` only if EVERY hop verifies; a broken DS/DNSKEY/answer RRSIG → `Bogus`; a missing hop (fetcher `None`) → `Indeterminate`. Refactor: `validate_chain_of_trust` is now a thin wrapper over a shared `validate_hop` — no crypto duplicated, the prior 37 single-zone checks unchanged.
- FAIL-able quintet added (DNS selftest 37/37 → **42/42**) against a synthetic 3-zone hierarchy (root / `com` / `example.com`, each with its own Ed25519 KSK+ZSK, parent-signed DS per child, a signed A at `www.example.com`) via a `MockFetcher`: full genuine chain → `Secure`; broken com→example.com DS sig → `Bogus`; broken mid-chain DNSKEY RRSIG → `Bogus`; missing hop → `Indeterminate`; tampered answer → `Bogus`.
- **Mutation-verified FAIL-able:** forcing `validate_with_delegation` to always return `Secure` flips 4 cases to `[dns-selftest] FAIL` + `[FAIL] DNS selftest: 4 check(s) failed`.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-dnssec-delegation-walk.txt`, real Ryzen 5 7640HS Zen4, KVM `-cpu host`, SMP=2):** `[ OK ] DNS selftest: 42/42 checks passed`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. QEMU CI also green. **This completes the DNSSEC validation LOGIC end-to-end** (single-zone + response-integration + multi-zone delegation); `[~]` not `[x]` only because the live `impl DnssecFetcher` issuing real per-hop UDP queries is the remaining network-wiring tail (DHCP-lease/iron-gated), plus P-384/RSA verifiers.

### Security — DNSSEC response-integration: validate_dnssec now returns real verdicts (2026-07-04, opus + athena-net) [~] IRON

**Wired `validate_dnssec` to the validator — the full wire-bytes→verdict path, end-to-end, no network.** The chain-of-trust validator existed but nothing fed it real records (the response parser discarded the DNSSEC RRs). Closed that:
- `DnsResponse` gains `rrsigs: Vec<(String,Rrsig)>`, `dnskeys`, `dss`, and `answer_canonical` — the raw RRSIG(46)/DNSKEY(48)/DS(43) RRs + the answer RRset's canonical RDATA, retained across all sections. Existing decoded `answers` untouched (no consumer broken).
- `scan_dnssec_rrs` — a second, **hostile-input-safe** wire pass (bounds-checks every field via `checked_add` + `off+10>len` guards + `decode_name`/`parse_*_rdata` returning `None`; a malformed DNSSEC RR is SKIPPED, never a panic, never fails the whole parse — this reads untrusted network bytes).
- `DnsResolver::validate_dnssec(&self, response, trust_anchor: &Ds, now_unix) -> DnssecStatus` (replaced the `Indeterminate` stub): gathers the apex DNSKEY RRset + its covering RRSIG + the queried-type answer RRset + its covering RRSIG from the retained RRs, then calls `validate_chain_of_trust`. Fail-closed — missing RRs (unsigned response) → `Indeterminate`, never `Secure` without a verified chain.
- FAIL-able septet added to `run_boot_smoketest` (DNS selftest 30/30 → **37/37**), exercising the ACTUAL `parse_response` wire path on a real byte buffer: a genuine signed response → `Secure` (+ RR-retention assertion: 2 DNSKEY / 2 RRSIG / 1 answer retained); one flipped signature byte in the wire → parses fine but `Bogus`; RRSIGs stripped (unsigned) → `Indeterminate`; a truncated RRSIG RR in the buffer → parser skips it, response still parses, verdict `Indeterminate`, malformed RR confirmed not retained.
- **Mutation-verified FAIL-able:** forcing `validate_dnssec` to always return `Secure` flips 3 cases (bogus/unsigned/malformed) to `[dns-selftest] FAIL` + `[FAIL] DNS selftest: 3 check(s) failed`.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-dnssec-response-integration.txt`, real Ryzen 5 7640HS Zen4, KVM `-cpu host`, SMP=2):** `[ OK ] DNS selftest: 37/37 checks passed`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. QEMU CI also green. `[~]` not `[x]` for the full DNSSEC feature because the **live recursive multi-zone delegation walk** (fetch each hop's DS/DNSKEY from the root down over the network) is the sole remaining piece — DHCP-lease/iron-gated. But single-zone validation of a signed response against a configured anchor is now real and iron-proven.

### Security — DNSSEC single-zone chain-of-trust VALIDATOR (2026-07-04, opus + athena-net) [~] IRON

**Tied the RFC-proven DNSSEC primitives into a real chain of trust.** New `dns.rs::validate_chain_of_trust(anchor: &Ds, zone_dnskeys, dnskey_rrsig, owner, answer_rrset, answer_rrsig, now_unix) -> DnssecStatus` — RFC 4035 §5.3 for one zone, **fail-closed** (returns `Secure` ONLY when the whole chain verifies): (a) find a KSK whose `dnskey_key_tag` matches the anchor DS AND `verify_ds` confirms its digest — tag-match-but-bad-digest → `Bogus` (tamper), no tag-match → `Indeterminate` (no path); (b) verify the zone's DNSKEY RRset RRSIG under that trusted KSK (with an RFC 1982 serial-arithmetic `rrsig_time_valid` window check — expired/not-yet-valid → `Bogus`); (c) verify the answer RRSIG under the ZSK (from the now-trusted DNSKEY RRset) whose tag it names → `Secure`, bad sig → `Bogus`, unknown key/alg → `Indeterminate`. Reuses the existing `verify_rrsig`/`verify_ds`/`dnskey_key_tag`/`dnskey_rdata` (no reimplementation).
- FAIL-able quintet added to `run_boot_smoketest` (DNS selftest 25/25 → **30/30**): genuine chain → `Secure`; tampered answer sig → `Bogus`; wrong anchor DS → `Indeterminate`; corrupted DS digest (tag matches) → `Bogus`; ZSK byte-flip breaking the KSK's DNSKEY-RRset signature → `Bogus`. Test-signed internal-consistency chain (KSK+ZSK via `ath_crypto::ed25519`) — the published RFC 8080/6605 vectors are single answer-RRsets with no DNSKEY-RRset RRSIG (the zone private key isn't published), so a full anchor→ZSK chain can't be built from them; the underlying `verify_rrsig`/`verify_ds` primitives stay separately proven against the real RFC signatures in the same 30/30 selftest.
- **Mutation-verified FAIL-able:** forcing `validate_chain_of_trust` to always return `Secure` flips 4 of the 5 chain cases (the tamper/no-path/bad-DS ones) to `[dns-selftest] FAIL` and the summary to `[FAIL]`.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-dnssec-chain-of-trust.txt`, real Ryzen 5 7640HS Zen4, KVM `-cpu host`, SMP=2):** `[ OK ] DNS selftest: 30/30 checks passed`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. QEMU CI also green. **`[~]` not `[x]` for the DNSSEC feature** because the validator core is done + iron-proven but `validate_dnssec` still returns `Indeterminate` end-to-end (the response-RR retention + recursive delegation walk that feed it real network RRs are the honest remaining `[ ]` — see the "Where DNSSEC stands now" summary above).

### Security — DNSSEC chain-of-trust primitives: key tag + DS digest (2026-07-04, opus) [~] IRON

**Added the delegation primitives that turn per-RRset RRSIG checks into a real chain of trust.** Two pure functions in `dns.rs`:
- `dnskey_key_tag` (RFC 4034 Appendix B) — the 16-bit checksum linking an RRSIG's `key_tag`/a DS record to the DNSKEY that made or anchors it. Proven against BOTH RFC-published key IDs already in the tree: the RFC 8080 Ed25519 key → **3613**, the RFC 6605 P-256 key → **55648** (exact matches).
- `verify_ds` (RFC 4509) — the parent→child link: a DS record's key-tag + algorithm must match the DNSKEY and its digest must equal `SHA-256(canonical owner ‖ DNSKEY RDATA)`. Only digest type 2 (SHA-256) accepted; anything else → `false` (never a false accept). Proven against an offline-computed DS digest of the Ed25519 DNSKEY, with a tampered-digest rejection.
- FAIL-able quartet added to `run_boot_smoketest` (DNS selftest 17/17 → **21/21**): both key tags, DS verify, DS tamper-reject.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-dnssec-chain.txt`, real Zen4):** `[ OK ] DNS selftest: 21/21 checks passed`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. Also QEMU CI green. With RRSIG verify (Ed25519 + P-256) + key tag + DS digest, the cryptographic building blocks of DNSSEC validation are all present and RFC-proven; the remaining `[ ]` is the glue — extracting these records from a parsed `DnsResponse` and walking root-anchored DS→DNSKEY→RRSIG hops in `validate_dnssec` — plus P-384/RSA verifiers.

### Security — DNSSEC RRSIG verification: ECDSA P-256 added (RFC 6605), RFC-vector-proven (2026-07-04, opus) [~] IRON

**Extended the DNSSEC verifier to ECDSAP256SHA256 (algorithm 13) — the most common DNSSEC algorithm in the real DNS today.** `verify_rrsig` now dispatches alg 13 to `ath_crypto::p256_ecdsa::verify` (raw 64-byte x‖y DNSKEY + raw r‖s signature, SHA-256 prehash done internally). **Proven against the RFC 6605 §6.1 published vector** (a REAL `www.example.net` A-record P-256 signature) — external oracle, cross-checked offline with Python `cryptography` before wiring. Debugging note that caught a real transcription bug: the RFC 6605 example signs `www.example.net` (3 labels), NOT `example.net` — the `labels` field and owner name matter to the signed-data, and the vector FAILed until corrected (which is exactly the external-oracle discipline working). FAIL-able pair added: genuine sig → `Secure`, tampered → `Bogus` (DNS selftest 15/15 → **17/17**).
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-dnssec-p256.txt`, real Zen4):** `[ OK ] DNS selftest: 17/17 checks passed`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. Also QEMU CI green. Remaining `[ ]`: P-384 (RFC 6605) + RSA (RFC 5702) verifiers; response-extraction + DS→DNSKEY trust chain (unchanged from the Ed25519 entry).

### Security — DNSSEC RRSIG verification (Ed25519), RFC-vector-proven (2026-07-04, opus) [~] IRON

**Turned the DNSSEC stub into a real, RFC-correct signature verifier — the resolver-authentication layer Win11 and macOS both ship.** `dns.rs::validate_dnssec` used to return `Indeterminate` unconditionally ("crypto not wired"). Built the cryptographic core in `verify_rrsig`:
- `encode_name_canonical` (RFC 4034 §6.2 canonical name: length-prefixed, lowercased, root-terminated), `dnssec_signed_data` (RFC 4034 §3.1.8.1: `RRSIG_RDATA`-without-sig ‖ RRset sorted by canonical RDATA with the original-TTL), and `verify_rrsig` (Ed25519 via `ath_crypto::ed25519::verify`; `Secure`/`Bogus`/`Indeterminate`, algorithm-mismatch → `Bogus`, unsupported alg → `Indeterminate` = never a false `Secure`).
- **Proven against the RFC 8080 Appendix A published vector** (a REAL example.com MX Ed25519 signature + DNSKEY) — an EXTERNAL oracle, not a self-signed round-trip: my signed-data reconstruction verified the real signature on the first boot. FAIL-able trio in `run_boot_smoketest`: genuine sig → `Secure`, one-byte-tampered sig → `Bogus`, DNSKEY algorithm mismatch → `Bogus` (DNS selftest 12/12 → **15/15**).
- **Scope/honesty `[~]`:** the verification PRIMITIVE is done + RFC-proven; `validate_dnssec` still returns `Indeterminate` because extracting RRSIG/DNSKEY RRs from a parsed `DnsResponse` and walking the DS→DNSKEY chain to a trust anchor is the next slice, and ECDSA P-256/P-384 (RFC 6605) + RSA (RFC 5702) verifiers are follow-ups (ath_crypto has p256_ecdsa; the DNSSEC ECDSA encoding needs wiring).
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-dnssec-ed25519.txt`, real Zen4):** `[ OK ] DNS selftest: 15/15 checks passed`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. Also QEMU CI green.

### Security — FDE TPM auto-unlock wired end-to-end (BitLocker/FileVault parity) (2026-07-04, opus) [~] IRON (software TPM)

**Wired the TPM sealing mechanism into the actual FDE unlock path — the encrypted volume now recovers WITHOUT a passphrase when the machine boots into the same measured state, exactly like Win11 BitLocker / macOS FileVault auto-unlock.** Builds on the seal/unseal primitive below. New `EncryptedVolume` API:
- `enroll_tpm(pcr_selection)`: binds the volume's master key to the machine's current measured-boot state (seals it to the given TPM PCRs). Requires the volume Active (master key in hand).
