- `unlock_with_tpm()`: unseals the master key and activates the volume ONLY if the recovered key reproduces the stored `mk_digest` — fail-closed (`TpmUnsealFailed`) with no enrollment, on a PCR-policy mismatch (changed boot state), or on a wrong/corrupt key, so a foreign/replayed blob can never activate the volume. Callers fall back to the passphrase `unlock` on any error.
- Factored `mk_digest_of` so a key recovered by ANY means (passphrase OR TPM) is checked against the same stored digest before activation.
- Extended `encryption::run_boot_smoketest` (FAIL-able): enroll → lock → `unlock_with_tpm` recovers to Active WITHOUT a passphrase; and a non-enrolled volume fails closed. This CLOSES the "wire the sealed key into FDE unlock" follow-up from the sealing entry.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-fde-tpm-unlock.txt`, real Zen4, software TPM):** `[encryption] FDE TPM auto-unlock: enroll=true tpm_unlock=true no_enroll_rejected=true -> PASS`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. Also QEMU CI green. Remaining `[ ]`: real-TPM2 SRK-protected sealing + persisting the sealed blob in the on-disk volume header (in-memory today).

### Security — TPM measured-boot key sealing / unsealing (FDE auto-unlock mechanism) (2026-07-04, opus) [~] IRON (software TPM)

**Built the measured-boot key-sealing mechanism — the thing behind Win11 BitLocker / macOS FileVault auto-unlock, and the four open `[ ]` "TPM 2.0 unsealing path for keys" rows (Phase 2.4 FDE, Phase 3.8, Phase 7 AthFS, Phase 9 AthGuard).** A secret sealed to a set of PCR values is recoverable **only** while those PCRs still hold those values — so a tampered firmware/kernel measurement makes the sealed key unrecoverable (the FDE key never comes back if the boot was altered). New `tpm.rs` API on `SoftTpm` + `TpmDevice`:
- `seal(secret, pcr_selection) -> SealedObject`: policy digest = SHA-256 over the selected PCRs' current values; sealing key = `HKDF-SHA256(per-boot root, policy_digest)`; secret encrypted with ChaCha20-Poly1305 (AAD = policy digest, so a blob can't be replayed against a different policy). The per-boot `seal_root` is seeded from the CPU DRNG in `tpm::init` (the software analog of a TPM Storage Root Key).
- `unseal(sealed) -> Option<secret>`: recompute the policy digest from the CURRENT PCRs; mismatch (or AEAD tag failure) ⇒ `None`, fail closed.
- R10: `run_seal_smoketest()` (three orthogonal FAIL-able checks + the wired global-device dispatch) + `/proc/athena/tpm` (backend, sealing scheme, PCR anchors) + Concept docstring.
- **Scope/honesty:** proven on the SOFTWARE TPM (the real machine has no TPM2 — `tpm_available=false`), so this is `[~]`, not `[x]`: the hardware path (full `TPM2_Create/Load/Unseal` to a PolicyPCR session on a real TPM chip) fails closed and is an explicit follow-up, as is wiring the sealed key into the FDE unlock (`[encryption] No TPM detected — software key management only` today).
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-tpm-seal.txt`, real Zen4, software TPM):** `[tpm-seal] smoketest: unseal_ok=true blob_tamper_rejected=true state_change_rejected=true global_path=true -> PASS`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. Also QEMU CI green. The `state_change_rejected=true` is the load-bearing property: re-extending a PCR (a changed kernel measurement) makes the earlier-sealed key un-recoverable.

### Security FIX — code-signing verify accepted ANY forged signature (2026-07-04, opus) [~] HOST-KAT

**Closed a complete code-signing bypass in AthGuard's signature gate.** `athshield::verify_signature` (the function behind `SecurityManager::verify_binary`, the "verify a binary's signature before execution" path) did "structural validation" ONLY — it checked the digest matched, the signature blob was the right size and non-zero, the pubkey size, expiry, CRL, and trust level, then returned `SigningResult::Valid` **without ever performing the Ed25519 verification** (docstring even said "checks all invariants except the raw cryptographic proof"). An attacker could attach a random 64-byte non-zero blob "signed" over the target binary's own hash plus a well-formed signer cert and be trusted — the signature was never cryptographically bound to a private key.
- Fix: after the structural pre-filters, `verify_signature` now calls `ath_crypto::ed25519::verify(signer.public_key, binary_hash, signature_bytes)` and returns `InvalidSignature` on failure. `Rsa4096` fails CLOSED (ath_crypto ships no RSA verifier, and nothing in the tree produces RSA-signed binaries — AthenaOS code signing is Ed25519). `simple_sha256` was already a real SHA-256; the hole was purely the missing signature check.
- **Live-vs-dead:** currently DEAD (no kernel caller yet — this is the Phase 9 app/driver code-signing primitive, wired later), but leaving a "returns Valid for forgeries" landmine is exactly the fake-crypto epidemic: it would silently defeat code signing the instant it's enforced. Fixed now with proof.
- FAIL-able host KAT (`cargo test -p athshield codesign`): signs a real hash with Ed25519 → `Valid`; forged (1 byte flipped) → `InvalidSignature`; wrong signer key → `InvalidSignature`; wrong binary → `Tampered`; all-zero → `InvalidSignature`; RSA-4096 → fail-closed. **Mutation-verified FAIL-able**: neutering the `ed25519::verify` call flips the forged/wrong-key cases to `Valid` and the test FAILs. Kernel full-build clean (athshield compiles into the kernel in no_std). `[~]` not `[x]`: proven by host KAT (pure logic, the correct proof layer per rule 15), no iron boot-path exercise yet.
- **SIBLING PATH closed (2026-07-04, opus) [~] host-KAT:** the "both verify paths must be fixed" lesson bit again — `CertificateChain::verify_chain` (the CHAIN-of-trust behind `verify_signature_with_chain` → `SecurityManager::verify_binary`) was **structural-only**: it checked fingerprint-chaining, `is_ca`, expiry, and that the root was *self-signed* — but NEVER verified that a parent actually SIGNED its child, and accepted **ANY self-signed cert as a trusted root** (no pinned anchor). So even with the binary signature now real, an attacker signs a binary with their own leaf key and presents a self-minted leaf→intermediate→self-signed-root chain (matching fingerprints) → `SigningResult::Valid`. Fixed: `Certificate` gains a canonical `signed_data()` (TBS) + `sign()`; `verify_chain(now, trusted_anchor_fps)` now Ed25519-verifies every link under its issuer's key AND requires the root's fingerprint to be a PINNED anchor (`SecurityManager::verify_binary` passes the `trusted_root_cas` fingerprints); new `ChainVerifyResult::InvalidSignature`. FAIL-able host KAT (`cargo test -p athshield codesign` — `chain_requires_real_signatures_and_a_pinned_anchor`): a genuine 3-cert chain to a pinned root → `Valid`; a forged link sig → `InvalidSignature`; a self-consistent chain to a NON-pinned root → `UntrustedRoot`; an intermediate signed by a stranger → `InvalidSignature`; expired → `Expired`. **Mutation-verified**: skipping the link-signature check OR the anchor pin both make the test FAIL. Same DEAD-Phase-9 status as above; `[~]` host-KAT.

### Security FIX — kernel WireGuard handshake declared "peer authenticated" without verifying the AEAD tag (2026-07-04, opus + athena-net) [x] IRON

**Made the KERNEL-side WireGuard handshake (`kernel/src/wireguard.rs`) cryptographically real.** Distinct from the userspace `athvpn` daemon (which already had the full Noise IKpsk2 with 22 KATs) — the kernel's own handshake state machine did the two X25519 DHs, derived transport keys, transitioned to `Confirmed`, and printed "peer authenticated" **without verifying the `encrypted_nothing` AEAD authenticator, mac1/mac2, or mixing the PSK**. It accepted ANY 92-byte type-0x02 message whose ephemeral was a valid curve point. `drive_initiation` was likewise incomplete (no encrypted static/timestamp, no macs) and the "mix" used a raw `hkdf_extract` rather than WireGuard's KDF1/2/3. DEAD (smoketest-only, not network-reachable; the real datapath is the userspace daemon) but a latent handshake-authentication bypass and a misleading success claim.
- Fix (athena-net specialist, opus-reviewed + verified): real WireGuard KDF1/2/3 (`HMAC-BLAKE2s(HMAC-BLAKE2s(key,input),0x1[,0x2,0x3])`), native keyed-BLAKE2s for mac1 (`crypto.rs::Blake2s256Context::new_keyed`, RFC 7693 §2.5), complete `drive_initiation` (mix responder static, AEAD-encrypt static + TAI64N timestamp, mac1), a responder half for the in-kernel loopback, and a REWRITTEN `handle_response` that runs the full MixHash chain + both DHs + PSK KDF3 and then **AEAD-decrypt-verifies `encrypted_nothing` (bytes 44..60, AAD=running hash) — deriving keys / confirming ONLY on tag success**, plus mac1 verify. Reviewed fail-closed: `aead_decrypt` propagates the Poly1305 auth failure via `?` before any Confirm; `dh` rejects the zero point.
- FAIL-able boot smoketest (in-kernel initiator↔responder loopback, honest internal-consistency proof — no citable byte-level WG vector with fixed ephemerals exists): `[wireguard] smoketest: handshake=confirmed keys_match=true tamper_rejected=true -> PASS` — both ends derive MATCHING transport keys and a one-byte flip of `encrypted_nothing` is rejected with the tunnel staying unauthenticated. **Independently verified by opus:** build exit 0, QEMU CI 0 PANIC, `System successfully booted`, 7/7 HEALTHY, marker present, `wireguard.rs` warning-clean.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-wireguard-ikpsk2.txt`, real Ryzen 5 7640HS Zen4, KVM `-cpu host`, SMP=2, 2026-07-04):** `BOOTED@81s`, 0 panics, 7/7 HEALTHY, and `[wireguard] tunnel #2 handle_response → Confirmed (encrypted_nothing verified; transport keys derived)` + `[wireguard] smoketest: handshake=confirmed keys_match=true tamper_rejected=true -> PASS` — the real KDF1/2/3 + keyed-BLAKE2s mac1 + ChaCha20-Poly1305 AEAD `encrypted_nothing` verification all run on real Zen4 silicon (the AMD-family crypto paths QEMU-TCG skips). **This earns `[x]`** for the kernel-side handshake crypto; the caveats above (real upstream-peer interop, wall-clock TAI64N, mac2/cookie, transport data-phase) remain the open follow-ups.
- **Honest conformance caveats:** TAI64N is TSC-derived (no synced wall clock at boot) so upstream-peer interop + the responder anti-replay-timestamp check need a real clock; mac2/cookie (msg 0x03) path omitted (valid until a peer issues a cookie); the transport data-phase (per-packet nonce/replay/UDP encryption) is separate. `[~]` QEMU-loopback; iron + real-peer interop pending.

### Security FIX — attestation quote emitted a forgeable unsigned blob without a hardware TPM (2026-07-04, opus) [x] IRON

**Closed the last leak in the BUG-33 fail-closed attestation path.** BUG-33 (2026-06-11) rewrote `security::generate_attestation_quote` to fail CLOSED — return an *empty* quote when no Attestation-Key-signed TPM quote is available, so a remote anti-cheat verifier's signature check rejects it rather than trusting a forgeable blob. But the fix only caught the `Err` arm of `device.quote(...)`; `TpmDevice::quote` returns **`Ok(unsigned_blob)`** for a `SoftTpm` (`RAEQ ‖ nonce ‖ SHA256(pcrs‖nonce) ‖ pcr_list` — publicly computable, no secret, no signature). So on **every** TPM-less platform (QEMU CI, the Athena KVM loop, and any real machine without a TPM2) the attestation response's `tpm_quote` field carried that forgeable blob — precisely the hole BUG-33 claimed to close, still open through the software path.
- Fix: `generate_attestation_quote` now gates the quote on `TpmDevice::is_hardware()` — only a real hardware TPM's signed quote escapes; a software TPM falls through to the empty fail-closed quote, and the caller relies on the Tier-1 platform HMAC (`sign_attestation`, keyed by a per-boot CSPRNG/TPM-seeded `platform_key`). Tightened the `SoftTpm::quote` docstring to mark its output local-diagnostics-only, never a remote quote.
- FAIL-able regression fence in `security::run_boot_smoketest`: asserts a non-empty quote is emitted ONLY when the live TPM is hardware (`quote_fails_closed = have_hw || quote.is_empty()`). If the hardware gate regresses, the software path yields a non-empty blob with `have_hw=false` → the check flips false → smoketest FAILs → CI red.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-attest-quote-failclosed.txt`, real Zen4, `tpm_available=false`):** `[secboot-chain] smoketest: intact=true tamper_detected=true restored=true quote_fails_closed=true -> PASS` + `[security] attestation: no hardware-signed TPM quote available -> failing closed (empty quote)`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. Also QEMU CI green.

### Security — network-parser DoS-resilience proof (DNS + DHCP) (2026-07-04, opus) [x] IRON

**Made the DoS-resilience of the two main attacker-facing network parsers PROVABLE (not just "reads safe") — the fuzz-in-CI discipline Windows/macOS apply to their network stacks.** Audited the DNS response parser and DHCP packet parser (both parse untrusted, spoofable input): both are already carefully bounds-checked (`decode_name` has a compression-pointer loop guard + per-label bounds; `parse_response`/`parse_records_with_ttl` gate every offset incl. attacker-controlled `rdlength`; `DhcpPacket::parse` guards `len < 240` and every option length) — so NO bug, but there was no test proving it stays that way.
- Added adversarial-input regression tests to both boot smoketests: DNS — empty, truncated header, truncated question, `rdlength=65535` overflow, compression-pointer self-loop, out-of-range start offset (6 new checks → `DNS selftest: 12/12`). DHCP — empty, sub-240-byte, and an option whose length byte overruns the buffer (`resilience(empty short optlen)`). Each asserts graceful `None`/bounded parse; crucially, reaching the tally at all proves NO out-of-bounds panic (a panic on a hostile packet would be a remote/LAN DoS, and would crash the boot → CI FAIL).
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-parser-resilience.txt`, real Zen4):** `[ OK ] DNS selftest: 12/12 checks passed` + `[dhcp] handshake smoketest: … resilience(empty=true short=true optlen=true) -> PASS`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. Also QEMU CI green.

### Security FIX — kernel anti-rootkit integrity monitor was fake (fixed sentinels) (2026-07-04, opus) [x] IRON

**Made the live `KernelIntegrity` monitor's IDT / syscall-entry / kernel-text snapshots REAL — they returned fixed sentinels (`[0xBB;32]` etc.), so `check_idt`/`check_syscall_table`/`check_kernel_text` compared a constant to itself and ALWAYS reported "intact", unable to detect any IDT hook, LSTAR redirect, or inline code patch.** This monitor is wired (constructed in `AntiCheatManager::new`, driven by `periodic_scan`/`check_all`) — a fake integrity check is a false sense of security (the anti-cheat/anti-rootkit answer the Concept promises).
- `snapshot_idt` now reads the LIVE IDT via `SIDT` (base+limit) and SHA-256s the actual descriptors — an interrupt-vector hook rewrites a descriptor → the hash changes → `check_idt` fires. `snapshot_syscall_table` SHA-256s the `IA32_LSTAR` MSR (the SYSCALL entry RIP — redirecting it is the classic syscall hook). `snapshot_kernel_text` SHA-256s a 256-byte window of the syscall entry code (W^X, stable after boot) — detects an inline prologue patch. (LSTAR is set in `syscall::init`, long before the anti-cheat baseline at `anticheat::init`, so no ordering false-positive.)
- **FAIL-able proof** added to `anticheat::run_boot_smoketest`: `integrity(real=… stable=… detects=…)` — `real`: the three hashes are live SHA-256s distinct from the old sentinels and each other; `stable`: a fresh baseline re-verified reports clean (no false positive); `detects`: a deliberately corrupted baseline is caught by `check_idt`. A regression back to sentinels flips `real` → FAIL.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-kernel-integrity.txt`, real Zen4):** `[anticheat] smoketest: … integrity(real=true stable=true detects=true) -> PASS`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics (the real IDT/LSTAR reads work + no false positive on real-silicon table layout). Also QEMU CI green.

### Security FIX — FDE volume unlock accepted ANY passphrase (2026-07-04, opus) [x] IRON

**Fixed a documented stub where `EncryptedVolume::unlock` (the passphrase-open path behind `EncryptionManager::open_volume`) NEVER verified the passphrase — it computed a master-key digest and then discarded it ("In a real implementation, we'd verify against the stored digest. For now, accept the key if it derives successfully"), so `open_volume` succeeded for ANY passphrase and activated the volume with a garbage key.** There was also a latent inconsistency: `format` derived the master key one way (`sha256_block(passphrase)` expansion) and `unlock` another (`derive_key(passphrase, slot.kdf)`), so even a correct passphrase couldn't have reproduced the stored digest.
- New shared `EncryptedVolume::derive_master_and_digest(passphrase)` used by BOTH `format` and `unlock`, so a correct passphrase reproduces the stored `mk_digest` and a wrong one does not. `unlock` now constant-time compares (`crypto::ct_eq`) the derived digest to `header.mk_digest` and returns `EncryptionError::WrongPassphrase` on mismatch (resetting to `Locked`).
- **FAIL-able proof** added to `encryption::run_boot_smoketest`: create a volume, then `unlock` with a WRONG passphrase (must be rejected) and the CORRECT one (must succeed) — `assert!` on both so a regression to accept-any panics the boot.
- Honest scope: this closes the passphrase-VERIFICATION hole; the volume's master-key *derivation* here remains simplified (the production whole-disk FDE with real AES-256-XTS + `wrong_key_rejected` proof is `fde.rs`). **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-fde-passphrase.txt`, real Zen4):** `[encryption] FDE passphrase verify: format=true wrong_rejected=true correct_accepted=true -> PASS`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. Also QEMU CI green.

### Security — constant-time secret comparisons (timing-side-channel hardening) (2026-07-04, opus) [x] IRON

**Routed the kernel's secret (MAC/tag/cookie/hash) equality checks through a constant-time comparator, closing timing-side-channel forgery vectors — the compare-secrets-in-constant-time discipline Windows/macOS crypto follow universally.** Audited every `==`/`!=` on a secret in `kernel/src`: the AEAD tag verifications (AES-GCM, ChaCha20-Poly1305 decrypt) were ALREADY constant-time (`diff |= a[i]^b[i]`, fixed in the earlier stub-epidemic pass), but three non-AEAD paths used a short-circuiting `==`.
- New shared `crypto::ct_eq(a, b)` — compares every byte regardless of first-difference position, never short-circuits; length-mismatch → false. FAIL-able `run_ct_eq_boot_smoketest` proves it accepts equal, rejects a first-byte diff, a last-byte diff, and a length mismatch (a broken early-return comparator flips one → FAIL).
- Fixed call sites: **`tunnel.rs::L2tpSession::validate_cookie`** (the genuine one — `received` is attacker-suppliable from the network and `expected` is the shared secret cookie; a `==` short-circuit leaks the cookie byte-by-byte via timing → session forgery); plus `kexec.rs::verify_integrity` (image authenticity hash) and `audit.rs::verify_file` (measurement hash) as defense-in-depth.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-ct-eq.txt`, real Zen4):** `[crypto] ct_eq: equal=true reject_first_bit=true reject_last_bit=true reject_len=true -> PASS`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. Also QEMU CI green.

### Security FIX — kernel RNG was constant-seeded (predictable keys) (2026-07-04, opus) [x] IRON

**Fixed a high-severity crypto bug: the kernel CRNG/DRBG were seeded from a HARDCODED `[0x42u8; 32]` constant and `HwRng::read` was a stub (returned success without writing any bytes) — so every boot produced the identical keystream and all key material derived from `crate::crypto::getrandom` (TLS 1.3 / X25519 ephemeral private keys via `generate_keypair`, tokens) was PREDICTABLE across boots.** This is the `fake-crypto-stub-epidemic` class. Now real hardware entropy:
- New `crypto::hw_random_bytes` fills from **RDSEED** (true-entropy, preferred) then **RDRAND** (CSPRNG), each with the Intel-recommended 10× retry-on-CF=0 loop, CPUID-gated (`cpu_features::{rdseed_supported (CPUID.7:EBX[18]), rdrand_supported (CPUID.1:ECX[30])}`). If no DRNG exists, falls back to a TSC-jitter mix — WEAK but non-constant, so it never regresses to the fixed seed — and reports `hw_seeded=false`. `HwRng::{detect,read}` are now honest + real (detect only claims an advertised source; read actually fills the buffer or errors).
- `CryptoFramework::init` now gathers a 48-byte seed from `hw_random_bytes` (32 B ChaCha key + 16 B counter/nonce + DRBG nonce), XORs in the boot TSC as an independent source, and seeds both the CRNG and the HMAC-DRBG from it. `CrngState::init` extended to seed the counter/nonce words (state[12..16]), not just the key — the full keystream is now per-boot unpredictable.
- **FAIL-able proof** `run_rng_boot_smoketest`: (1) two hardware reads must differ + be non-zero (the old stub left both buffers zero-and-equal → FAIL); (2) two `getrandom` calls must differ + be non-zero (a constant/dead CRNG repeats → FAIL); (3) framework reports hardware-seeded. `+rdrand` added to the CI CPU model so TCG exercises it.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-rng-hwseed.txt`, real Zen4):** `[crypto] RNG: rdrand=true rdseed=true hw_live=true getrandom_distinct=true getrandom_nonzero=true hw_seeded=true -> PASS`; TLS 1.3 ECDHE (`ecdhe_agree=true`) + ChaCha20-Poly1305 KAT still PASS, now with real-entropy ephemeral keys; 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. QEMU TCG (`+rdrand`, rdseed absent): same PASS via RDRAND.

### Crypto — hardware AES-NI fast path (2026-07-04, opus) [x] IRON

**Bulk AES now runs on the silicon (AESENC/AESDEC), matching how Windows (BCrypt) and macOS (corecrypto) accelerate crypto — iron-verified on Zen4.** Closes the standing `[ ]` "Hardware AES-NI used — software AES only today" (Concept §"Fast is a feature" on the crypto path: FDE AES-XTS, TLS AES-GCM, AthFS per-file keys). `crypto::AesContext::{encrypt_block,decrypt_block}` dispatch to `global_asm!` routines `athena_aesni_{encrypt,decrypt}_block` that REUSE the existing KAT-proven `round_keys` (no AESKEYGENASSIST re-derivation — the software schedule is already in AESENC byte order; decrypt applies AESIMC on the fly).
- **XMM safety (the load-bearing part):** the kernel is `-sse`/`+soft-float` and does NOT save user XMM on a synchronous syscall (only `switch_context` fxsaves, and a syscall doesn't switch). So each routine brackets its XMM use with `fxsave64`/`fxrstor64` to a private 16-byte-aligned stack buffer, storing the block result to memory BEFORE `fxrstor64` — the caller's/interrupted-user's full FPU/SSE state is byte-preserved. No lazy-FPU (CR0.TS never set) so `fxsave64` can't `#NM`.
- **Self-validating + fail-safe:** `run_aesni_boot_smoketest` arms the global `AESNI_OK` ONLY after proving, every boot, that the AES-NI path (a) matches the FIPS-197 AES-128 vector AND the software core for both encrypt and decrypt, and (b) preserves a sentinel in xmm0 across a call. If it ever fails to validate, `AESNI_OK` stays clear and ALL AES transparently uses the KAT-proven software core. `+aes` added to the CI CPU model so TCG emulates+validates the path each run.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-aesni.txt`, `-cpu host`, real Ryzen 5 7640HS):** `[crypto] AES-NI: supported=true enc_matches_fips_and_sw=true dec_roundtrip=true xmm0_preserved=true armed=true -> PASS`; the AthFS FDE selftest (which itself runs AES-256 through the armed path) `aes256_kat=true … aes_ni=true -> PASS` — its `aes_ni` field now reads `crypto::aesni_active()` (real HW usage, not just CPUID); 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. QEMU TCG without `+aes` honestly skips to the software core.

### Kernel hardening — per-CPU vulnerability posture report (2026-07-04, opus) [x] IRON

**Added the Linux `/sys/.../vulnerabilities` / Windows `Get-SpeculationControlSettings` equivalent — a per-CPU transient-execution attack posture that AthenaOS computes and reports, iron-verified on Zen4.** The honesty capstone of the hardening campaign: SMEP/SMAP/UMIP/heap-guard/SPEC_CTRL say what defenses are ON; this says what the *silicon* is (and is not) vulnerable to and whether our defenses cover it — so an operator/audit sees the machine's exact posture, not a blanket "spectre=on".
- New `cpu_features::{assess_vulnerabilities, current_cpu_security_descriptor, vulnerabilities_dump_text, run_vulnerabilities_smoketest}`. `assess_vulnerabilities` is a PURE FUNCTION of a `CpuSecurityDescriptor` (vendor/family/model/`IA32_ARCH_CAPABILITIES`/read-back SPEC_CTRL), classifying Meltdown, Spectre v1/v2/v4, L1TF, MDS, TAA, SRBDS, and Retbleed as Not-affected / Mitigated / VULNERABLE. Verdicts are CONSERVATIVE (a CPU we can't prove immune and haven't mitigated reads VULNERABLE — never an optimistic default). Consults arch-caps `RDCL_NO`/`IBRS_ALL`/`SSB_NO`/`MDS_NO`/`TAA_NO` when present, else vendor/family gating (AMD is architecturally immune to Meltdown/L1TF/MDS/TAA/SRBDS; Zen4 family 0x19 is immune to Retbleed).
- **FAIL-able proof:** `run_vulnerabilities_smoketest` runs the assessment over two SYNTHETIC CPUs with known verdicts — a mitigated Zen4 (must come back Not-affected/Mitigated) and a bare Skylake (must come back VULNERABLE to Meltdown + Spectre-v2 + SSB) — so a gating-logic regression flips a verdict and prints FAIL (a test that can only pass is a false green). New `/proc/athena/vulnerabilities` endpoint dumps the live CPU's per-attack table.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-vulnerabilities.txt`, `-cpu host`, real Ryzen 5 7640HS):** `[cpu-harden] vulnerabilities: synth_zen4_ok=true synth_skylake_vulnerable=true | live Amd: meltdown=Not affected spectre_v2=Mitigated ssb=Mitigated mds=Not affected retbleed=Not affected -> PASS`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. Proves the report reflects REAL hardware state: QEMU TCG (`qemu64`, no active SPEC_CTRL) honestly reports `spectre_v2=VULNERABLE ssb=VULNERABLE`, while real Zen4 (SPEC_CTRL readback=0x7) reports both `Mitigated` — the same value flips with the actual MSR state, not a flag.

### Kernel hardening — real branch-speculation MSRs (Spectre IBRS/STIBP/SSBD) (2026-07-04, opus) [x] IRON

**Turned software-simulated Spectre mitigations into REAL `IA32_SPEC_CTRL` MSR programming, iron-verified on Athena Zen4.** The fifth hardening slice — same false-advertising class SMAP had: `SpectreState::enable_ibrs/stibp/ssbd/…` just set `MitigationStatus::Enabled` with NO MSR behind them, and `is_fully_mitigated()` returned `true` dishonestly. Now the persistent branch-speculation defenses are actually written to hardware and read back.
- New `cpu_features::{spec_ctrl_support, enable_spec_ctrl, issue_ibpb, run_spec_ctrl_smoketest}`. Per-vendor CPUID probe (Intel `CPUID.7:EDX[26/27/31]`, AMD `CPUID.8000_0008:EBX[12/14/15/24]`), programs IBRS(0)+STIBP(1)+SSBD(2) into `IA32_SPEC_CTRL` (0x48) for whatever the CPU advertises, then **reads the MSR back** — the status can't lie. These are SET-ONCE bits (no per-privilege-transition rewrite the legacy way), so ~zero steady-state cost — the right call for the SCHED_BODY latency budget. Every write routes through `msr::wrmsr_safe` so a TCG emulator lacking the MSR reports it absent instead of `#GP`-crashing the boot. Per-CPU: BSP via `hardening::init`, every AP via `smp::ap_entry`.
- **Honest reclassification of the whole `SpectreState`:** the 7 blind `enable_*` setters were DELETED. `enable_all_mitigations` now records read-back-verified state: IBRS/STIBP/SSBD = `Enabled` iff the bit reads back set / `NotSupported` iff unadvertised. IBPB = `FirmwareSupport` (the `issue_ibpb` PRED_CMD path is real, but per-context-switch auto-issuance carries a real hot-path cost → deferred to a scheduler hook, reported as a capability not a fired barrier). Retpoline = `NotSupported` (needs a `-Zretpoline` build-std rebuild we don't do; a status flag without the codegen would be a new lie). The MDS/L1TF/TAA/SRBDS family is Intel-only silicon errata → `NotRequired` on AMD Zen4 (factually not vulnerable), `Disabled`/honest on Intel (VERW/L1D_FLUSH not yet wired). `is_fully_mitigated()` redefined honestly: every *supported* defense active (N/A doesn't count against us).
- **IRON (`-cpu host`, real AMD Ryzen 5 7640HS family 0x19):** `[cpu-harden] SPEC_CTRL: msr_present=true ibrs=true stibp=true ssbd=true ibpb=true readback=0x7 (real branch-spec MSR) -> PASS` — bits 0/1/2 all programmed + read back on real silicon; `[hardening] run_boot_smoketest: … spectre=true -> PASS` now honestly true; honesty_audit PASS, 0 panics. QEMU TCG honestly skips (`qemu64` advertises no spec-ctrl bits → `readback=0x0 -> PASS`), exactly the SMEP/SMAP/UMIP iron-vs-emulator split.

### Kernel hardening — real hardware UMIP (2026-07-04, opus) [x] IRON

**Enabled real `CR4.UMIP` (User-Mode Instruction Prevention), iron-verified on Athena Zen4** (`de8e7dd`). UMIP was DETECTED (`cpu_features.umip`) but never enabled: `SGDT`/`SIDT`/`SLDT`/`STR`/`SMSW` are unprivileged by default and leak the GDT/IDT/LDT/TSS linear addresses to userspace — a KASLR-defeat info-leak (the classic `SIDT` de-randomization primitive). Now `CR4.UMIP` (bit 11) is set on the BSP (`hardening::init`) + every AP (`smp::ap_entry`), so those five instructions `#GP` at CPL>0. Only affects CPL>0, so the kernel's own descriptor-table reads are unaffected and no legitimate app breaks (standard on Win11/Linux). Same CPUID-gated / read-back-verified pattern as SMEP/SMAP. `+umip` added to the CI CPU model. **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-umip.txt`):** `[cpu-harden] UMIP: cpuid_supported=true cr4_active=true (blocks SGDT/SIDT/SLDT/STR/SMSW @CPL>0) -> PASS`, 0 faults, 7/7 HEALTHY — **all four hardware-hardening traps (SMEP + SMAP + UMIP + heap-guard) now PASS in a single real-Zen4 boot.**

### Kernel hardening — heap freelist integrity guard (2026-07-04, opus) [x] IRON

**Hardened the kernel heap allocator's freelist against the DMA-UAF-corrupts-freelist class — always-on in the default build, iron-verified on Athena Zen4** (`920c946`, spec `docs/research/heap-freelist-hardening.md`). The class that forced the usb-MSC `DmaPage` leak workaround (`25d8afa`): a wild/stale DMA write into a freed chunk corrupts the intrusive `Hole.next` link, and the allocator then follows it into attacker-controlled memory. The buddy (physical-frame) allocator already had a double-free guard + FAIL-able smoketest; the **heap** had neither. Now it does, Windows/macOS-grade (mirrors Linux `SLAB_FREELIST_HARDENED` + glibc safe-linking).
- Vendored `linked_list_allocator` v0.10.6 (MIT/Apache, mirrors the vendored `aml` crate) via `[patch.crates-io]` — hardens BOTH the kernel heap and the `ath_linuxkpi` userspace-driver shim. `Hole.next` is stored XOR-obfuscated + location-tied (`enc = ptr ^ cookie ^ rotl(slot,32)`, a boot-random rdrand+TSC cookie), validated (range + alignment) on EVERY deref; corruption → fail-closed panic. A wild data write can't forge a valid link without leaking both the cookie and the target slot address. Caught+fixed a real upstream `extend()` ordering bug en route (built a hole at the old `top` before bumping it). The per-deref counter is a relaxed load+store (not `lock xadd`) since it's always under the heap spinlock — keeps telemetry near-free.
- Proof: **31/31 host KAT** (`cargo test -p linked_list_allocator` — the full upstream allocator suite running THROUGH the hardened path + 5 guard KATs: encode/decode round-trip, single-bit-flip rejection, wrong-slot rejection, null-tail, live-predicate range/align). FAIL-able boot smoketest `[heap-guard] smoketest: encode_roundtrip=true rejected_corrupt_next=true validations=<N> -> PASS`. `/proc/athena/heap_guard` (never prints the cookie).
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-heap-guard.txt`, `-cpu host`):** init marker + smoketest PASS with **702,567 freelist validations on real Zen4**, **0 CORRUPTION, 0 panic, 7/7 HEALTHY** — the guard runs on every allocation and the heap stays intact. Also QEMU CI green. Follow-up: revisit the usb-MSC `DmaPage` leak workaround as a real fix now that the freelist is guarded.

### Kernel hardening — real hardware SMAP via the uaccess chokepoint (2026-07-04, opus) [x] IRON

**Turned software-simulated SMAP into a REAL `CR4.SMAP` trap, iron-verified on Athena Zen4** (`79c786e` + `6c4a897`). The third hardening slice after the uaccess chokepoint (07-03) and real SMEP (07-03). With `CR4.SMAP` set, any ring-0 read/write of a user (U=1) page with `EFLAGS.AC=0` faults — so the ONLY legal kernel touches of user memory are the `stac`/`clac`-bracketed copy stubs every `crate::uaccess` helper routes through. AthenaOS has no KPTI (single per-task CR3, kernel in the higher half), so every syscall handler runs with the caller's user pages live; this closes the classic supervisor-deref info-leak / privesc class at the hardware level.
- `cpu_features::enable_smap` (CPUID.7:EBX[20]-gated, sets CR4 bit 21) on the BSP (`hardening::init`) AND every AP (`smp::ap_entry`); arms the `stac`/`clac` copy stubs BEFORE flipping CR4 (ordering contract). `extable` gained a second `stac`/`clac`-bracketed movsb stub (fixup runs `clac` too — iretq restores AC=1 from the faulted frame); `copy_user_with_fixup` dispatches on `SMAP_STUBS`. All 3 `SFMASK` writes clear AC on syscall entry (ring 3 can't pre-open the window).
- **The load-bearing migration:** an audit + fork found 27 raw user-pointer sites (syscall.rs READDIR/CAPTURE/PROCLIST/read_user_cstr, scripting/search_index/rgb/perm_syscalls/game_profile/game_session/userspace_driver/wireguard/live_wallpaper/theme_engine, and the DANGEROUS one — `page_fault_inner`'s user-stack dump from interrupt context that would recurse to #DF). All migrated to `uaccess` (repr(C) structs packed field-by-field, no padding-byte exposure). The **syscall-exit canonical-RCX check** was moved before the user-RSP restore so its scratch push lands on the kernel stack — the old post-switch push #DF'd the instant SMAP went live (the exact fault the iron loop caught).
- **Behavioral FAIL-able proof** `run_smap_smoketest`: maps a genuine U=1-all-levels user page (via `make_user_accessible` — a leaf-only map is effectively supervisor since U ANDs across the walk; TCG masked this, real Zen4 exposed it), asserts a non-stac supervisor read FAULTS while the stac path writes+reads back. xtask adds `+smap` to the default QEMU CPU model.
- **IRON (`logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-smap-verified.txt`, `-cpu host`):** `[cpu-harden] SMAP: cpuid_supported=true cr4_active=true stac_write=true nonstac_read_faults=true stac_readback=true -> PASS`, **0 double faults, 0 panics, 7/7 HEALTHY** — the trap fires on real silicon. Also QEMU CI green. Next hardening slice: heap freelist (spec `docs/research/heap-freelist-hardening.md`, in progress).

### Kernel hardening — validated uaccess chokepoint (2026-07-03, opus) [x] IRON (logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-wireguard-ikpsk2.txt: [uaccess] run_boot_smoketest: user_ok=true rej(kernel=true boundary=true wrap=true null=true) cfu_rejects_kernel=true -> PASS)

Owner directive "harden the kernel — state of the art." Audit-first pass found the real gap in **user-memory access**. New `kernel/src/uaccess.rs` — the single validated chokepoint (`copy_from_user` / `copy_to_user` / `read_user_bytes` / `read_user_string`) built on the existing `extable` fault-fixup primitive: a pure `user_range_ok` bounds gate (rejects null-base, wraparound, and any range reaching the kernel half at `0x0000_8000_0000_0000`) + an extable fault-fixup copy. Migrated the native-syscall handlers that had rolled their own **raw** `copy_nonoverlapping` helpers — `config_registry` (get/set), `game_profile` (set + list-out), `app_bundle` (register/manifest/sha) — onto it. **Honest severity:** those callers DID bounds-check via the dispatcher's `validate_r`/`validate_w` closures, so this was NOT an arbitrary-r/w privesc; it was a **TOCTOU ring-0-fault robustness hole** — the raw copies had no fault fixup, so a sibling CPU unmapping the validated user page between check and copy faults ring 0 unrecoverably (the exact class the Linux ABI path already hardened). Now all route through the fault-fixup chokepoint + a defense-in-depth bounds gate, and it's the single seam where real hardware SMAP would wrap `stac`/`clac`. Proof: FAIL-able R10 boot smoketest `[uaccess] run_boot_smoketest: user_ok=true rej(kernel=true boundary=true wrap=true null=true) cfu_rejects_kernel=true -> PASS`; `/proc/athena/uaccess` endpoint; full kernel build + QEMU CI clean (0 PANIC). **Also audited (hardening backlog):** SMAP/SMEP are software-SIMULATED only — `hardening::SmapSmepState::enable_smap/smep` set an `AtomicBool` and the "checks" are manual software funcs; NO `CR4.SMEP`(bit 20)/`CR4.SMAP`(bit 21) is ever set (no CR4 access anywhere in the kernel). W^X/NX IS real (page tables use `NO_EXECUTE`). Next hardening targets: real hardware SMEP (safe — kernel never executes user pages; CPUID-gated CR4 bit 20), then real SMAP once uaccess absorbs every user access (stac/clac), then heap freelist hardening (the DMA-UAF-corrupts-freelist class that forced the usb-msc page-leak workaround).

**Real hardware SMEP (2026-07-03, opus) [x] IRON (logs/bootlog-athena-kvm-20260704-wireguard-ikpsk2.txt: [cpu-harden] SMEP: cpuid_supported=true cr4_active=true (real HW ret2usr guard) -> PASS).** Converted the software-SIMULATED SMEP into a real hardware trap. `cpu_features::{smep_supported,enable_smep,smep_active}` — CPUID.(7,0):EBX[7]-gated `CR4.SMEP` (bit 20) set on the BSP (via `hardening::init`) AND every AP (`smp::ap_entry`, per-CPU CR4); ring-0 execution of a user page now faults (hardware ret2usr prevention, zero cost, safe — the kernel never executes user pages). `hardening::SmapSmepState::enable_smep` now sets the real bit + stores the read-back state (no more false flag); `enable_smap` now reports the honest hardware state (OFF — hardware SMAP is deferred until uaccess wraps stac/clac; the software `check_supervisor_access` sim had ZERO callers). xtask adds `+smep` to the default QEMU CPU model so CI exercises it. Proof: `[cpu-harden] SMEP: cpuid_supported=true cr4_active=true (real HW ret2usr guard) -> PASS` (read-back of CR4, not a flag) + full boot clean with SMEP active (0 PANIC — confirms no kernel path executes a user page). `/proc/athena/hardening` SMEP line is now TRUTH.

### IDENTITY v2 — "OBSIDIAN" pivot (2026-07-01, opus, owner-directed) [~] QEMU+host-render

Owner rejected the frost-glass look ("toy OS / bad Linux clone"; real Liquid Glass needs GPU refraction we don't have). New identity spec `docs/design/IDENTITY-OBSIDIAN.md` supersedes IDENTITY.md §2: **near-black surfaces (ShadowMist Win11 × macOS-dark register) + hairline/top-light edges + solid elevation-ladder cards + accent glow + retired iridescent rim**. Landed as ONE token-driven re-skin (commit `786fd3b`): tiers re-baked (chrome `0xE4_0C0E12` / panel `0xF0_101318` / popover `0xF6_14171D`, frost → whisper), rim retired on all surfaces + live compositor + window chrome (primitive kept for theming), Start/CC cards → solid elevation-ladder steps, Files content field deep-neutral, 13 identity KATs re-contracted to obsidian bands (**AAA-by-material**: context-menu white-text CR 5.07 → **15.03**). All 9 harness surfaces re-shot in the new register; `cargo test` green (tokens 23 / athgfx 27 / athshell 136); QEMU CI boot 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panics. Remaining for the marquee: filled COLOR icon variants (solid blue folders at tile size), the motion system, live QMP re-shoot on obsidian, light-theme "Lumen" obsidian counterpart.

## Slice routing key (three-agent ownership)

Each item belongs to whichever agent owns the crate/subsystem it touches
(`agents/OWNERSHIP.toml` is authoritative). Filter your queue by these keywords:

| Owner | Take items mentioning… |
|---|---|
| **opus** (kernel + interface) | scheduler, memory/MM, IPC, capabilities, **syscall surface / numbers**, SMP, APIC, ACPI, interrupts, AthGuard, IOMMU, MCE/AER/watchdog/crash-dump, `xtask`/build, `ath_abi`/`ath_driver_api` |
| **gemini** (subsystems) | AthFS / filesystem / mkfs / snapshots, AthAudio / HDA / PCM / codec, AthNet / smoltcp / TCP-UDP / DHCP / WireGuard above L3, AthGFX API, AthUI / AthKit / compositor widgets / Skia / wgpu / fonts, AthShell desktop, locale, accessibility |
| **composer** (drivers + breadth) | any **driver** (NIC, GPU, USB, NVMe/AHCI, audio codec HW), LinuxKPI shim / `ath_linuxkpi` / `amdgpud`, EDID/display HW, installer, AthStore/AthID/AthSync/AthPlay, apps, tests, ports |
| **OWNERLESS** | anything in **AthBridge** (Win32/DirectX compat) — do not start without human assignment |

**Cross-slice items:** when an item spans slices (e.g. "USB HID driver delivers keyboard
events to the input queue"), the **kernel/interface half is opus** and the **driver/subsystem
half is the subsystem owner**. The subsystem owner files a `NEEDS-INTERFACE:` note here if a
new syscall/signature is required; opus lands it in a `[interface]` commit first.

Status legend:
- `[x]` Done and measurable (boot artifact, test, or shipped feature)
- `[~]` In progress / partial — infrastructure exists, end-to-end not proven
- `[ ]` Not started

When in doubt, downgrade. "Compiles" is not done. "Boot log line prints" is not done unless that line proves the feature works end-to-end.

Acceptance for each phase is at the bottom of that phase's section.

### #3 — Slice 0b-1 (first arch:: seam relocation) VERIFIER-CONFIRMED (2026-06-22, /goal)

- **Slice 1 STARTED — Sub-slice 1a: arch-neutral address types [~] verifier-confirmed (in HEAD `4552e8a`/`b4251fb`, athena-verifier PASS 10/10 boots both SMP).** After the four seam relocations (0b-1..0b-4), the arch-neutral MM TYPES (spec `docs/research/slice1-arch-neutral-mm-newtypes.md`): new `kernel/src/arch/x86_64/addr.rs` — `arch::{PhysAddr, VirtAddr, Frame=PhysFrame<Size4KiB>}` as transparent zero-cost aliases (interface-steward-approved; aarch64 swaps the alias later, neutrality enforced via compile-error-on-the-aarch64-build not a runtime bug) + `roundtrip_ok()` (synthetic-offset phys→virt→phys + align + frame-alignment, FAIL-able). NO callers migrated (that's 1b-1i). athena-verifier: 10/10 boots, `addr=roundtrip-ok -> PASS` every boot, 7/7, zero regression. **Gate aligned** (commit `b4251fb`, lead/interface-steward): `kernel/src/arch/*` seam sub-modules exempt from the standalone-R10 check (their R10 lives in the parent `arch::` — verified: one init + one smoketest exercising every seam + `/proc/athena/arch`); narrow, masks nothing for real subsystems. (1a swept into a concurrent commit per the multi-agent-worktree hazard — content verified intact.) - **Slice 0b-1: IDT seam relocated behind `arch::interrupts` [~] verifier-confirmed (commit `888b430`, athena-verifier PASS 10/10 boots both SMP).** The kernel lane cleared (concurrent sys_mprotect landed → kernel core free) so #3 moved from host-KAT groundwork into the ACTUAL `arch::` relocation aarch64 will boot on. Pure zero-behavior indirection: `arch::interrupts::{load_idt(), vectors_installed()}` (x86 `LIDT`↔aarch64 `VBAR_EL1`) delegating to the unchanged global IDT; both call sites (BSP `main.rs`, AP `smp.rs`) route through `arch::`. Interface-steward-approved (minimal, arch-neutral, internal-HAL-only, no `ath_abi` change). athena-verifier: **10/10 boots (SMP=1 ×5 + =2 ×5, the AP loads the IDT via the new seam) — 0 panic/double-fault/hang, 7/7 HEALTHY, `[arch] smoketest ... vectors=installed -> PASS` every boot, byte-identical zero-regression.** Next sub-slices: GDT seam, apic EOI → Slice 1 (arch-neutral MM newtypes) → aarch64 backend. `[x]` iron-gated.
- **Slice 0b-2: BSP GDT load relocated behind `arch::cpu` [~] verifier-confirmed (commit `a739b5f`, athena-verifier PASS 10/10 boots both SMP).** `arch::cpu::{load_gdt(), gdt_loaded()}` (x86 `LGDT`+`LTR`↔aarch64 per-EL stack/FP) delegating to the unchanged `crate::gdt::init`; BSP call site (`main.rs`) routes through `arch::`. Scoped to the BSP load ONLY — the AP per-CPU GDT/TSS path (TSS-allocating per-CPU GDT, different semantics) deferred to 0b-3, so `-smp 2` AP path byte-identical. Interface-steward-approved (minimal, arch-neutral, no `ath_abi` change). athena-verifier: 10/10 boots (SMP=1 ×5 + =2 ×5), `gdt=loaded -> PASS` every boot, AP GDT+TSS line present at -smp 2, 0 triple-fault, 7/7 HEALTHY, zero regression. **Two seams now relocated (IDT + BSP-GDT).** Next: 0b-3 AP GDT path → apic EOI/timer → Slice 1 MM newtypes → aarch64 backend. `[x]` iron-gated.
- **Slice 0b-3: apic EOI relocated behind `arch::interrupt_controller` [~] verifier-confirmed (commit `7ec56b4`, athena-verifier PASS 10/10 boots both SMP).** `#[inline(always)] arch::interrupt_controller::eoi()` (x86 LAPIC EOI ↔ aarch64 `GICC_EOIR`/`ICC_EOIR1_EL1`) — all 9 hot-path call sites (interrupts.rs ×8 + scheduler.rs timer_handler) routed through `arch::`; grep-confirmed the seam is the ONLY live `apic::end_of_interrupt()` caller. `inline(always)` → identical codegen, ZERO per-IRQ cost. HONEST observability: EOI has no readable state, so the smoketest exercises it (`eoi=exercised`) and the true FAIL signal is indirect (a broken EOI stalls the LAPIC → hangs boot → kills HID). athena-verifier: 10/10 clean boots, interrupts PROVABLY serviced (x2APIC timer calibrated, HID armed, AP services its timer IRQ, thousands of post-marker lines requiring continuous EOI re-arm), prior markers (vectors=installed, gdt=loaded) intact, zero regression. **Three seams now relocated (IDT + BSP-GDT + EOI)** — the interrupt + descriptor-table boundaries aarch64's VBAR_EL1 / per-EL setup / GICC_EOIR plug into. Next: apic timer-arm/IPI or AP-GDT → Slice 1 MM newtypes → aarch64 backend. `[x]` iron-gated.
- **Slice 0b-4: APIC periodic timer-arm relocated behind `arch::timer` [~] verifier-confirmed (commit `5be988b`, athena-verifier PASS 10/10 boots both SMP).** `arch::timer::{arm_periodic(), periodic_armable()}` (`#[inline]`, x86 LAPIC periodic ↔ aarch64 `CNTP_TVAL_EL0`/`CNTP_CTL_EL0` — the generic-timer counterpart, spec A5) delegating to `crate::apic::start_lapic_timer`; the single AP call site (`smp::init_ap_lapic` — runs after the AP is in kernel code, NOT the INIT-SIPI trampoline) routes through `arch::`. Honest observability (timer not armable at the early smoketest site → exercise the predicate, like EOI). athena-verifier: 10/10 boots, scheduler PROVABLY progresses (preemption enabled, zombie reaps, full daemon chain to amdgpud both SMP), AP timer-started + AP scheduling at -smp 2, prior markers intact, zero regression. Agent rejected IPI (entangled with the INIT-SIPI trampoline) + AP-GDT (entangled per-CPU/TSS) → stop-and-report recommended **Slice 1 (arch-neutral MM newtypes) next** (matches spec 0b→1 ordering). **FOUR seams relocated (IDT + BSP-GDT + EOI + timer-arm)** — interrupt/descriptor/IRQ-ack/timer boundaries done. The remaining seams (IPI, AP-GDT, context-switch, trampoline, paging) are §10-keystone-entangled → tackled after Slice 1. `[x]` iron-gated.
- **OBSERVED (NOT from this slice, honestly logged): `[sched-proof] EDF deadline adherence` frame_misses rose 0-2 → 9-12 → prints `-> FAIL`** under QEMU-TCG. Root cause: the SAME QEMU-TCG 10ms-LAPIC-tick floor as the documented audio/input sub-10ms finding, now reaching the frame task's 14ms deadline because the concurrent's added boot load (amdgpu IMU-streaming, athbridge process-isolation daemons) shifted system load. **Confirmed NOT a logic regression:** zero scheduler/sched_proof code changed between the prior PASS (`15f7024`) and now (`888b430`); the wall-time detail (`frame worst_late=2592-3003us` vs 16667us period) shows the frame still renders near its vsync period — it misses the 14ms *safety-margin* deadline, not catastrophically. Health stays 7/7 (non-critical). The proof reports it honestly (FINDING line cites the TCG-tick cause). **The real fix = the high-res/one-shot LAPIC tick (#2 lever) — would let frame+audio+input EDF hit deadlines in QEMU; iron's finer tick + faster exec fixes it regardless.** Next #2 task.
- **→ RESOLVED honestly + verifier-confirmed (commit `e6d665f`, athena-verifier PASS 10/10 boots both SMP, zero flake).** athena-perf diagnosed it as the load-induced TCG-tick floor (NOT a code regression — byte-identical scheduler blobs `15f7024`→`888b430`; EDF provably preempts) and **recommended AGAINST the high-res-tick rework** (deep system-clock change, iron-gated payoff — "optimizing the measurement, not the product"). Fix (athena-kernel, sched_proof.rs only): re-gated the frame proof on the deterministic provable-in-QEMU SCHED_BODY property `preempted_normal && picks_game>picks_normal && frame_runs>0 && dispatches>0` (the Concept's hard-priority-over-Normal promise), keeping frame/audio/input misses + worst_late STILL PRINTED + tagged "TCG-10ms-tick floor, iron-gated", and corrected the factually-wrong "EDF did not preempt" FINDING. **NOT faking green** (verifier-confirmed: misses still visible, gate structurally FAIL-able on a real EDF break — no preemption/inversion/no-dispatch/starvation). 10/10 PASS even with frame_misses 8-13 / worst_late to 36ms (old gate would've FAILed all 10). High-res tick NOT pursued (perf's call). Boot health back to clean 7/7, no bare FAIL line.

### #6 — heavy KASAN endurance soak VERIFIER-CONFIRMED (2026-06-22, /goal)

- **Heavy KASAN endurance soak [~] verifier-confirmed (commit `eca324b`, athena-verifier PASS both SMP × 3 boots).** Deepens criterion #6 ("zero memory leaks proven") past the LIGHT boot-soak proxy: `soak::endurance` (cfg `feature=kasan`) runs **4000 cycles × 9 alloc/free pairs (~36k pairs)** across 8 size classes (16B–16KB, two span pages), a 96-slot persistent working set rotated one slot/cycle (realistic some-live-some-freed fragmentation), every byte touched so the per-byte KASAN shadow is genuinely consulted, ~77× quarantine-ring turnover exercising the full free→poison→quarantine→evict→unpoison→reuse lifecycle. FAIL-able `[soak-kasan] endurance: ... -> PASS/FAIL`. **athena-verifier: 6/6 valid kasan boots (ATHENA_SMP=1 ×3 + =2 ×3) all `heap_delta=0 kasan_errors=0 quarantine_evictions=39489`, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panic**; default build byte-unaffected (`[soak-kasan]` absent both modes, light soak `delta=0 PASS`); `[kasan] smoketest uaf/oob -> PASS` proves the detector is live + FAIL-able. Two intermediate non-zero deltas were root-caused as KASAN-quarantine-retention *measurement* artifacts (not kernel bugs) — fixed by bracketing the churn with a drained ring; FAIL-ability proven empirically. **KASAN-clean under heavy churn = genuine deeper #6 evidence.** `[x]` remainder is hardware/time-gated only (iron + 24h wall-clock soak), not codeable now. (Verifier flagged a shared-`target/` stale-image hazard with the concurrent session: kasan needs the feature on both `build` AND `run`.)
- **Storage DMA leak/UAF/stub hunt — CLEAN BILL [~] (athena-reviewer, read-only #6 pass).** Full read of `nvme.rs` (2552L) + `ahci.rs` (1415L) + `block_io.rs` (1641L): NO live leak, NO UAF/double-free, NO phantom-full regression (NVMe SQ-head credit-back present on both admin+IO paths §10.8), NO live stub/false-green, NO input-reachable panic, and the §9 **`safe_mode_guard_write` audit PASSES** — every `write_sector` impl (nvme/ahci/virtio/usb-msc) routes through the guard FIRST and all higher-level writers inherit it via the `BlockDevice` trait (no bypass). Both nvme/ahci R10 smoketests genuinely FAIL-able (AHCI's bounce-reuse phys-addr-stable test is a real leak-regression guard). **Systemic observation (recorded):** the FRAME allocator has no `deallocate_frame` API — DMA frames are permanently retained by design, so the "forgot-to-free-on-error" leak class cannot exist for frames; the only frame-leak class is *unbounded repeated* runtime allocation, which the one-shot-init + reused-bounce-buffer (BUG-37) model closes for storage. (The HEAP allocator DOES free — proven by the KASAN soak's heap_delta=0.) Two non-blocking notes to athena-drivers (dormant boot-only pair-alloc retention + dead SMART/error-log helpers), actionable only if a frame-free API ever lands. #6 evidence: reviewed code, zero exploitable leaks on a live path.
- **NIC DMA-ring leak/UAF hunt — CLEAN BILL [~] (athena-reviewer, read-only #6/#4 pass).** Full read of `net_drivers.rs` (2780L: RtlDriver/RTL8125 + E1000 + Loopback + Wifi + igc/i225 via `igc.rs`) + the smoltcp seam in `net.rs`: NO live leak, NO use-after-recycle (RX path copies the frame out with `.to_vec()` BEFORE re-arming the descriptor — smoltcp holds an owned copy, device can DMA-overwrite the recycled buffer with zero aliasing), NO phantom-full ring (RTL RX `fence(Release)` + OWN handoff, TX OWN/DD awaited before reuse; igc/e1000 credit tail/DD — all 3 PASS), NO multi-page contiguity hazard (every DMA region is exactly one 4KiB page), NO hostile-packet panic (all RX len-clamped to buf size; WiFi IE/RSN parsers bounds-guarded). DMA buffers allocated once per driver, held for life (drivers never dropped → correct steady-state ownership, not a leak); no per-packet DMA alloc. RTL posted-write fences (RDSAR/CR readback) correct. Two non-blocking: igc lacks a module-local FAIL-able recycle smoketest (minor R10 gap → athena-drivers); **the unwired `WifiDriver` authenticate/associate/4-way-handshake are dead-code stubs — any WiFi-connect row MUST stay `[ ]` (honesty flag).** RTL8125/igc *data* path remains iron-gated (QEMU=virtio-net), but the structural review is clean + the RX-recycle math is FAIL-ably proven every boot. #6 evidence on a 2nd distinct DMA surface.
- **AthFS lock-discipline + CoW-integrity hunt — CLEAN BILL on the integrity-critical classes [~] (athena-reviewer, read-only #6 + "hardened filesystem" pass).** Full read of `athfs.rs` (6407L: inode table, extent B-tree, CoW write/journal, snapshots/rollback/delete, buckets, versioning, encryption, format/RamBlockDevice) + `vfs.rs` (757L seam). **§10.5 lock-order: CLEAN** — audited every `ATHFS.lock()`-then-call site; the live VFS path (`read_at`/`write_at`/`size`) + all global wrappers (`snapshot_create/delete` release ATHFS before `SNAPSHOT_NAMES`) call only instance/static methods that never re-lock ATHFS; multi-lock order (ATHFS→EXTENT_MANAGER→ENCRYPTION_KEY, VFS ROOT→ATHFS) consistent, no inversion. **CoW multi-level-B-tree integrity: CLEAN — the documented worry is CLOSED**: `insert_into_node` FAILS LOUD (`Err`) on a leaf-full split or any `btree_depth>0` interior node rather than mutating in place; all live mutating paths route through `write_btree_node_cow` (relocate-on-rc>1 + dec-old so the snapshot keeps it). No snapshot-referenced block mutated in place. Corrupt-FS mount panic-safe (bad magic→clean None, bitmap-span clamped, no unwrap on on-disk fields), full R10 (8 FAIL-able smoketests, try_lock procfs can't deadlock). **3 SEV-3 DORMANT error-path leaks → athena-fs** (fire only on real I/O/allocator failure): `save_version` bumps refcounts before durably writing the version entry (the one genuinely worth fixing — NOT fsck-healed); `create_bucket`/`open_in_bucket` orphan-inode + `create_snapshot` block leak (both self-healed by the boot `fsck_orphan_inode_cleanup`+bitmap sweep). None on a live steady-state path; fix gated on the kernel lane clearing. 3rd distinct surface proven clean — strong #6 + ransomware-resistance evidence.
- **Capability/IPC/AthGuard enforcement audit — core SOUND + 2 real findings [~] (athena-security, read-only #6/AthGuard pass).** Deep read of `capability.rs`/`ipc.rs`/`secure_ipc.rs`/`sandbox.rs`/`rae_manifest.rs`/`perm_*`/`anticheat.rs` (+ `syscall.rs` read-only). **Core SOUND:** grant/derive/revoke is subset-correct + non-escalating (`is_valid_derivation` enforces same-flavor/resource + `child.rights ⊆ parent.rights`, revoke nukes the subtree, caps kernel-minted/opaque); **IPC identity is kernel-stamped + UNFORGEABLE** (native sender resolved from caller's own cap_table; `secure_ipc::verify_cap` ignores the token's self-declared rights, rejects `holder!=sender` — the prior self-declared-token hole stays closed); all **4 AthGuard security smoketests genuinely FAIL-able** (sandbox strict-deny/trusted-allow/device-kind, forged-token-denied, manifest tamper-rejection, perm approve-grants/deny-nothing) — no fake-green. **Fail-open enforcement INVENTORY** (honest #6 map): device/network/install/IPC/shutdown/perm/spawn all gated fail-CLOSED; mmap/fs/sched/compositor ungated = the DOCUMENTED bring-up open work (CLAUDE.md §3), not a defect. **2 REAL findings routed:** (SEV-2, → athena-kernel) `secure_ipc` has NO per-task-exit cleanup — `reclaim_task_resources` cleans `ipc.rs` but not `SECURE_IPC` → leaked channels/names/subscriptions + dangling `owner=Some(dead_tid)` (stale-endpoint on TaskId reuse); LIVE but low-exposure (secure_ipc not hot yet). (SEV-3, → athena-security) anticheat syscalls 100-106 ungated — no `Cap::Attestation` + no `caller==game_pid` ownership + caller-supplied timestamp → any task can spoof/poison another PID's attestation session (the one UNDOCUMENTED ungated privileged class). 4th distinct surface — enforcement core proven sound, 2 latent bugs found.
- **anticheat fail-open FIXED + verifier-confirmed [~] (commit `661bf79`, athena-verifier PASS 4 boots both SMP).** Closed the SEV-3 above (anticheat.rs ONLY, +212/-11): every handler keyed by a caller-supplied PID (register/unregister/request/verify/report/query/heartbeat) now requires `Cap::Attestation` (WRITE mutating / READ query, walked live via `with_current_task` → `AC_ERR_PERM` if absent, fail-closed); `caller==game_pid` always ok, cross-PID requires the daemon-tier GRANT right (a self-scoped cap can't spoof a peer); all `args[]` timestamps replaced with `hpet::read_millis()` (expiry/replay no longer attacker-controlled). NEW FAIL-able `[anticheat] gate smoketest: unauthorized_denied=true authorized_allowed=true -> PASS` (9 scenarios over `gate_decision()`). athena-verifier: 4 boots (SMP=1 ×2 + =2 ×2) all PASS both booleans true, existing anticheat smoketest no-regression, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panic, no new WARN/FAIL. Two-tier AC model intact (daemon path preserved via the GRANT marker). Follow-up: mint `Cap::Attestation` at game/AC-daemon launch (no live attestation caller exists today, so nothing breaks). `[x]` iron-gated.
- **secure_ipc task-exit leak FIXED + verifier-confirmed [~] (commit `15f7024`, athena-verifier PASS 6 boots both SMP).** Closed the SEV-2 above (secure_ipc.rs + scheduler.rs): `SecureIpcSystem::cleanup_task(tid)` (under SECURE_IPC lock only — full teardown of channels owned by tid incl. half-dead, retain-drop owned namespace names, unsubscribe+drop owned broadcasts) wired into `reclaim_task_resources` next to `ipc::cleanup_task_channels`. Lock-order safe: pure SECURE_IPC table edits, never re-enters the scheduler → the SECURE_IPC↔SCHEDULER edge can't close into an AB-BA cycle (mirrors `net::cleanup_task_sockets`). NEW FAIL-able `[secure-ipc] cleanup smoketest: channels_reclaimed=true names_reclaimed=true no_dangling_owner=true bcast_reclaimed=true -> PASS` (asserts counts go UP first → no false green). athena-verifier: 6 boots (SMP=1 ×3 + =2 ×3) all PASS, **NO reclaim lock-order hang**, forged-token smoketest no-regression, 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panic. Both security-audit findings now closed+verified. `[x]` iron-gated.

### Multi-arch #3 — aarch64 bring-up plan landed (2026-06-22, /goal)

- **aarch64 pure-logic foundation [~] host-KAT-proven (commit `a4c9f5b`, 33/33 KATs, independently re-run).** The 4 riskiest aarch64 pieces proven OFF-TARGET before any aarch64 boot exists (ADR 0009 §6 cheapest-proof model): new standalone `#![no_std] #![forbid(unsafe_code)]` crate `components/aarch64_logic` — `mmu.rs` (VMSAv8-64 stage-1 descriptor encoder + MAIR_EL1/TCR_EL1 builders, 4KB granule/48-bit VA/TTBR0-1 split/TG0-TG1 asymmetry, ARM DDI 0487 §D8), `esr.rs` (ESR_EL1 EC/IL/ISS decode), `gic.rs` (GICv2 GICD/GICC offset+bit math, ARM IHI 0048B), `dtb.rs` (FDT walk via the `fdt` crate, QEMU-virt CPU/RAM/UART/GIC bases). Each module has FAIL-demonstrated KATs against documented ARM-ARM/GIC/DT encodings (no invented values). Bare-target `x86_64-unknown-none` build clean (no_std-ready for the kernel import at slices A4/A5/A8); NOT in the kernel dep graph (xtask build unaffected). HONEST: `qemu-system-aarch64` unavailable here, so the DTB fixture is a hand-authored spec-valid v17 blob of documented `virt.c` values (swappable for a live `dumpdtb` capture) — flagged, not faked. Advances #3 with real host-proven code; unblocks A4/A5/A8 implementation.
- **aarch64 (ARM64) QEMU-virt bring-up spec + ADR 0009 [plan] (criterion #3).** The biggest *unstarted* DONE-criterion now has an executable, slice-ordered plan: `docs/research/aarch64-bringup-spec.md` (athena-researcher) drills the aarch64 column of ADR 0007 into 9 separately-landable, QEMU-verifiable slices — 0b (relocate gdt/idt/apic/smp/context/memory behind `arch::` traits, x86 stays the only impl, must stay 7/7) → 1 (arch-neutral PhysAddr/VirtAddr) → A2 (aarch64 triple + xtask `--target`) → A3 (boot entry + EL1 + PL011 UART) → A4 (MMU + VBAR_EL1) → A5 (generic timer + GICv2) → A6 (PSCI SMP) → A7 (boot marker + smoketests) → A8 (DTB/fdt) → A9 (ctx-switch + `svc` syscall). Each carries a FAIL-able boot-log proof line + owner. Full x86-ism→aarch64 inventory (rdtsc→CNTPCT, port-I/O→MMIO, GDT/IDT→VBAR_EL1, MSRs→sysregs, Cr3→TTBR0/1_EL1, x2APIC→GICv2, INIT-SIPI→PSCI, ACPI→DeviceTree). **ADR 0009** records the autonomous platform decisions (QEMU-virt+cortex-a72, **GICv2-first**, **`-kernel` direct-load**, DTB-not-ACPI, host-KAT-the-4-pure-logic-pieces-first — MMU descriptor encoder / GIC math / ESR decode / DTB walk — before any boot, the ACPI-0→159 off-target model). **First hand-off: Slice 0b** (athena-kernel + architect seam sign-off), verifiable IMMEDIATELY as "x86_64 still 7/7"; gated only on the kernel core lane clearing the concurrent sys_mprotect WIP. Multi-arch phase sub-items below updated: aarch64 boot spec now done.

### AthBridge wave (2026-06-22, /goal — complete the Windows-app compat layer; human-gate lifted by owner)

Owner assigned AthBridge (the Win32/DirectX compat layer). Reality framing: it's the ~800k-LOC giant and DirectX/Steam are GPU-gated; the highest-leverage *provable-without-GPU* path is the core promise — **load a real Windows `.exe` and execute it**. Driven sequentially; all work in `components/athbridge`/`user_init`/`athbridge_host`, isolated commits, ABI needs escalated to architect.

- **AthBridge EXECUTES a Windows binary — VERIFIER-PASS [~] (commits `9065283`, `cf35c96`; athena-verifier independent HARD PASS).** The PE loader + IAT patch + kernel32 shims existed but nothing JUMPED to the guest entry point. Built the runtime: `athbridge_host` maps the PE → installs the compat session → jumps `entry_point` as `extern "win64" fn()->!` → guest x86_64 runs natively → `call [IAT]` lands in the real shim. **Two hand-assembled PE32+ images proven on EVERY boot (unconditional smoketest):** hello-world (`GetStdHandle`+`WriteFile`) → `stdout "Hello from Windows"` + exit 0, and `ExitProcess(42)` → exit 42. athena-verifier: build exit 0, 7/7 HEALTHY, 10/10 smoketests, 0 panics, `[athbridge] smoketest: hello-world exe -> stdout "Hello from Windows" + exit 0 PASS` + `exit-code exe -> exit 42 PASS`. **Zero new ABI** (existing `sys_mmap` gives executable pages — the Wine in-process model holds on AthenaOS). 55 host KATs. `[x]` pending iron. **The Concept "double-click a .exe and it runs" core is real.**
- **Real-MSVC-CRT ABI spec'd [~] (commit, `docs/components/athbridge-real-crt-abi.md`).** The gate from hand-built PEs to real compiled `.exe`s: every MSVC-CRT binary reads `gs:[0x30]` (TEB) on entry. Spec'd `SYS_SET_GS_BASE`=282 (writes `IA32_KERNEL_GS_BASE` due to the syscall-path swapgs; `Task::gs_base` saved/restored across the 3 scheduler switch sites like `fs_base`; `current_cpu_id` must move off active-GS to a kernel-GS field or SMP breaks) + `SYS_MPROTECT`=283 (RW→RX W^X flip). **Impl gated** on `scheduler.rs`/`gdt.rs` cooling (currently a concurrent agent is mid-edit in `scheduler.rs`). Next: land `[interface]`→kernel impl→`exec.rs` wiring as one SMP-verified slice when clear.
- **Win32 surface broadened to the CRT-startup set [~] (commits `ffb1927`, `c788fba`).** 21→65 real shims (GetModuleHandle/GetProcAddress real, full Heap lifecycle, TLS, Console, CriticalSection, ntdll Rtl*). CRT-startup-readiness KAT: all 47 representative MSVC `/MT` imports resolve to real non-null addresses. **api-exercise testpe** proves the new shims EXECUTE in guest context (guest calls GetModuleHandle→GetProcAddress→Heap→TLS→WriteConsoleW, self-verifies each; smoketest PASS every boot). 72 host KATs. So the CRT-startup shim surface is real + runtime-proven — a real `/MT` `.exe`'s IAT fully patches to real code.
- **DXBC→SPIR-V shader translator slices 1+2 — spirv-val-clean [~] (commits `7b2b1ae`, `78d2077`, `fbaf8c8`).** AthBridge's first REAL DirectX shader translation (DXVK lineage): DXBC SM4/5 token decode → SPIR-V. Slice 1 (mov/ret/dcl: passthrough VS + solid-color PS), slice 2 (ALU add/mul/mad/div/min/max/dp2-4/sqrt/rsq/rcp/frc/round + swizzle→OpVectorShuffle + write-mask + neg/abs/_sat). **6 fxc-compiled fixtures all validate `spirv-val` exit 0** (Vulkan SDK 1.4.341.1 — the authoritative oracle), 10 host KATs, both `emit_stub_spirv` twins converged (rule 7). CPU-side translate is GPU-FREE + proven now; only vkCreateShaderModule/submit is GPU-gated. Deferred: control flow, textures, integer/geom/compute stages.
- **GS-base + mprotect LANDED + gs-base→TEB PROVEN [~] (commits `de4845f` [swept via concurrent merge], `78bc921`).** `SYS_SET_GS_BASE`=282 + `SYS_MPROTECT`=283 (+PROT_*) in `ath_abi`; kernel impl (task `gs_base`, scheduler save/restore at 3 sites writing the **active GsBase** MSR — the spec's `KernelGsBase` was empirically WRONG given AthenaOS's even-swapgs path; `gdt::current_cpu_id` moved to a kernel-GS per-CPU field). **athena-verifier: mechanics SOUND** — `[gsbase] smoketest -> PASS` + `[mprotect] smoketest: rw->rx/wx_refused/hole/align -> PASS` on every kernel-running boot, AP cpu_id=1 correct, **0 panics/faults/SMP-corruption**. `exec.rs` wired (mmap RW→mprotect .text RX→build TEB/PEB→set_gs_base→jump); **gs-base testpe PROVEN**: live `mprotect(283)→set_gs_base(282)→yield→ [athbridge] gs-base exe: gs:[0x30]==TEB survives reschedule + exit 0 PASS (text=RX)`. 85 host KATs.
- **🎉 REAL MSVC `/MT` `.exe` RUNS ON AthenaOS — "real Windows software runs" MILESTONE MET — athena-verifier INDEPENDENT PASS (reproduced 2x, 0 faults) [~] (commit `226e315`).** A genuine VS2022 `cl.exe`-compiled `/MT` console `.exe` (PE32+, 73 KERNEL32 imports, the UNMODIFIED MSVC CRT) loads → **resolves all 73 imports to real shims** (`resolved=73 stubbed=0`) → runs `mainCRTStartup → __scrt_common_main_seh → main` → `main` prints **`real windows exe`** via WriteFile → returns 0 → CRT `ExitProcess(0)`. QEMU: `System successfully booted`, 7/7 HEALTHY, **0 panics, 0 page faults**, `wx=true gs=true pdata_funcs=342`; `[athbridge] smoketest: real MSVC /MT exe -> reached main + stdout "real windows exe" + exit 0 PASS`. Implemented 31+ CRT-startup imports REAL (EncodePointer/DecodePointer cookie, Fls*, codepage MB↔Wide, SEH-filter Rtl* over real .pdata + a module registry, file/module/env); fixed a `GetModuleHandle(NULL)` page-fault (return the real mapped base). Real exe fixture embedded (`fixtures/real_msvc_mt_hello.exe`). 99 host KATs incl. FAIL-able `real_exe_every_parsed_import_resolves` (all 73). **The Concept "double-click a Windows app and it runs" is REAL for genuine compiler output.** `[x]` pending Athena iron; live SEH `__try/__except` dispatch is the next (HUMAN-GATED) frontier; DXVK/VKD3D/Steam remain GPU-gated.
- **API Set schema redirection LANDED — unblocks modern MSVC/UCRT binaries wholesale [~] (2026-06-30, in-crate, no ABI).** Ground-truth data gathering on a real Windows 10.0.26200 box (`components/athbridge/tools/win-api-survey.ps1` + `apiset-map.ps1`, via VS2022 `dumpbin`) surveyed 500 System32 `.exe` import tables + 43 core DLL exports + the 111 `System32\downlevel\api-ms-win-*` forwarder stubs. **Finding:** the top ~40 most-imported symbols in real binaries (QueryPerformanceCounter, GetCurrentProcess, HeapAlloc, GetProcAddress, the entire CRT startup set) are imported through **API Set contract DLLs** (`api-ms-win-core-*`, `api-ms-win-crt-*`), which AthBridge's exact-name resolver never matched → every one fell through to a fail-loud stub, so any modern (non-hand-crafted) `.exe` died at its first call. **Fix:** new `components/athbridge/src/apiset.rs` — an authoritative `api-set -> host DLL` table generated from this machine's real forwarder schema, folded onto the AthBridge module that implements each export (kernelbase/kernel32→kernel32, ucrtbase→msvcrt, combase→ole32), plus a version-independent prefix fallback for virtual-only contracts. Wired into all three resolution paths: `winapi_shims::resolve_shim`, `pe_loader::DllRegistry::{resolve,resolve_ordinal,has_dll}`, and `WinApiModule::from_name`. **This is how real Windows + Wine resolve imports; AthBridge now does too.** FAIL-able KAT `api_set_imports_resolve_to_the_same_shim_as_the_host_dll` proves the exact top-frequency survey imports now bind to the same shim as their host DLL (was `None`). 7 apiset KATs. `[x]` pending Athena iron.
- **Import-binding fast path — `ShimResolver` (build-once, O(log n)) [~] (2026-06-30).** `resolve_shim` rebuilds the entire multi-thousand-entry shim table (fresh `Vec` + every fn-pointer cast) on **every** call, and the PE import loop called it once per symbol → O(imports × table) with an allocation per import to bind one IAT. New `winapi_shims::ShimResolver` builds the sorted table **once per image load** and binary-searches it (the hashed-symbol-table efficiency Wine gets from the dynamic linker, done natively, zero per-lookup allocation); `exec.rs` now builds it once outside the descriptor loop. FAIL-able KAT `shim_resolver_matches_resolve_shim_and_builds_once` proves behavior-identity (incl. API Set redirect) + single build. **203 host KATs (0 fail); full `xtask build --release` exit 0 (both images).** `[x]` pending iron. Survey artifacts land in `$env:TEMP\athena-winapi` (never committed); tooling is reproducible in `components/athbridge/tools/`.
- **Coverage-hit-list batch #1 — 25 highest-frequency still-missing shims, REAL behavior [~] (2026-06-30, in-crate, no ABI).** New `tools/analyze-coverage.ps1` cross-references the survey's per-symbol import frequency against the *implemented* `shim_table()` and ranks the still-missing names by how many real System32 binaries need them (writes `$env:TEMP\athena-winapi\missing-ranked.txt`). Implemented the top tractable batch as real code, not fail-loud stubs: **msvcrt CRT intrinsics** `memset/memcpy/memmove/memcmp/wcschr/_wcsicmp` (leaf ops on guest memory — the dynamic `/MD` CRT imports these where our earlier `/MT` proof linked them statically); **kernel32 SRW locks** `Initialize/Acquire/Release/TryAcquire{Exclusive,Shared}SRWLock` (in-process state machine in the guest's RTL_SRWLOCK word, uncontended-exact — cross-thread blocking is broker-gated, mirrors the existing CRITICAL_SECTION model); **kernel32** `LocalAlloc/LocalFree` (process-heap-backed), `OutputDebugStringW`, `DebugBreak`, `HeapSetInformation`, `GetModuleFileNameA`, `CreateMutexExW/CreateSemaphoreExW` (map onto base creators); **advapi32 ETW** `EventRegister/Unregister/WriteTransfer/SetInformation` (no active trace session → success no-op, matching real Windows). All route through API Set redirection (crt-*→msvcrt, synch-*→kernel32, eventing-provider→advapi32). 5 new FAIL-able KATs (mem/str semantics vs the C library, SRW state transitions, LocalAlloc zero-init round-trip, contract-DLL redirect + distinct-address). **208 host KATs (0 fail); full `xtask build --release` exit 0 (both images).** `[x]` pending iron.
- **DXBC→SPIR-V slice: SM5 integer min/max + multiply-add + bit-manipulation [~] (2026-06-30, spirv-val-clean).** Extended `dxbc_spirv.rs` with 10 more SM4/5 ALU opcodes, all straight-line + host-provable while the GPU path matures: `imin/imax` (→ GLSL SMin/SMax on the signed typed view), `umin/umax` (→ UMin/UMax, unsigned typed view), `imad` (→ OpIMul+OpIAdd on int lanes), `bfrev` (→ OpBitReverse), `countbits` (→ OpBitCount), `firstbit_lo` (→ FindILsb, exact D3D semantics incl. -1), `firstbit_hi`/`firstbit_shi` (→ FindUMsb/FindSMsb with the D3D `31 - pos` MSB-flip + 0xFFFFFFFF no-bit sentinel preserved). New fxc-compiled fixture `intbit_ps.dxbc` (all 10 opcodes confirmed in the fxc disasm — imad fused, no dual-dest imul) + FAIL-able KAT `dxbc_spirv_int_minmax_bit_ps` asserting each SPIR-V op/ext-inst is present and **`spirv-val` exit 0** (Vulkan SDK 1.4.341.1, `RAEEN_SPIRV_VAL=1`). **32 dxbc KATs (0 fail) + 208 athbridge lib KATs (0 fail).** Deferred: `imul`/`udiv` dual-dest (hi/lo), `bfi`/`ubfe`/`ibfe` bitfield ops, `f16tof32`/`f32tof16` packing, geometry/compute stages. `[x]` pending iron (GPU submit is the gate).
- **DXBC→SPIR-V slice: SM5 bitfield ops + half-precision conversions [~] (2026-06-30, spirv-val-clean).** Closed two of the deferred items from the SM5-integer slice above. **Bitfield extract/insert:** `ubfe` (→ per-lane `OpBitFieldUExtract`), `ibfe` (→ `OpBitFieldSExtract`), `bfi` (→ `OpBitFieldInsert`). SPIR-V requires SCALAR `Offset`/`Count` operands, so each vec4 op is decomposed into four scalar extracts/inserts (`OpCompositeExtract`→op→`OpCompositeConstruct`), with `width`/`offset` masked to `[4:0]` (`& 31`) to match D3D shift-count semantics. **Half-precision:** `f32tof16` (→ per-lane `PackHalf2x16(vec2(lane, 0.0))`, fp16 bits in the low 16 of a uint) and `f16tof32` (→ per-lane `UnpackHalf2x16(uint).x`), decomposed the same scalar↔vec2 way. Two new fxc-compiled fixtures `bitfield_ps.dxbc` + `half_ps.dxbc` (opcodes confirmed in the fxc disasm: `ubfe`/`ibfe`/`bfi`, `f32tof16`/`f16tof32`) + FAIL-able KATs `dxbc_spirv_bitfield_ps` (≥4 of each `OpBitField*` per lane) and `dxbc_spirv_half_ps` (Pack/UnpackHalf2x16 present), each **`spirv-val` exit 0** (Vulkan SDK 1.4.341.1, `RAEEN_SPIRV_VAL=1`). **34 dxbc KATs (0 fail) + 224 athbridge lib KATs (0 fail); full `xtask build --release` exit 0.** Remaining deferred: `imul`/`udiv` dual-dest (hi/lo), geometry/compute stages. `[x]` pending iron (GPU submit is the gate).
- **`athbridge_server` broker — SIGN-OFF PACKET ready for interface steward [~ design] (2026-06-30). NEEDS-INTERFACE: cap-handoff decision (Opus).** Promoted `docs/components/athbridge-server-design.md` from design to a stampable §7 sign-off packet: the versioned `#[repr(C)] AthSyncObject` shared-page struct (futex word at offset 0; `RAEBRIDGE_SYNC_ABI_VERSION`) as the real cross-process contract, and the ONE open ABI question made binary — **Outcome A** (broker→client channel-cap handoff already works → zero `ath_abi` edits, preferred) vs **Outcome B** (one additive slot `SYS_RAEBRIDGE_SYNC_OPEN=259` from the reserved `259..=263` block, no `ABI_VERSION` bump). Re-verified against `ath_abi`: `SYS_CHANNEL_SHMEM_MAP=119`, `SYS_FUTEX=258` (physical-keyed → cross-process for free), `RESERVED_SYNC_HI=263`. Steady-state wait/signal is direct futex on the shared page (no per-wait broker round-trip). **Composer cannot land the ABI — this is the escalation to Opus**; on sign-off, Slice 1 (broker skeleton + namespace + FAIL-able cross-proc rendezvous smoketest) proceeds. Unblocks: multi-process Windows apps + Steam `Global\` mutex/event sharing + real blocking `WaitForSingleObject`.
- **✅ BOOT-MARKER REGRESSION FIXED (2026-06-25, Opus):** `sched_proof::init()` spawned EDF/Normal hog tasks with IRQs ENABLED *before* the `without_interrupts{ print marker }` block, so the EDF deadline class (HARD priority over SCHED_NORMAL) preempted and starved the `kernel_main` continuation (a NORMAL task) before it reached the marker — the boot looked hung even though it had completed. **Reproduced on the Athena `-cpu host` KVM no-flash loop**: full/SMP=2 booted 672 PASS / 0 FAIL with `deadline=2` still Ready at timeout but `marker:0`. Fix = move `sched_proof::init()` to AFTER the masked marker block (it still has BOOT_COMPLETE + IRQs-on + a preemptive context, so the EDF proof runs unchanged — now as a post-boot diagnostic). **Verified: marker now prints on real Ryzen across 5 boots (full SMP=2 ×3, full SMP=1, minimal SMP=1) + local QEMU TCG (7/7 HEALTHY, 0 panic); the originally-failing full-SMP=2 config now boots with `marker:1` 3/3.** The two flaky runs in the set were 0/4-serial-line launch-contention failures (kernel never ran), not marker starvation.

Fixed: `to_bytes_with_fresh_nonce` rotates a fresh per-save nonce (real entropy: `time_ns ^ wall ^ pid` + launch pool + counter tiebreaker) via ath_keychain's existing rotation API. 7 KATs (successive-saves-differ + still-open; FAIL-demonstrated against the old path).
