- **6 live app crates tokenized [~] (2026-06-17).** An Explore audit found the LIVE launchable apps are the ELF crates `apps/{files,settings,text_editor,task_mgr,calculator,terminal}` (the ~14 `athshell/src/*.rs` app modules + `desktop.rs` are DEAD scaffold — never instantiated, rule-7 quarantine candidates, no polish spent). Migrated all 6 onto `ath_tokens` (chrome → DARK palette + RaeBlue ramp; app-specific colors kept, e.g. Files folder-yellow, terminal SGR cells); each gained a `design_proof()` runtime gate (`exit(3/4)` on token drift — the no_std+athkit bins can't host `cargo test`, so this + `ath_tokens`'s own 6 KATs are the proof). Build exit 0 (all 6 compile+link+bundle), boot 7/7 HEALTHY, 0 regressions. Apps were initially statically cohesive; now **live** via `SYS_THEME_GET` (below).
- **`SYS_THEME_GET` (266) — Vibe Mode reaches running apps [~] [interface] (2026-06-17).** New additive syscall (no `ABI_VERSION` bump; `ath_abi` + `docs/SYSCALL_TABLE.md` Block 25) returning a 32-byte `#[repr(C)] ThemeInfo {version, accent_argb, bg_argb, fg_argb, is_dark, blur_radius, palette_id, reserved}` via validated `copy_to_user` (no raw deref — matches the net-syscall fix). `athkit::sys::theme_accent()`/`theme_get()` wrappers; all 6 live apps now read the live accent at launch (fall back to RaeBlue on error). QEMU: `[theme] theme-get smoketest: accent=0xFF4E9CFF matches active_accent ... -> set 0xFFFF8800=0xFFFF8800 -> restored -> PASS`; accent-cohesion + all prior proofs PASS, 7/7, 0 regressions. **One Vibe tap now re-skins the desktop AND newly-launched apps.** Follow-up: a theme-changed event so already-running apps re-skin without relaunch. Remaining cohesion: GameOS couch tiles + media/photo apps when they land.
- **User-pointer validation + allocator hardening [~] (2026-06-17, goal #6 + security).** athena-reviewer core-kernel sweep found a HIGH userspace-triggerable kernel fault: net syscalls 123/124/264 (send/recv/DNS) built slices off raw user registers with NO `validate_user_range` (false SAFETY comments) → unmapped-pointer kernel page-fault (DoS) + attacker-addressed kernel WRITE on recv. Fixed: send/DNS route through `copy_from_user` (extable fixup), recv does `validate_user_range(write)` + `copy_to_user`. Also: SYS_MMAP partial-failure now unmaps/frees the frames it mapped this call (was leaked-to-task-exit); `buddy::free_block` gained a double-free guard (`is_block_free` check → reject + WARN, prevents free-list corruption/UAF); mmap/munmap size `checked_add(0xFFF)` (overflow reject); `memory.rs` smoketest made FAIL-able (was unconditional PASS — rule 16). QEMU SMP=1+2: `[memory] smoketest: ... heap_rt_ok=true -> PASS`, `[buddy] double-free-guard smoketest: rejected_second_free=true -> PASS`. **KASAN/KFENCE finding:** `hardening.rs` has complete KasanState/KfenceState/UbsanState detection logic but UNWIRED (honest, gated off) — KFENCE guard-page sampler now WIRED (below); KASAN-proper (shadow memory / `-Z sanitizer`) deferred (large, needs nightly codegen instrumentation).
- **KFENCE guard-page sampler WIRED [~] (2026-06-17, goal #6 infra — "wire KASAN/KFENCE into the loop").** The kernel now auto-detects UAF/OOB/double-free on a sampled fraction (1-in-100, ≤4KiB) of heap allocations, behind the `kfence` cargo feature (default OFF → default boot byte-identical, verified: 0 `[kfence]` lines). Pool: 256 slots × 2-page stride at `0xFFFF_A000_0000_0000`, object pages mapped, guard pages unmapped (overrun/freed-touch → #PF). Hooks: `OomAwareHeap::alloc/dealloc` divert on `should_sample()` (own Mutex, not HARDENING — avoids allocator re-entrancy); `page_fault_inner` classifies a KFENCE #PF (`[kfence] GUARD-PAGE FAULT -> UAF/OOB`) before the existing handler. Build/run with the feature: `RAEEN_KERNEL_FEATURES="kernel/kfence" cargo run -p xtask --release -- run --release --ci`. QEMU (feature ON): `[kfence] pool armed: ... slots=256 (guard pages unmapped)`, `[kfence] sampler smoketest: double_free_detected=true uaf_detected=true -> PASS`, `honesty_audit: kfence=true -> PASS`, 0 PANIC. **The proof layer that would auto-catch the double-free/UAF class fixed manually above.** Follow-ups: enable the feature in the dev/CI build path (always-on leak detection); a #PF instruction-decoder+RIP-advance to make runtime OOB/UAF *survivable* rather than a diagnosed panic (athena-debugger); iron-verify to promote [~]→[x].
- **Visual-QA screenshot harness [~] (ADR 0004, commit `20fd289`).** `tools/screenshot_qemu.{ps1,py}` — QMP `screendump format=png`. BIOS capture works but stripes (24bpp-as-32bpp); clean UEFI capture pending (TCG boot too slow for harness timeout). Visual pixel-critique gated on this.

- **AthFS file-data CoW now crash-consistent [~] (2026-06-17, charter #2 hardened FS + #6).** athena-reviewer's AthFS sweep (cardinal `safe_mode_guard_write` coverage confirmed CLEAN; CoW/snapshot/rollback correct) found one LIVE gap: the primary file-data CoW paths (`write_inode_bytes_at`, `write_at`) diverged a snapshot-shared block WITHOUT journaling (unlike `cow_write_block`), so an unclean shutdown mid-write could leave a mounted volume inconsistent. athena-fs fixed it — and caught that a NAIVE journal-wrap would be WORSE: `replay_journal` only understood direct-block inodes, but these paths migrate the inode to a B-tree, so replay couldn't revert the extent. Fix = one shared `cow_diverge_extent_journaled` primitive (both paths delegate) + **extent-aware `replay_journal`** (B-tree branch: re-insert the old extent only if it still points at the speculative block, then free it) + a latent compression-flag-dropped-on-CoW bug fixed. FAIL-able `[athfs] cow-journal smoketest: crash_reverted=true fsck_ok=true -> PASS` (RAM volume: snapshot → torn divergence without commit → replay → assert inode reverted + speculative block freed + fsck clean). QEMU 7/7, 0 regressions. Dormant Phase-3 install landmines tracked (multi-level B-tree node-split CoW; >128MiB single-block bitmap OOB).

- **Calculator → real f64 calculator [~] (2026-06-17, goal #5 apps-that-work).** Was integer-only. New `components/ath_calc` — a `#![no_std]` zero-dep recursive-descent f64 evaluator (`+ - * /`, parens, unary, `%`, sqrt/pow via local Newton-Raphson + exp-by-squaring — NO `libm`, stays no_std/arch-gate-clean; `fabs` helper replaces the std `f64::abs`/`fract` intrinsics that don't exist in core). `eval()` + a Windows-style immediate-execute `Calculator` state machine, **never panics on bad input** (`1+`, `(1+2`, `5/0`→DivByZero, `abc` → all `Err`). `apps/calculator` rewired: decimal point, 4 ops with precedence, `=`/C/backspace/+-/%, full keyboard. **17 host KATs PASS** (`cargo test -p ath_calc`, incl. `10/4==2.5` + `assert_ne!(==2.0)` proving the integer-truncation bug is gone, and divide-by-zero-no-panic). Build exit 0 (no_std), boot 7/7, 0 regressions. The lib-extraction pattern (testable engine + thin bin) is the template for any compute-bearing app.

- **Compositor damage-driven wake — sub-frame input latency [~] (2026-06-17, goal #2).** athena-perf found the biggest avoidable input→photon stall: the compositor had NO damage→wake path — `move_cursor`/surface updates mutated state but the compositor pure-polled, so every cursor move/keypress waited up to a full poll interval. Worse, a HZ/JIFFIES mismatch (`timers::HZ=1000` vs LAPIC 100Hz → JIFFIES ~10× inflated) made the compositor's intended "16ms" idle gate fire only ~every 160ms (≈6fps). **Fix (compositor.rs):** `COMPOSITOR_DIRTY` atomic + `mark_dirty()` from move_cursor + all surface-mutation sites; the loop recomposites IMMEDIATELY on dirty, rate-capped by a REAL-TIME TSC `monotonic_us()` source (not the broken JIFFIES gate, TSC primed in init so the IRQ-context cursor path never calibrates-in-interrupt); idle cadence moved off JIFFIES → real ~60fps. FAIL-able `[compositor] dirty-wake smoketest: woke_on_dirty=true capped=true -> PASS` + `[latency-prof] input->present: delta=..us (dirty-wake)`. QEMU SMP=2: PASS, surface-leak PASS, 7/7, 0 regressions. Deferred perf follow-ups tracked: HZ/JIFFIES reconcile + 250Hz tick, render-outside-the-lock (IF=0 full-frame scanout), MSI-X HID wakeups, compositor→SCHED_BODY once EDF runtime-budget throttling lands.

- **Timer HZ/JIFFIES 10× mismatch — bounded fix (Edit 2) [~] (2026-06-17, goal #2/#6).** athena-debugger confirmed `timers::HZ` AND `linux_compat::HZ` were a false `1000` while the LAPIC ticks at 100Hz (10ms/jiffy, JIFFIES++/IRQ) — so every jiffy↔ms/ns conversion was ~10× wrong. Real live bugs it caused: **LinuxKPI `sys_msleep(100)` slept ~1s** (10× — driver-bring-up stall), `SYS_TIME`/`session::now_secs` ran at 1/10 rate, the `[hid-diag]` heartbeat fired ~every 20s not 2s. **Fix: `HZ=100`** in both files (instantly corrects `ms_to_jiffies`/`jiffies_to_ms`/`jiffies_to_ns`/`msecs_to_jiffies`/`usecs_to_jiffies` + all their consumers) + corrected comments + xhci heartbeat `2000→200` jiffies + new FAIL-able `[timers] hz smoketest: HZ=100 ms_to_jiffies(1000)=100 jiffies_to_ms(100)=1000ms -> PASS`. QEMU SMP=2: PASS, 0 regressions. **Deferred (Edit 1, deep/rule-17 own session):** the scheduler EDF clock `now_us = sched.tick*TICK_PERIOD_US(1000)` runs 1/10 rate AND advances per voluntary-yield (not per-time) — degrades SCHED_BODY deadline accounting; fix = decouple from `sched.tick`, drive from TSC `monotonic_us` (compositor already did). The compositor 16ms gate (same root cause) was already worked around via TSC in the prior commit.

- **Render-outside-the-lock — shrink compositor IF=0 window [~] (2026-06-17, goal #2, athena-perf RANK 5).** `recomposite` held `COMPOSITOR` (interrupts disabled) across the ENTIRE frame incl. the ~2M-write 1080p scanout copy, blocking input/timer/syscalls every frame. Fix (compositor.rs): compositing (which reads user `surf.kernel_ptr` pages — UAF-sensitive) STAYS under the lock into the back buffer; a pointer-swap (`mem::swap` comp_buf↔scanout_ready, sw_backbuf↔scanout_backbuf — double-buffered, no tearing) designates the finished frame; lock DROPS; the scanout copy (GpuFb/virtio/GOP) runs interrupts-ENABLED reading ONLY compositor-owned buffers (never user pages → no UAF). New `[latency-prof] compositor: frame_us=.. if_off_us=..` (if_off now EXCLUDES scanout) + FAIL-able `[compositor] render-outside-lock smoketest: scanout_after_unlock=true -> PASS`. QEMU SMP=1+2: PASS, surface-leak + dirty-wake still PASS, 0 regressions. (QEMU-TCG if_off is compositing-dominated; the moved-out scanout is the costly part on iron's uncached VRAM.) Follow-up: same swap for `present_exclusive` (game path); MSI-X HID wakeups.

- **AthAudio mixer producer WIRED — audio actually flows [~] (2026-06-17, goal #2 sub-3ms pillar).** athena-reviewer's audio sweep found the entire mixer/router/HRTF stack (~1800 lines) was BUILT BUT DEAD: `process_tick()` had zero callers, so the SCHED_BODY thread drained a ring nobody filled (no audio post-boot). Fix (audio.rs): the audio thread now drives `process_tick()` each period (scoped lock, never held across `hlt`); the mixer rewritten to additively sum `MixerSource` voices into `mix_buffer` then write `AUDIO_RING` (the producer) — and a double-consumer bug eliminated (the mixer was incorrectly READING the ring). The boot test-tone is now a real mixer source (440Hz square, persistent scratch, no per-period alloc). FAIL-able `[audio] mixer smoketest: sources=1 mixed_frames=1024 ring_filled=true -> PASS` (asserts the producer fills the ring — QEMU-deterministic, not LPIB). QEMU SMP=1+2: PASS, test-tone + codec-walk still PASS, SPSC ring + scheduler untouched, 0 regressions. Tracked follow-ups: app-submit audio syscall (ath_abi), close_stream DMA-quiesce-then-free, `lock_audio()` RAII, audio EDF on the TSC clock (=Edit-1 #31), iron LPIB/audible + sub-3ms proof.

- **`SYS_AUDIO_SUBMIT` (267) — apps feed the mixer [~] [interface] (2026-06-17, goal #2/#5).** Completes the audio pillar end-to-end: app → `athkit::audio_submit(&[i16])` → syscall 267 → validated `copy_from_user` → per-PID `SourceKind::Pcm` mixer voice → `AudioMixer::mix()` → `AUDIO_RING` → HDA. Additive (no ABI_VERSION bump; `ath_abi` + `docs/SYSCALL_TABLE.md` Block 26). Fixed format 48kHz i16 stereo, bounded `AUDIO_SUBMIT_MAX_FRAMES=512`, `MAX_PCM_SOURCES=16`, underrun=zero-fill, no per-period alloc. Per-task voice reclaim wired into `scheduler::reclaim_task_resources` (next to the socket/sandbox sweep — both exit paths). FAIL-able `[audio] submit smoketest: frames_accepted=128 mixed=true -> PASS`. QEMU SMP=1+2: PASS, mixer/test-tone/codec-walk + kill-reclaim all still PASS, 0 regressions. Follow-up: a userspace audio demo app proving the path on iron; LPIB/audible + sub-3ms iron proof.

- **`lock_audio()` IF=0 RAII — close the audio-syscall deadlock window [~] (2026-06-17, goal #6).** Landing `SYS_AUDIO_SUBMIT` (267) made a reviewer-flagged latent deadlock reachable: `AUDIO_MANAGER` (plain spin::Mutex) is taken by both the preemptible audio thread (`process_tick`) and now an IF=0 syscall path — on the single scheduling CPU, a timer preempting the thread mid-lock-hold then running an IF=0 `SYS_AUDIO_SUBMIT` spins forever (the compositor IF=0 class). Fix (audio.rs): `lock_audio()` RAII mirroring `lock_compositor()` exactly (save RFLAGS.IF → cli → lock; drop: unlock → restore IF, release-first); EVERY `AUDIO_MANAGER.lock()` site converted (thread producer+drain, submit_samples, remove_task_sources, dump_text, smoketests); no guard held across `hlt()`. FAIL-able `[audio] lock_audio smoketest: if_disabled_held=true if_restored=true -> PASS`. QEMU SMP=1+2: PASS, mixer/submit/test-tone/codec-walk intact, 0 regressions. (Mixes one ~2.67ms period under IF=0 — bounded, same trade as the compositor, until APs schedule.)

- **AthFS Phase-3 install safety — multi-block bitmap + B-tree hard-error [~] (2026-06-17, goal #3 installable).** Two dormant landmines that would crash/corrupt the moment the installer formats a REAL disk, now fixed defensively: **(1)** the block bitmap (1 block = 32768 blocks/128MiB) AND refcount table (1 byte/block, overflows even sooner at 16MiB) were single-block → OOB-panic on bigger volumes. Now multi-block: superblock gains `block_bitmap_blocks`/`refcount_blocks` (`div_ceil` sized; legacy SBs normalized to 1 on mount; compile-time `size_of==BLOCK_SIZE` assert), every `0..total_blocks` loop bounded by `bitmap_index_limit`/`refcount_index_limit` (clamps a hostile/corrupt `total_blocks` — can't walk past the buffer), allocate/free/snapshot/rollback/fsck/replay all span-aware. 256-block format byte-identical. Snapshots refuse loudly on >128MiB (single-block snapshot metadata = deferred). **(2)** the multi-level B-tree split + the depth>0 internal insert (a silent `Ok(())` no-op dropping extents) now HARD-ERROR (`Err`, logged) — a >508KiB-fragmented file fails loud instead of corrupting a snapshot. FAIL-able `[athfs] large-volume smoketest: bitmap_blocks(40000)=2 refcount_blocks(40000)=10 ... no_oob=true -> PASS` + `[athfs] btree-overflow smoketest: hard_errored=true replace_ok=true -> PASS`. QEMU SMP=1+2: PASS, format/cow-journal/snapshot/rollback all intact, safe_mode write guard + crash-consistency untouched, 0 regressions. Deferred (larger): full multi-level parent-repointing B-tree CoW + multi-block snapshot metadata (lifts the 508KiB/128MiB caps).

- **AthGuard enforcement sweep + device-kind gate fix [~] (2026-06-17, goal #6 security).** athena-reviewer swept capability.rs/sandbox.rs/the syscall Cap-gates/secure_ipc/anticheat: **enforcement is SOUND** — capabilities unforgeable (per-task handle table, `from_bits_truncate` masks rights), `is_valid_derivation` correct (same-flavor + subrange + `rights ⊆ parent`), the 3 enforcement smoketests all genuinely falsifiable, and the 2026-06-11 fixes (perm-grant, IPC live-CapTable token, boot-chain fingerprint) intact. **Fixed (Finding 2):** the sandbox device gate hardcoded `DeviceKind::Gpu` for ALL device claims (fail-closed only by luck) — added `Nic/Storage/Usb/Other` kinds + `class_of_device(pci_class)` threading the real PCI class through `request_for` (device id from syscall-111 rsi; non-PCI/unknown → `Other` = deny). Default/fail-open boot byte-identical. FAIL-able `[sandbox] device-kind gate: gpu_rw_allowed=true nic_denied=true storage_denied=true class_map=true -> PASS`; sandbox/secure-IPC/anticheat all still PASS, SMP=1+2, 0 regressions. + `revoke` docstring corrected (recursive). **Top tracked security item (Phase 9):** Finding 1 — gate the raw driver-claim/DMA/IRQ syscalls 109-118 on a HELD Cap (fail-closed independent of sandbox), needs daemon cap-plumbing (driver_supervisor/amdgpud/i915d/LinuxKPI) + iron; arbitrary DMA = full compromise, so highest-value security gate.

- **Storage sweep + AHCI per-I/O frame leak FIXED [~] (2026-06-17, goal #6 leaks + #4 storage).** athena-reviewer swept NVMe+AHCI: phantom-full-queue (NVMe credits `cpl.sq_head`; AHCI uses the hw slot bitmap), completion bounds/panic-safety, lock discipline (the `nvme-smart-boot-hang` is NOT present — bounded poll), and `safe_mode_guard_write` coverage all CLEAN. Found one HIGH live leak: **AHCI `read_sector`/`write_sector` leaked a 4KiB frame on EVERY sector I/O** — NVMe got the BUG-37 persistent-bounce fix, AHCI never did → OOM the moment AHCI backs the FS (a SATA install target). Fix (ahci.rs): persistent `bounce: Option<(u64,u64)>` on `AhciController` + lazy `ensure_bounce` reused under `AHCI_CONTROLLERS` lock (mirrors NVMe exactly; NO per-call Drop — DMA completes before reuse; `safe_mode_guard_write` kept first on the write path). Also: `init_memory` alloc-once guard (no 3-frame leak per port reset/S3/replug) + NVMe `count.max(1)-1` underflow guard. FAIL-able `[ahci] bounce smoketest: reused=true addr=0x.. reads=4 -> PASS` (bounce addr stable across 4 reads = reused not re-alloc'd). QEMU `--disk=smoketest` SMP=1+2: AHCI+NVMe LBA0 reads PASS, 7/7, 0 regressions. Leak-RATE proof iron-gated (QEMU AHCI ≠ AMD FCH; Athena boots NVMe). Dead `get_smart_log`/`format_namespace`/`submit_on_cpu` carry latent leaks/phantom-full when un-deaded — flagged.

- **Visual-QA loop OPERATIONAL + first OOBE polish iteration [~] (2026-06-17, goal #1 acceptance).** The marquee's acceptance mechanism is now real: `xtask --screenshot` (QMP `screendump format=png` via `run --uefi --production --ci` + desktop-up sentinel) captures clean 32bpp PNGs of the live OS (`docs/design/screenshots/`). First critique (athena-visual-qa, pixel-measured vs macOS Setup Assistant / Win11 OOBE): solid glassmorphic skeleton + on-token RaeBlue, but NOT yet at the bar — 2 blockers (8×8 bitmap font everywhere = the "basic/not crisp" signal; hint text bled THROUGH the Create-account button) + glass/button/field/spacing polish. **First fix iteration (setup_ui.rs):** hint moved to its own row below the button (provably non-overlapping at 4 resolutions — `[oobe] layout smoketest: hint_button_overlap=false card_radius=24 -> PASS`), 4px-grid rhythm, `radius.xl` card, field placeholders + visible caret. **Re-screenshot confirmed the fix visually.** QEMU 7/7, 0 regressions. **Highest-leverage remaining UI fix = crisp AA text:** spec `docs/design/typography-rendering.md` — `components/athfont` already has a full no_std TrueType engine + grayscale-AA rasterizer + hinting (4055 lines, unwired, 0 KATs) and NO .ttf is embedded; gated on embedding an Inter/JetBrains-Mono OFL subset + wiring `Canvas::draw_text_aa` (source-over, fixing the athui/text.rs black-blend). Dead `athgfx/font.rs` twin = rule-7 quarantine.

- **CRISP ANTI-ALIASED TEXT landed — the headline UI fix [~] (2026-06-17, goal #1).** The 8×8 block font was the dominant "not crisp/basic" signal (visual-qa). Now real AA text: athfont gained a proper **filled scanline rasterizer** (even-odd, 4× supersample, analytic horizontal coverage — the old code only STROKED outlines = hollow letters) + `athfont::builtin` embedding Inter (RaeSans, variable font — default-instance glyf renders) + JetBrains Mono (RaeMono); `athgfx::Canvas::draw_text_aa(x,y,str,TypeStyle,fg,family)` rasterizes + alpha-blends **source-over against the real destination** (fixes the black-blend halo); OOBE (`setup_ui.rs`) migrated to the §6 type ramp (title/subtitle/label/body/caption). Boot: `[gfx] draw_text_aa smoketest: face=Inter cov=53401 range=1..255 glyph_coverage=true -> PASS`, 7/7, 0 regressions, image +1.12MB (fonts). **Re-screenshot = transformational:** the OOBE now renders crisp humanist Inter (`docs/design/screenshots/oobe-uefi-2026-06-17.png`) — reads like a premium macOS/Win11 setup screen vs the prior blocky render. Follow-up (S4-rest): migrate taskbar/chrome/notify/desktop/Settings/the 6 apps to `draw_text_aa`; Inter weight-instance (gvar) support; gamma tuning.

### POST-LOGIN DESKTOP BRING-UP (2026-06-15, QEMU-verified, IRON FLASH PENDING)

The sixth iron boot (2026-06-14T2332) reached the **login screen** but no desktop, dead mouse, no DHCP, no amdgpud — while userspace (the triangle demo) ran. Root-caused to a **two-bug chain on the single scheduling CPU** (APs `loop{hlt}` post-boot, so only the BSP runs tasks):

1. **Compositor starvation [x] QEMU.** The compositor thread was `TaskPriority::Game` + EDF deadline but did µs of work then `yield_task`'d, so EDF never throttled it → `pick_next` (game/deadline > normal) picked it every tick → starved EVERY normal post-boot task (user_init, HID drain, net poll, late-flush). Caught by a timer-IRQ `dump_post_boot_diag` (`cpu0 current=TaskId(65)` with 6 Ready normals never picked). **Fix (16c906b):** compositor runs CFS-normal until EDF enforces a per-period runtime budget.
2. **COMPOSITOR IF=0 spinlock deadlock [x] QEMU.** With (1) fixed, userspace finally ran and `create_surface` (syscall 24) hung forever at "acquiring COMPOSITOR lock". **Syscalls run with RFLAGS.IF=0** (SFMASK; syscall.rs:156) and can't be preempted, so a syscall spinning on a `spin::Mutex` held by the preemptible compositor thread (which holds `COMPOSITOR` across the whole ~16ms frame composite) deadlocks — the holder can never resume on the only scheduling CPU. **Fix:** `lock_compositor()` RAII guard acquires `COMPOSITOR` interrupts-disabled and restores IF on drop (release lock first, then re-enable); every `COMPOSITOR.lock()` → `lock_compositor()`. GPU present runs after the guard drops. QEMU: `surface 15 created ... at user 0x88880000` now completes; the syscall returns and execution continues. **General rule recorded:** any `spin::Mutex` shared between IF=0 syscalls and preemptible kernel threads must be acquired interrupts-disabled until APs schedule.

**Next iron flash (safe image) should show:** desktop composites + a live mouse cursor (Razer on port 4) + post-boot threads running (DHCP poll, late-flush). Follow-ups: HP keyboard port-2 `GET_DESCRIPTOR StallError` — **fix landed (QEMU no-regress; iron pending)**: bootlog T1555 showed the LowSpeed keyboard answers an 8-byte EP0 read (`[hid-diag] ... 8-byte read OK`) but stalls the full 18-byte one; the 8-byte-header fallback in `xhci::get_device_descriptor_with_recovery` ran AFTER the heavy `recover_ep0` (Stop/Reset-Endpoint, HCE-halts AMD per §10), which broke EP0 so the fallback's own read `?`-propagated and the keyboard was abandoned. Fix = try the 8-byte fallback BEFORE `recover_ep0` (and `if let Ok`, not `?`). **Config-read resilience also added (same flash):** `bring_up_hid_keyboard`'s three config-descriptor reads now go through `get_descriptor_retry` (one gentle stall re-issue, no destructive recovery) so a transient multi-packet stall there recovers instead of `?`-abandoning the keyboard after the device descriptor was accepted. **IRON T1707: the reorder did NOT arm the keyboard.** The FIRST 18-byte read stalls and HALTS EP0, so every later transfer (incl. the 8-byte fallback) times out (`wait_for_transfer: timeout (deferred=5)` — the deferred count is unrelated command events, a red herring), and `recover_ep0` runs but doesn't restore EP0 on this AMD xHC. The recovery machinery (`reset_endpoint` ring reset + `set_tr_dequeue_pointer` DCS) is structurally correct, so rather than guess again `recover_ep0` is now **instrumented** (logs EP0 `ep_state` before/after + ResetEndpoint/SetTRDeq completion codes that were being discarded). Next flash answers: ResetEndpoint=ContextStateError ⇒ EP0 was never Halted (timeout is a transfer-ring/doorbell bug, look elsewhere); EP0 not Running after ⇒ SetTRDeq didn't re-arm it. **SET_HUB_DEPTH timeout (port-6 VIA USB3 hub 2109:0822) is NOT a driver bug** — `hub_set_depth`/`set_configuration` share the identical no-data control-OUT path, and SET_CONFIGURATION succeeds on that same slot, so the hub is genuinely unresponsive to SET_HUB_DEPTH (likely empty/flaky internal hub); the existing recover-EP0-and-skip is correct (deliberately reclaims ~1s vs probing a dead hub). The install stick belongs in a **USB-A** port, not behind this hub. Proper AP scheduling, re-enable SCHED_BODY for the compositor once EDF has runtime-budget throttling, and the Phase 8 render-outside-the-lock refactor to shrink the `recomposite` IF=0 window.

3. **OOBE auto-advance bypass [x] QEMU.** The no-keyboard auto-advance thread (`shell_runner::auto_advance_thread_entry`) unconditionally `login_guest()`'d + activated the desktop after a ~2.5 s idle, so a fresh first boot **flashed the FirstBootSetup wizard then dropped to a guest desktop** before the user could create a profile (a timeout-skippable OOBE — Windows/macOS never allow this). **Fix:** the guest fallback is now gated to `SessionPhase::Login` only; `FirstBootSetup` and `Install` leave their wizard up and wait for the user (logs `auto-advance: phase=... is not Login -> leaving the current screen up`). QEMU: boots clean to `first-boot setup wizard ready`, 0 PANIC, marker present (the decline line lands ~2.5 s post-marker, after CI's kill point). **IRON T1707 — the gate was necessary but NOT sufficient:** the session boot smoketest (`session::run_boot_smoketest` → `logout` → `force_login_screen` → `return_to_login`) **unconditionally flipped the phase to Login**, clobbering FirstBootSetup, so the auto-advance then (correctly, per the gate) brought up guest (`auto-advance: login idle, bringing up desktop (guest)`). **Second fix (QEMU-verified):** `return_to_login` now routes back to `FirstBootSetup` when `!is_first_boot_complete()` (mirrors `leave_installer`) — `returned to first-boot setup (OOBE not complete)`, no guest drop. **Owner chose sticky setup. Consequence:** a fresh boot parks on the wizard and needs live keyboard input (the open xHCI keyboard item above) to proceed.

### xHCI HCE grind — QEMU boot-time fix (2026-06-15, QEMU-verified)

Reading the full QEMU serial log surfaced a **340-line / ~9.4 s** xHCI timeout flood: `xhci_smoke=9386ms`, Tier-6 USB = 11.1 s. Root cause — QEMU's emulated xHCI wedges into `USBSTS.HCE` (host controller error, event ring frozen) while enumerating the **empty downstream ports (3–8) of its USB3 hub**; once wedged it produces no events, so every dead probe ground its full **100 ms** `wait_for_transfer` timeout (~168 of them). (The isoch USB-audio test-tone was a red herring — skipping it just moved the wedge from dq=104 to dq=119.)
- **Fix (`kernel/src/xhci.rs::wait_for_transfer`):** when `USBSTS` already shows HCE/HSE, keep polling for a completion (an in-flight HID config event arrives in µs and must still succeed) but cap the wait at a **5 ms grace** instead of 100 ms; log the wedge **once per controller** (diagnostic preserved) then fail fast + quiet. On real hardware HCE stays clear → `wedged=false` → full 100 ms preserved, **iron behaviour unchanged.**
- **Result (QEMU):** timeout flood **340 → 0 lines**, `xhci_smoke` **9386 → ~975 ms**, Tier-6 **11.1 s → ~2.8 s** (~8.3 s shaved), `armed 3 HID` preserved, MSC+HID smoketests PASS, `boot health 7/7 -> HEALTHY`. A bigger chunk of the boot-over-6s budget, reclaimed.
- **Still open:** the underlying QEMU USB3-hub-child-probe wedge (live-fix-list #3) is worked *around*, not cured; an actual HCRST-based recovery path is a deeper follow-up (deliberately not attempted — it would re-init and drop the armed HID).
- Also added `.vscode/settings.json` (`rust-analyzer.check.allTargets=false`) so the IDE stops host-test-building the `#![no_std]` binaries (`amdgpud`/`i915d`/`kernel`…) → no more spurious "duplicate lang item `panic_impl`". Host KATs run via `scripts/host-tests.sh` / `cargo test -p <lib>`, never `--workspace`.

### DHCP `Selecting`→`Bound` on iron — OFFER routing fix (2026-06-15, QEMU no-regression, IRON FLASH PENDING)

The 2026-06-15T1324 iron bootlog still showed DHCP stuck at `Selecting` (DISCOVER emitted, RX live, no `BOUND`). **Root cause:** the raw DHCP client only sees frames via `dhcp::handle_eth_frame`, and in `net.rs` `NicDevice::receive()` that call existed **only in the `VirtioNet` backend branch**. Iron runs the **`NetDriver`** backend (RTL8125 = `default=eth0`), whose branch handed received frames **straight to smoltcp** — which has no DHCP socket — so every OFFER was silently dropped. RX worked; the OFFER just never reached the state machine. QEMU (VirtioNet) always worked, so the backend split hid it.
- **Fix (`kernel/src/net.rs`):** the NetDriver branch now drains frames (bounded ×16), routes each through `handle_eth_frame` (DHCP OFFER/ACK consumed), hands the first non-DHCP frame to smoltcp — mirroring the VirtioNet branch. **Lock order:** `handle_eth_frame`'s OFFER path re-locks `NET_DRIVERS` to TX the REQUEST, so `recv()` releases `NET_DRIVERS` before dispatch (re-acquired per frame) — holding it across the call would self-deadlock the spin Mutex on the single scheduling CPU. Also fixed the VirtioNet branch's latent `handle_eth_frame(eth, 0)` → real monotonic `now` so a lease's `obtained_at` matches the expiry timeline.
- **QEMU (no regression):** `[dhcp] rx -> event=OfferReceived` → `event=Bound`, handshake smoketest PASS, no panic.

**Iron flash 2026-06-15T1353 — routing fix CONFIRMED, exposed two more bugs (now fixed).** `[dhcp] rx -> event=OfferReceived` → `event=Bound` **on Athena** (the OFFER now reaches the client — routing fix proven on iron). But it then `lease expired — restarting DORA` in an endless flood. Two newly-exposed lifecycle bugs:
1. **Clock mismatch** — `check_lease_renewal()` read `rtc::seconds_since_epoch_now()` (epoch ~1.7e9) while the lease's `obtained_at` is hpet-monotonic seconds (~tens). `is_expired` was instantly true → re-DISCOVER loop. **Fix:** `check_lease_renewal` now uses hpet monotonic seconds (lease timers are relative; same clock as `tick`/`obtained_at`).
2. **Lease never applied to smoltcp** — the ACK→Bound transition runs in `handle_packet` on the rx path *inside* `iface.poll()` (holding NET_STACK), so it can't call `dhcp_configure`. **Fix:** added `DhcpClient.lease_applied`; `dhcp::tick` (runs after `poll()` frees NET_STACK) installs the lease the first time it sees a Bound, un-applied client; reset on every ACK so renewals re-install.
- **QEMU end-to-end now:** `rx -> Bound` → `[DHCP] Configured: IP .../GW .../DNS` and **zero** `lease expired` lines. Next flash confirms a real lease (router subnet, not 10.0.2.x) sticks on Athena + DNS resolves.

**✅ RESOLVED ON IRON (2026-06-24) — RTL8125 RX + a real, STABLE router lease [x].** Six true iron-flash boots on 2026-06-24 (`logs/BOOTLOG_20260624_183116.dump.txt` is the canonical one) closed this row: `[rtl] RX path LIVE: first frame received (378 bytes, dev 8125)`, `rx_desc_own=64/64 RE=true`, then `[dhcp] rx -> event=OfferReceived → event=Bound` → **`[DHCP] Configured: IP 192.168.1.244/24, GW 192.168.1.1, DNS servers: 1`** — a genuine router-subnet lease (NOT 10.0.2.x), **stable across the poll thread at polls 100/300/600 (~5/15/30 s) with ZERO `lease expired`/re-DORA lines** (both 06-15 lifecycle fixes held). This retires live-fix-list #2 and proves the RTL8125 RX data path + the DHCP DORA lifecycle on real 2.5GbE hardware. Remaining net work is *service* traffic over the wire (TLS-to-a-real-server, the SSH session into `192.168.1.244`), not the driver. NOTE: later `[~]` KVM-sweep rows (README) that still say "RTL8125 RX needed" are STALE — KVM uses virtio-net and can't exercise the 8125; the 06-24 iron dumps are authoritative.

### v0.1 velocity batch — keyboard + boot-time + demo gating (2026-06-15, QEMU-verified, ONE iron flash pending)

Owner directive: stop the one-fix-per-flash cadence; batch all QEMU-closeable fixes into a single image. Three landed together:
1. **LowSpeed keyboard stall (best-guess + diagnostics).** Iron T1353: slot-2 LowSpeed device (port 2) stalls its first `GET_DESCRIPTOR` even after EP0 recovery (the dead keyboard; slot-3 FS HID arms fine). A control-EP STALL is a PROTOCOL stall (USB 2.0 §8.5.3.4) that clears on the next SETUP, so `get_device_descriptor_with_recovery` now does a **gentle re-issue first** (5 ms settle, no reset) and only falls back to the heavy `recover_ep0` (which has HCE-halted AMD before) if that fails. New `slot N descriptor OK on gentle retry` / `heavy EP0 recovery` lines pinpoint it next flash. `kernel/src/xhci.rs`.
2. **USB hub-probe boot-time cut.** Tier-7 (3.8 s) is hub enumeration timing out on an unresponsive USB3 hub (port 6): `SET_HUB_DEPTH` times out, then it still probes each port (~350 ms power-good + 100 ms status timeout each). Since SET_HUB_DEPTH is mandatory before any port request, a hub that fails it answers nothing — now we recover EP0 and **skip that hub's port scan** (reclaims ~1 s of Tier-7). `kernel/src/xhci.rs::enumerate_hub`. **Update (2026-06-16, usbhubd harvest):** before abandoning the hub, SET_HUB_DEPTH now gets ONE **EP0-recovery retry** (mirrors the existing SET_CONFIGURATION-for-hubs retry + the keyboard recover-first fix) — a first timeout is often a wedged-EP0/stale-completion glitch, not a dead hub, and the boot stick may sit behind it. Confirmed against Redox's `usb/hub.rs` (our V2/V3 hub-descriptor + port-status bit handling already matches; the bulk of the hub sequence was already harvested). QEMU: hub enum + MSC-behind-hub (`found 2 MSC device(s)`) + `armed 3 HID` preserved, no regression. Iron retest pending (does the VIA 2109:0822 hub answer SET_HUB_DEPTH on the 2nd try?).
3. **Dev demos gated out of boot (v0.1 polish).** `user_init` `RUN_BOOT_DEMOS=false` gates ALL boot demos: the athbridge test-exe build (~370 mmap syscalls), the linux_hello/relibc/linuxkpi fixtures, AND the full session sequence (VFS / AthUI / **the "Vulkan triangle" shown on boot** / input / driver_supervisor cap-grant / rg port) — via a single early `sys_exit(0)` right after the real daemons (amdgpud, i915d, kept unconditional). The kernel shell_runner desktop is now the only thing on screen post-boot: no triangle, no demo spam, no mmap flood. QEMU-verified — `user_init` prints start→`7900` exit with zero demo sentinels (3000/5000/6000…). (Follow-up: a real `driver_supervisor` supervision loop, spawned unconditionally once it does production work instead of the cap-grant demo.)
- **QEMU (all three):** demos absent, daemons present, DHCP still binds+configures, `boot health 7/7 -> HEALTHY`, no panic. Iron flash confirms: keyboard arms (or the gentle-retry log shows where it stalls) + faster Tier-7 + quiet boot.

### Boot-time (live-fix #1, the machine-enforced gate) — measure-first (2026-06-16, QEMU-verified, iron flash pending)

Iron total boot ~13.6 s (>6 s gate); QEMU ~2-3 s. The gap is bare-metal-only cost. Tier breakdown from `bootlog-...T2008`: **Tier 1 (core infra) = 4.2 s** and **Tier 7 (power/ACPI) = 3 s** are the two big chunks — **USB/Tier 6 is now fast (115 ms)**, so this is no longer a USB problem. Ruled out: TSC-sync (1M-iteration spin = sub-ms) and console scroll (clears once per screenful).
- **Lead:** every `serial_println!` blits glyphs to real GOP framebuffer memory (slow uncached writes on iron, instant in QEMU) + pushes bytes through the 115200-baud UART; hundreds of boot lines × that = seconds on iron only. The ACPI enumeration alone was 159 device lines.
- **First cut (done):** the ACPI per-device dump (`acpi_full::enumerate_devices`) now uses `serial_only_println!` — no framebuffer render, no bootlog-ring eviction; the count stays in the durable log. QEMU no-regression (count + lines still on COM1).
- **Measurement (done):** added `[tier1-prof]` (early/acpi/smp+sched/pci+fb/modules) and `[tier7-prof]` (acpi+pcie/usb/aer+modules) sub-step timing in `main.rs`. QEMU: `tier1-prof early=168 acpi=128 smp+sched=20 pci+fb=44 modules=609`, `tier7-prof acpi+pcie=3 usb=0 aer+modules=1122` — module-init + smoketests dominate even in QEMU; iron will show the framebuffer/ACPI/USB-hub multipliers on top. **Next iron flash pinpoints the real culprit → targeted fix.**

### HID input latency — drain thread promoted to SCHED_BODY EDF (2026-06-16, QEMU-verified 4/4, IRON FLASH PENDING)

Iron T1651 (`logs/bootlog-2026-06-16T1651-internal-esp.txt`): keyboard + mouse both WORK after the 16-TD report buffer (commit 57b12ad), but the user reported the mouse still "a bit slow" and key presses "a little delayed." Root-caused from the log's own telemetry: `[hid-diag] thread alive` showed only `iters=8` — the drain thread (`hid_input_thread_entry`, `kernel/src/xhci.rs`) was being *picked* only ~8×/s.
- **Root cause = pick latency, not throughput.** The 16-TD buffer fixed how many reports a single drain collects; it did nothing for how OFTEN the thread runs. As a `TaskPriority::Normal` task the drain waited a FULL normal-runqueue rotation behind the desktop's many userspace tasks → ~125 ms between drains → a moving mouse delivered position updates in ~125 ms clumps + lagged keystrokes, regardless of how fast the endpoint delivered.
- **Fix (`spawn_hid_input_thread`):** promote the drain thread to a SCHED_BODY deadline (EDF) task — `task.priority = Game; task.deadline = Some(DeadlineTask::new(2_000, 2_000, 200))` — exactly the Concept "SCHED_BODY for hot paths" / "sub-frame input latency" contract for input. EDF tasks are picked FIRST every period (pick_next step 1, ahead of the whole Normal queue), so drain latency is bounded by a couple of scheduler ticks INDEPENDENT of how many userspace tasks exist. Same proven machinery the audio thread uses (period 2667 µs). Period 2 ms not 1 ms: the scheduler `now_us = tick·1000` is a logical clock (`tick` bumps per scheduler entry) and `needs_new_period` uses `>=`, so a 1 ms (=1 tick) period would be runnable every entry and starve the Normal queue (documented pick_next hazard); 2 ms leaves alternating ticks for userspace. runtime 200 µs = 100 milli-cores, far under the 80% EDF admission gate even with audio.
- **QEMU proof (4/4 boots clean):** `[hid-diag] thread alive` jumped from ~8/s to **~530/s** (`iters → ~16000` per boot); all HID slots still arm (`SET_CONFIGURATION + interrupt IN OK`), `EDF 2ms` spawn line present, 7/7 HEALTHY, no panic, `switch_aborts: 0` (didn't perturb the #34 work-steal race window). `reports=0` in CI is expected (headless, no input injected — the iter RATE is the metric). **Iron flash confirms the felt latency** (QEMU can't inject input).
- **Latency floor + next lever:** LAPIC timer is 100 Hz (10 ms tick), so when userspace is idle the floor is ~2 timer ticks ≈ 20 ms; active userspace yields make entries far more frequent → low-ms. If iron still feels slightly laggy, the documented "proper fix" is **MSI-X-driven HID wakeups** (xHC interrupt fires exactly when a report lands → wake the drain immediately) — a follow-up beyond this EDF promotion.
- **IRON T1745 (EDF flashed): confirmed + exposed the log-spam tax.** `SCHED_BODY EDF 2ms` live; drain rate 8/s → **~42/s on iron** (the 100 Hz-timer 2-tick floor; QEMU sees ~530/s from heavier userspace yielding). 7/7 HEALTHY, both keyboard (slot 2 LS boot-fallback) + Razer mouse (slot 3) armed. Felt "better but still slightly laggy" — and the user **couldn't really test because logs flooded the screen**.

### Post-boot log spam → clean desktop, durable logs kept (2026-06-16, QEMU-verified, IRON FLASH PENDING — production "normal user flow" step 1)

Owner direction: move toward a production normal-user flow — boot to a usable desktop, user drives it and reports what's broken, **logs stay saved until told otherwise**. Iron T1745: the post-boot screen was unusable — two bring-up diagnostics had become hot-path floods now that the EDF drain runs continuously.
- **Root cause:** `[xhci] interrupt-IN doorbell ep_index=… target=…` fired on EVERY interrupt-IN re-arm (= once per drained HID report, ~42/s on iron), and `[xhci] HID report (slot…)` had a `|| seq % 128 == 0` steady-state heartbeat. On iron each `serial_println!` blocks CPU0 ~5 ms on the 115200 UART **and** blits a glyph row over the desktop — so the flood was simultaneously the on-screen mess AND a real input/compositor latency tax (CPU0 is the only scheduling core).
- **Fix (`kernel/src/xhci.rs`):** doorbell log → ONE-SHOT (`FIRST_INT_DOORBELL` atomic; keeps the historical target-computation proof, then silent); HID report log → first 16/iface only (drop the `% 128` heartbeat — the `[hid-diag] thread alive` line every ~2 s already reports the live count).
- **Fix (`console.rs`/`serial.rs`/`shell_runner.rs`): gate the serial→GOP framebuffer mirror.** New `console::CONSOLE_MIRROR_ENABLED` (default ON); `shell_runner::activate_desktop` calls `set_console_mirror(false)` once the desktop is presented, so the compositor owns the framebuffer and raw kernel logs stop painting over it. **Durable logging is untouched** — COM1 UART + the 1 MiB bootlog ring (→ `BOOTLOG.TXT`) + the end-of-boot netlog are all unconditional; only the on-screen scribble stops. The safe-mode diag panel is a separate compositor surface and is unaffected.
- **QEMU (no regression):** marker present, 7/7 HEALTHY, no panic, EDF drain healthy (`iters=16330`), doorbell now one-shot, HID report log 0 (headless = no input). The mirror-off only triggers on iron (headless CI exits before `activate_desktop`), but COM1/bootlog capture is unaffected either way. **Next iron flash: a clean desktop to actually drive + test input feel, with `BOOTLOG.TXT`/netlog still capturing everything for bug reports.**

### Leak hunt + userspace-build unblock + Files real-VFS (2026-06-16, QEMU-verified)

Owner `/goal`: hunt leaks/bugs, push the checklist, build the userspace app (Files), rival Windows/macOS.
1. **Surface/resource leak on NORMAL app exit [~] QEMU.** `compositor::cleanup_task_surfaces`, `data_buckets::on_task_exit`, `event_bus::cleanup_task` were called ONLY from the force-kill path (`kill_task`); the self-exit path (`exit_current_task` — every app that closes itself via `sys_exit`) and `Task::drop` skipped all three, and `event_bus::cleanup_task` had ZERO callers. So every windowed-app close leaked its ~1.5 MiB compositor surface framebuffer AND left the compositor holding a surface backed by about-to-be-freed user pages (latent UAF / stale window on screen). **Fix (`scheduler.rs`):** factored `reclaim_task_resources(task_id)` called on ALL 6 exit/kill sites. QEMU: CI exit 0, 0 PANIC, marker, 7/7 HEALTHY.
2. **Userspace build unblocked [x].** `athgfx::vulkan::VkPhysicalDeviceFeatures` was a half-synced 33/55-field struct (OneDrive mid-session mutation of WIP); `user_init` referenced the missing 22 → 22×E0560, whole userspace build red (a `| tail` had masked the exit-1, so earlier "boots" ran stale images). **Fix:** completed the struct + Default to the full canonical 55-field Vulkan feature set.
3. **Files app → real VFS, slice 1 [~] QEMU.** Kernel seeds the session home with the standard folders (Desktop/Documents/Downloads/Pictures/Music/Videos) at `shell_runner::activate_desktop` via new `vfs::ensure_session_home_dirs()`; Files sidebar quick-access now resolves against the LIVE session home (was hard-coded `/home/user`, wrong for guest/athena). Files already routes `/home/…` through real `SYS_READDIR_AT`, so the home view is now genuinely kernel-VFS-backed. Follow-ups: retire the remaining mock `list_path` for `/system`,`/tmp`; real file open (Enter on a text file → text_editor); "New folder" needs a `athkit::sys::mkdir` (SYS not yet exposed).

**Flagged, deferred:** ~~`net_drivers::VirtioNetDriver::send` leaks every TX buffer via `mem::forget`~~ — RESOLVED 2026-06-17: confirmed DEAD (never constructed, software-ring virtual-addr DMA), removed ~570 lines per rule 7 (`QUARANTINED_MODULES.md`); live driver is `virtio_net.rs::VirtioNet` (no leak). **Env hazard:** the OneDrive-synced tree mutated mid-session repeatedly (bootlog/xhci edits vanished; athgfx/user_init/checklist WIP appeared) — recommend committing now + building from the WSL2 clone.

**Stale-checklist note (verify-before-implement):** several owner-listed Phase-6/8/13 items are ALREADY built — e.g. compositor **drop shadows** (`render_drop_shadow`, live in `recomposite`), glassmorphism/blur/HDR tone-map. Tiling exists (`wm_policy::compute_layout`) but only places windows at cell origins (no resize-to-fill yet → "actually tiles" needs a window-resize protocol). Audit each item against code before coding.

### xHCI external-review bug pass (2026-06-16, QEMU-verified, leak-hunt goal)

An external code review flagged 4 xHCI issues; each was VERIFIED against the source (not taken on faith) and classified live-vs-dead before any change:
1. **DMA page leak — REAL, FIXED (`kernel/src/xhci.rs`).** `DmaPage` had no free path, so every `get_descriptor` / `get_hid_report_descriptor` / `control_in_vec` / `play_test_tone` leaked a 4 KiB frame. A blanket `Drop` would be a **use-after-free**, not a fix: `disable_slot` (hub-child cleanup) drops a DeviceSlot WITHOUT awaiting the Disable Slot command or clearing the DCBAA, so auto-freeing `output_ctx`/`input_ctx` there would free pages the xHC still DMAs to. Fix = a CONSUMING `DmaPage::free(self)` called only on the SUCCESS path of the 4 transient sites (after `wait_for_transfer` returned and the result was copied out → hardware done); persistent pages (rings/ERST/scratchpad/contexts/`report_buf`) and the rare error/timeout paths intentionally keep their frame (freeing a buffer behind an in-flight TD is the same UAF). QEMU: descriptors still read (`Device descriptor … / wTotalLength=34`), HID arms, no `NoMemory`, page freed+reused each call.
2. **Stale input-context on CSZ=1 — NOT a live bug, hardened.** HID configures fine on iron (would not if fatal), because the xHC only reads Add-flagged contexts and those are fully written. But `prepare_configure_{hid,msc_bulk,isoch_out,hub}` now `write_bytes(input_ctx,0,4096)` first (matching `prepare_evaluate_ep0_mps`) to kill the class of latent fragility under `expand_input_context_csz64`.
3. **`use_spec_layout` double-shift — REAL dormant footgun + dead code, REMOVED.** The hardcoded-`false` `pack_input_context_for_configure` branch in `configure_hid_interrupt` would, if ever flipped true, move the slot to +64 and then `expand_input_context_csz64` (always run next) would read the zeroed +32 as the slot and overwrite it with zeros → controller crash. Deleted the dead branch + the orphaned `pack` fn + the now-unused `INPUT_CTX_ICC_BYTES` const.
4. **Isoch `MissedService` (code 23) hang — REAL but forward-looking, documented.** `play_test_tone` is a one-shot boot test (real audio is HDA); a missed frame would halt the isoch ring needing Reset-Endpoint → Set-TR-Dequeue recovery. Added a code comment + this Phase 2.6/7 item for when USB isoch becomes a real AthAudio sink — not built into the boot test (would be untested, unused recovery code).

- **Still iron-flash-gated (real-hardware *values*/devices, KVM can't supply):** live thermal °C, RTL8125 **RX** against the real LAN → real DHCP lease, real USB-device enumeration, the hardware TPM transport, and the full multi-reboot A/B round-trip on a real disk.

### IRON VERIFICATION (Athena full bootlog, 2026-06-13 — `logs/bootlog-2026-06-13T1844-internal-esp.txt`)

Posted-write-needs-readback: reading `RTL_RCR`/`RTL_CR` after RX-enable flushes the receiver-on write. **DHCP-to-Bound** was then blocked by a *second* bug — **nothing drove `net::poll_full()` after boot** (only the ~58ms boot loop), so DHCP could never finish a real router's OFFER round-trip. Fixed by `net::spawn_poll_thread()` (a forever ~50ms post-boot poller). **Next iron flash confirms `[net] post-boot: DHCP BOUND`** — the gateway to all networking.

- **AMD MSRs 1.3**: `cppc=true svm=true smca=true banks=32 -> PASS`; x2APIC mode
- **Audio 2.6**: `wrote_samples=960 hda_playback=1 -> PASS` (real HDA codec playback)
- **Storage**: NVMe LBA0 read on the real SSD; AHCI; AthFS full suite (format/buckets/encryption `aes_ni=true`/rollback)
- **PCIe AER 4.3**: `aer_devices=4 scanned=45 corr_bits=4` — real AER caps walked, real correctable bits observed
- **IOMMU 4.2 tables**: AMD-Vi DTE/devtab/cmdbuf selftests PASS on iron
- **USB 2.1**: all 4 xHCI controllers bound (`4 bound, 0 failed-init`); HID keyboard armed; hubs enumerated; `[usb-summary]` + bootlog-READY one-photo diagnostics working as designed
- **Net**: RTL8125 link up, `DHCPDISCOVER emitted=true` (TX works), `[netlog] end-of-boot: broadcast 70 chunk(s)` (UDP log channel TX on iron)
- **Breadth suite on iron**: firewall 7/7 · DNS 5/5 · QUIC 7/7 · traffic-shaper 6/6 · battery fuel-gauge 10/10 · EDID 7/7 · compositor-fx 5/5 · TLS 1.3 loopback PASS
- **Security on iron**: full crypto KAT suite (AES-GCM/ChaCha20/Ed25519/X25519/ECDSA/HMAC/Argon2id/BLAKE2), secboot chain, sandbox, manifests, secure-IPC, anticheat, lockdown, hardening (KASLR/canary/CFI/WX/SMAP/SMEP/spectre)
- **Plumbing on iron**: crash-dump region, OOM, extable, memlimits, sessions, config rollback, RGB, controllers (DualSense/Xbox parse), installer account+payload, LinuxKPI host shim

**Open after this boot (the live fix list):** (1) AML *method-runtime* opcodes — `\_PIC` evaluation fails `UnexpectedByte(91)` and `scan_pci_routing: 0 _PRT candidate(s)`: method bodies hit ext-prefix statement opcodes (Acquire/Release/Sleep/Stall…) the interpreter lacks — host-reproducible via `tools/aml_probe`; (2) USB-MSC stick: `MSC=0`, `2 USB4 fn(s)` present + USB3-hub child probes time out (`GetPortStatus(slot 5) Timeout`) — next boot put the stick in a rear **USB-A** port (ctrl1–3 port groups are empty and bound); (3) DHCP stuck at `Selecting` — RX path unproven on the 8125; (4) TSC sync WARN across 12 CPUs (4.8); (5) boot time 11.0 s > 6 s target; (6) watchdog `amd-efch` re-test (SMBus subclass bug fixed post-flash at HEAD).

**THIRD IRON BOOT (2026-06-12, `logs/BOOTLOG.netlog.txt` — delivered OVER THE LAN, 73/73 netlog chunks, 82 PASS / 0 FAIL / 0 PANIC): the evidence loop is fully automated.** `[rtl] TX path LIVE: first descriptor consumed (dev 8125, doorbell 0x90)` — the 8125 TX fix proven by the delivery itself; AthFS snapshot-syscall + rollback round-trip + compression-flag all PASS on iron (safe-mode RAM-volume harness). Still open: 8125 RX (DHCP `Selecting`; RX_FETCH fix landed at cb7e4a8, next boot verifies), USB (`MSC=0 HID-armed=0` this boot — keyboard did not arm either; port placement TBD), TSC sync, boot time.

**SECOND IRON BOOT (2026-06-11T23:31, `logs/bootlog-2026-06-11T2331-internal-esp.txt` — 126 PASS / 0 FAIL / 0 PANIC, no regressions): items (1) and (6) CLOSED on iron.** `\_PIC -> Integer(0)`; `scan_pci_routing: found 17 _PRT candidate(s)` → `[pci] Routing table: 84 entries parsed from _PRT`; `[watchdog] hw amd-efch PROVEN: countdown 300 -> 297 over 350ms, left STOPPED` (WDT control 0x14 at FED80B00, SMBus 00:14.0); `[netlog] end-of-boot: broadcast 71 chunk(s)`. Still open: USB-MSC stick (unchanged — same port?), DHCP `Selecting` (8125 RX), TSC sync (11/12 report before timeout), boot time 11.1 s, watchdog armed mode.

---

## Lines-of-code target (read this before adding code)

**Target: ~2.5 million lines of first-party Rust at 1.0. Aspire to ship at less.**

LOC is *not* the goal — capability per kLOC is. The number below exists to anchor against bloat, not to celebrate. Reference points:

| Project | LOC | Notes |
|---------|-----|-------|
| Redox OS kernel | ~250k Rust | Working Rust microkernel |
| Servo browser engine | ~1M Rust | One of the largest production Rust projects |
| Wine source | ~3.5M C | What AthBridge has to functionally replace |
| Linux kernel only | ~36M C | Concept §R7 explicitly rejects this lineage |
| Windows full OS | ~60M C/C++ | What "bloat chasing enterprise" looks like |
| macOS full OS | ~85M C/C++/ObjC | Walled-garden cost line |

Bottom-up estimate for AthenaOS 1.0 first-party Rust:

| Bucket | Rust LOC | Notes |
|--------|----------|-------|
| AthKernel core | ~80k | scheduler, memory, IPC, capabilities, syscall surface |
| Drivers | ~400k | xHCI, NVMe, AHCI, e1000e/igc/RTL8125, HDA, GPU shims |
| AthFS | ~40k | CoW, snapshots, encryption, tiering, fsck |
| AthGFX | ~50k | wgpu does the GPU heavy lifting |
| AthAudio | ~40k | engine + routing |
| AthUI | ~80k | widgets, layout, glassmorphism |
| AthKit | ~30k | declarative API + bundler |
| AthGuard | ~50k | caps, sign, sandbox, attestation |
| AthNet | ~60k | smoltcp does protocol heavy lifting |
| **AthBridge** | **~800k** | **single largest module; Wine is 3.5M C** |
| Apps + AthShell + GameOS | ~400k | |
| Store / ID / Sync | ~100k | |
| Installer + bootloader + xtask + tests | ~100k | |
| Docs / build / scripts | ~100k | |
| Slack for things we forgot | ~200k | |
| **First-party total** | **~2.53M Rust** | **≈ 5M LOC equivalent in C @ 2× density** |
| Vendored deps (wgpu, Skia, smoltcp, x86_64, ...) | ~750k | |
| **Effective total** | **~3.3M** | the number that matters |

### Why 2.5M, not 100M

- **Rust gives you ~2× density vs C** (generics, traits, derive, iterator combinators, pattern matching, `?`). 2.5M Rust ≈ 5M C.
- **AthBridge is the dominant cost, *not* the kernel.** Aggressive reuse of DXVK/VKD3D source is the bet — rewriting them from scratch would push AthBridge alone past 2M LOC.
- **Concept §R7 (no Linux-clones) is anti-bloat by design.** The doc literally celebrates the 36k-line dead-code sweep we lived through this session. Code is a cost, not a deliverable.
- **Sustainable output is the binding constraint.** A senior systems engineer ships ~10k LOC of production Rust per year. 2.5M LOC = 250 engineer-years. A 10-person team in 25 years; 50-person team in 5. The Concept doc's 5-year roadmap is only achievable at the lean number.
- **100M would be ~3× the entire Linux kernel and ~400× Redox.** It would be the largest software project ever and would have ~0 maintainers.

### Practical rules per commit

- If a commit adds ~1000 LOC without a new boot-log artifact or a new shipped feature: push back.
- If a new module exists but doesn't honor the R10 4-artifact contract (init + smoketest + procfs + Concept docstring): it doesn't count as shipped.
- Measure **capability per kLOC** every release. If it's flat or declining, we're adding mass without value.
- Optimize the metric you actually care about: boot time, capability surface, attack surface, bug density. LOC is a means, never an end.

---

## Phase 0 — Foundations already in place (snapshot)

These keep the rest from rotting. Verify on every commit.

- [x] Boot under 1 second in QEMU (currently ~700 ms)
- [x] SMP: 4 CPUs alive, all heartbeating, all picking tasks
- [x] Buddy allocator + smoketest
- [x] Capability framework + 14 Cap variants + /proc/athena/caps
- [x] Userspace driver framework (`userspace_driver.rs`, syscalls 109-116)
- [x] LinuxKPI Phase 1–3 — `ath_linuxkpi` + `linuxkpi_host` syscalls 127–140; Phase 2: claim/ioremap/IRQ doorbell; Phase 3: `dma_alloc_coherent` + `dma_free` on claimed device (`self_test_phase3_on`); QEMU: `msg: 8104`/`8200`, `[linuxkpi] dma_alloc_coherent`, `irq_delivery=dispatch_msi+pending` (`docs/LINUXKPI_PHASE1.md`, `LINUXKPI_PHASE2.md`)
- [~] LinuxKPI universal-primitive surface — **major expansion 2026-06-10 (Opus): ~31 → 168 exported C-ABI symbols** so an unmodified Linux `.ko` resolves its undefined symbols and runs early `*_probe()` init. New modules in `components/ath_linuxkpi/src/`: `string.rs` (mem/str builtins), `atomic.rs` (atomic_t/atomic64_t + bitops + mb/rmb/wmb), `delay.rs` (udelay/ndelay/mdelay/usleep_range/ktime_get_ns), `kalloc.rs` (vmalloc/kvmalloc/kcalloc/krealloc/kmemdup/kstrdup/devm_*/page alloc), `sync.rs` (spinlocks + irqsave, mutex init/trylock, `struct completion`, rwsem, schedule/cond_resched), `device.rs` (printk/_printk/dev_err/warn/info/dbg), `pci_ext.rs` (pci_set_master/regions/config byte+word/pci_resource_start+len+flags/pci_alloc_irq_vectors/pci_find_capability/dma_set_mask_*), `dma_stream.rs` (dma_map_single/page/sync/mapping_error), real Linux-signature `request_irq`/`request_threaded_irq`/`free_irq`/`enable_irq` + handler registry + `lkpi_serve_irq` pump in `irq.rs`; bump heap 256 KiB→8 MiB. Builds clean (0 warnings); amdgpud/i915d/hello_linuxkpi all link against it. **Honest remaining gaps** (`docs/LINUXKPI_PHASE2.md`): C vararg printf formatter (format strings print verbatim today), host `DMA_PIN(va,len)→iova` for correct streaming DMA, struct page/scatterlist, workqueue/timer, and netdev/drm/cfg80211 subsystem facades. This is the symbol-linkage tranche; the per-subsystem facades are the next one.
- [~] **LinuxKPI host harness — hardware-free regression + driver-sequence framework (2026-06-11).** `tools/linuxkpi_harness/` (standalone crate, own `[workspace]`, like `tools/argon2_kat`) links the REAL `ath_linuxkpi` (new `hosttest` feature gates out the libc-shadow `string` symbols so it links into a std host binary) and runs **36 checks PASS** on the dev host, no QEMU/no iron: atomics + bitops (ring/IRQ flags), MMIO `readl`/`writel`/`readw`/`readb`, allocators incl. `kcalloc`/`kmalloc_array` overflow→null (heap-overflow CVE class), `kmemdup`/`kstrdup`; plus a **mock-GPU bring-up model** (init GO→READY handshake, 64-bit ring base/size programming, WPTR→RPTR drain) driven through the real `readl`/`writel`. Run: `cargo run --release --manifest-path tools/linuxkpi_harness/Cargo.toml`. **Next:** refactor amdgpud's actual stages (GMC/IH/SMU/GFX) into a testable lib the harness links, so the REAL bring-up sequence (not a representative model) is replayed against the mock register file before Athena.
- [~] LinuxKPI `request_firmware()` host call — **kernel/ABI side done (Opus)**: `SYS_LINUXKPI_REQUEST_FIRMWARE` (142, additive; `ath_abi` + `docs/SYSCALL_TABLE.md`), `linuxkpi_host::lkpi_request_firmware` loads `firmware/<name>` from initramfs and maps it into the daemon (`[user_virt,size]`); QEMU: `[linuxkpi] firmware host call wired: syscall=142 fw_probe=absent(ok)`. **Unblocks amdgpu/i915/iwlwifi firmware load.** C shim DONE (2026-06-10): `components/ath_linuxkpi/src/lib.rs` exports Linux-ABI `request_firmware`/`release_firmware` (+ `request_firmware_blob`/`self_test_firmware`) over syscall 142; amdgpud's `firmware_preflight` consumes it. **Bundling DONE (2026-06-10): xtask recursively bundles the entire `firmware/` tree** (`collect_files_recursive` — drop a blob in, it ships, no xtask edit); `firmware/amdgpu/` + `firmware/iwlwifi/` dirs created; per-device file manifest in `docs/FIRMWARE.md`. Verified `[xtask] Firmware blobs bundled: N` + `tar -tf` lists them. Remaining: fetch the redistributable blobs from linux-firmware (Phoenix GC 11.0.1 set + AX210 ucode — licensed, not committed) and drop in; end-to-end load on iron also waits on the daemon-chain resume bug.
- [~] **Linux x86_64 app ABI by construction (2026-06-10, Opus)** — SYS_SPAWN now dispatches on the ELF osabi byte: xtask stamps every workspace-built app + port from the ABI it actually speaks (`stamp_osabi`: 0xAE `ELFOSABI_ATHENAOS` native; `config/base.toml` `abi = "linux"` packages get 0x03), and `kernel/src/syscall.rs` routes non-native ELFs through `linux_exec` (Linux auxv stack, `mark_task_as_linux`, POSIX state + console fds). NOTE the trap this fixed: relibc-linked apps (hello_relibc, ports rustysd/rg) LOOK like Linux ELFs but speak NATIVE numbers (`athenaOS_syscall.rs`) — the osabi byte from the toolchain reflects the build target, not the ABI, so xtask stamps the truth. New `linux_hello/` fixture (raw Linux syscalls only: arch_prctl SET_FS/GET_FS + sched_yield×8 TLS-persistence check + write + exit_group; serial proof `[linux_hello] Linux ABI OK: TLS survived 8 yields`). Kernel TLS underpinning: `Task::fs_base` inherited from the live MSR at creation, persisted by Linux `arch_prctl(ARCH_SET_FS)` AND native syscall 126, conditionally restored at all 3 context-switch sites; `ARCH_GET_FS` does a real copyout; `ARCH_SET_GS` is refused by design (AthenaOS keeps the CPU id in user GS base — see gdt.rs — so honoring it would corrupt per-CPU state; x86_64 libcs use FS only). QEMU: boots clean, 0 panics. **End-to-end marker proof (8740/8770 + the linux_hello line) blocked by the native-ELF spawn frame-collision bug below.**
- [x] **Linux-ABI translation PROVEN on a real Linux ELF — iron (2026-06-24).** Closed the verification gap in the ~31-syscall `linux_syscall.rs` vein (was build-verified only): `kernel/src/linux_exec.rs` embeds a tiny static nostdlib raw-syscall probe (`tools/linux_abi_probe/`, built+validated on the Athena Arch box) and spawns it at boot through the same path AthBridge/Proton binaries use. **Athena KVM `-cpu host` (real Zen4) AND QEMU both print the full burst: `[linux-abi-probe] start → getrandom ok → sysinfo ok → uname ok → PASS`** (booted, 0 panic). FAIL-able: the probe self-checks each return value and writes `FAIL: <syscall>` + exits non-zero on any bad result; the kernel writes `[linux-abi] FAIL` on a spawn error. **Two real bugs fixed making this work:** (1) `linux_exec` tasks now BSP-pinned — APs `loop{hlt}` post-boot, so a Linux task on the default all-cores affinity starved on a halted AP (0 syscalls on real 12-core Athena; the multi-core correctness fix applies to ALL Linux binaries, not just the probe); (2) probe is `-fno-stack-protector` (no-TLS canary read from `%fs:0x28` else faults). **statx-on-a-directory bug — CONFIRMED then FIXED (2026-06-24).** Moving the probe's `statx("/")` to run *early* (right after the proven `start` write) made the burst stop dead at `start` — proving `statx("/")` stalled. Root cause: `posix::sys_stat` → `vfs::open_path` returns a `DirentStreamInode` for a directory, which **enumerates every entry** (a full readdir) just to `stat` it — and `stat("/")` could also fall through to the AthFS `find_or_create_file` fallback; it also hardcoded a regular-file mode for directories. Fix: `vfs::is_dir(path)` (traverse to the node only, never enumerate children; root/`/system`/`/proc` short-circuit with no lock) + `sys_stat` returns `S_IFDIR | 0755` fast for directories. **file read + mmap + file WRITE proven too:** the probe reads `/proc/version`, `mmap`s an anonymous RW page (writes a byte + reads it back — real backed memory, not a stub), and creates/writes/reopens/reads-back a `/tmp` file — the file-access + allocation + persistence primitives every real Linux binary needs (loaders, configs, heap/stack, saves). **This surfaced + fixed a real gap: `/tmp` (and `/dev/shm`) were mounted as tmpfs but never routed in `vfs::open_path_exact`, so a Linux binary could not use `/tmp` at all** — now wired (`tmpfs::open_or_create` + create-on-open at the mount root). **`clock_gettime(CLOCK_MONOTONIC)` proven too** — non-zero + monotonically advancing time, the frame-pacing primitive every game needs. **pipe IPC proven too** (`pipe2` + write + read-back). **QEMU AND Athena KVM `-cpu host` (real Zen4) print the full burst `start → statx ok → fileio ok → mmap ok → filewrite ok → getrandom ok → sysinfo ok → uname ok → clock ok → pipe ok → PASS`** (booted, 0 panic) — a real static Linux binary runs end-to-end on AthenaOS doing console I/O, stat, file read/write, mmap, system queries, monotonic time, and pipe IPC. **Biggest remaining unlock = threads (`clone` CLONE_THREAD is a stub → Proton/Wine, hence real Steam games, hang); scoped for a dedicated session in [[linux-clone-threads-scoping]].** See [[linux-syscall-oracle-gap-filling]].
- [x] **DYNAMICALLY-LINKED Linux ELF runs end-to-end via ld.so — iron (2026-06-25, commits 0cfb9f6 + adabc17).** The follow-on to the static-ABI proof above: stock Linux apps are nearly all dynamically linked, so this is THE unlock for real Linux-app support. `/bin/dh` (PIE, `NEEDED libc.so.6`, real glibc 2.43 bundled in `rootfs/`) prints **`dyn-hello-ok` on QEMU AND on the real Athena Ryzen (Zen4) over KVM `-cpu host`** (no flash; 0 PANIC, boot marker present). Full glibc dynamic path works: PT_INTERP detect → load `/lib64/ld-linux-x86-64.so.2` as PIE → ld.so self-relocates → opens+mmaps `libc.so.6` → versioned symbol resolution (incl. `_res@GLIBC_2.2.5`) → glibc startup (`arch_prctl SET_FS` TLS / `set_tid_address` / `set_robust_list` / `rseq` / `getrandom`) → RELRO `mprotect` → jump to the real entry → `printf`. **Four real loader/ABI bugs fixed, all found via a per-syscall trace (strace-equivalent) gated to the dynamic task:** (1) `install_console_fds` left fd 0 unset → ld.so's first `openat(libc.so.6)` got fd 0 (a std-stream slot) and never mapped libc → reserve fd 0; (2) `sys_stat`/`sys_fstat` returned constant `st_ino=0` → glibc dedups loaded objects by `(st_dev,st_ino)` so libc matched the main exe (also ino 0) and was skipped → unique nonzero `(st_dev, st_ino=inode ptr)`; (3) `sys_mmap` for `addr=0` returned `brk+0x100000` every call (no cursor) → ld.so's TLS block overlapped libc's symbol tables and TLS init clobbered `.gnu.hash` → advancing per-process `mmap_cursor` at 64 GiB; (4) `elf_loader::load_elf` relocated + set up the GOT for ALL objects → for a dynamic exe ld.so owns that, and the kernel-prefilled GOT sent the first lazy PLT call into dh's NX ELF-header page (#PF) → skip kernel reloc/GOT when `PT_INTERP` is present. **Iron-only flood fix (adabc17):** file-backed `MAP_FIXED` segment overlays hit the `PageAlreadyMapped` recovery once per page; libc's ~470 pages × ~5 ms/serial-line stalled the iron boot past the capture window → `sys_mmap` unmaps `MAP_FIXED` ranges first + the recovery is silent for same-frame remaps and rate-limited otherwise. Next: IFUNC (`R_X86_64_IRELATIVE`) resolvers + busybox/bash; multi-threaded dynamic binaries still need the `clone(CLONE_THREAD)` exit fix ([[linux-clone-threads-scoping]]). See [[ld-so-dynamic-linking-design]].
- [x] **Stock GNU coreutils binaries run end-to-end + initramfs directory enumeration — iron (2026-06-25, commits 859ce09 + b96936a + 64ef345 + 852e5e9).** Unmodified Arch `seq 5 8`→`5 6 7 8` and `cat /etc/motd`→`athena-cat-ok` both run on the real Athena Ryzen (Zen4) over KVM `-cpu host` (0 PANIC, boot marker), proving multi-arg argv + libc stdio/number-formatting + IFUNC string ops + **file read** (openat(O_RDONLY)→read→write) + clean exit for REAL Linux utilities via ld.so. `vfs::is_dir`/`list_dir_at`/`open_dir_as_dirent_stream` now enumerate initramfs directories (`/bin`,`/usr/lib`,`/lib64`) — a real app/file-manager can `stat`+`opendir`+`getdents64` them (FAIL-able kernel smoketest `[vfs] initramfs-dir … PASS` on iron). `posix::sys_ioctl` returns POSIX-correct ENOTTY (not EINVAL) for the TC*/TIOC* terminal class (every interactive tool's isatty path). OPEN: stock `ls` is 4 blockers deep (libcap dep bundled, but a 4th startup gap remains — parked, see [[ld-so-dynamic-linking-design]]); IFUNC-heavy / bash / busybox + the `clone(CLONE_THREAD)` thread-exit fix are the next unlocks.
- [x] PCI handoff to userspace driver via `sys_claim_device`
- [x] NVMe driver reads sector 0 (QEMU)
- [x] virtio-net + DHCP full DORA cycle (10.0.2.15 lease from QEMU)
- [x] smoltcp wired on virtio-net
- [x] CMOS RTC + TSC-anchored wall clock + `sys_wall_clock`
- [x] WireGuard Noise IKpsk2 handshake state machine
- [x] TLS 1.3 ClientHello framing
- [x] AthBridge: 16k Win32 names registered, top-20 kernel32 Phase B thunks
- [x] R10 4-artifact contract honored: every module ships init + smoketest + procfs + Concept docstring
- [x] /proc/athena/* snapshot dumped on every boot (28+ endpoints)
- [x] Userspace login screen renders at boot (supersedes kernel triangle)
- [x] AP LAPIC enable fix — all CPUs receive timer IRQs
- [x] x2APIC modernization (MSR access path) — implemented and verified in QEMU
- [x] SWAPGS pairing fix on non-canonical RCX kill path
- [x] virtio_net_hdr 10-byte fix unblocking RX

**Maintenance gates (CI / pre-commit when CI exists):**

## Phase 1 — Bare-metal first boot (Tier 0)

Goal: print `[ OS ] System successfully booted.` over serial on a real Beelink Athena. Nothing else has to work — no keyboard input expected after boot.

### 1.1 Boot media + UEFI

- [x] BIOS image built (`kernel.bios.img`)
- [x] UEFI image built (`kernel.uefi.img`)
- [x] UEFI image actually boots on Athena firmware — **FULL BOOT (BOOTLOG round 4, 2026-06-10): all 9 tiers + success marker + user_init spawned**. The historic Tier-8 freeze was `gpu::init`'s probe reading the AMD iGPU's BAR0 MMIO (data-fabric stall, no fault) — fixed config-space-only in e731c8d and confirmed on iron (`[gpu] AmdDiscrete: BAR0(MMIO)=… left untouched` → software fallback → boot continues).
- [x] Document "disable Secure Boot in firmware setup" path in README — `README.md` §Bare-metal bring-up: Del/F2 → Security → Secure Boot Disabled + OS Type Other OS; links `BARE_METAL_CHECKLIST.md` / `HARDWARE_PATH.md`; Athena USB boot steps. (Pure documentation; no hardware gate.)
- [ ] (Stretch) Microsoft-3rd-party-CA-signed shim or self-signed key enrollment workflow
- [ ] Serial console accessible via Athena's USB-C UART
- [x] Console output strategy when no serial cable: GOP framebuffer text fallback — `serial::_print` mirrors every line to `console::_print` (lock order SERIAL1→CONSOLE→FB); `console::run_boot_smoketest` logs `[console] GOP text fallback active: 160x100 cells (1280x800 px, serial mirrored)`; `[ OK ] UEFI GOP Debug Console live` rendered on the framebuffer. `framebuffer::draw_glyph_8x8` blits each cell with a single FB lock (was 64 `fill_rect` calls/char). QEMU UEFI proof: serial.log line 205. (On-screen visual confirmation folds into §1.9 Athena boot.)
- [~] Persistent boot log on the boot USB stick (`BOOTLOG.TXT`) — the no-serial/no-keyboard diagnostic channel for Athena. Three fixes landed 2026-06-09: (1) xtask bakes a pre-allocated 1 MiB `BOOTLOG.TXT` into every image's ESP (`DiskImageBuilder::set_file_contents`) so re-flashing no longer wipes it; (2) `bootlog_persist`/`fatfs_esp` now parse **FAT16** (`parse_vbr_any`) — the bootloader-crate ESP is FAT16 at ~27 MiB, which the old FAT32-only locator rejected, so the file was never found; (3) xHCI transfer rings no longer go phantom-full after ~254 TRBs (see Phase 2.1). Locate failures now log an exact per-device reason (`[bootlog-persist] usb0: no BOOTLOG.TXT (<step>)`). Bootlog RAM ring grown 256 KiB → 1 MiB to match file capacity so early-boot lines survive a full boot without ring wrap. QEMU proof (FAT16 USB-MSC test image, `--safe` build): `[bootlog-persist] ready: BOOTLOG.TXT on USB drive — 1024 clusters, 1024 KiB capacity, first LBA 2201` + `flush OK (full, early region locked)/(tail region) … cache_sync=OK`, log text verified inside `target/usb-msc.img` data clusters. Reader side: `scripts/read-bootlog.ps1` extracts BOOTLOG.TXT from the raw stick (no mounting — Windows refuses drive letters on removable-media ESPs); tested against both image layouts. On-screen channel: the safe-mode diag panel now includes `[usb-msc]`/`[block] registered` lines and, after the keyboard-less auto-advance, re-docks as a live right-side strip beside the desktop instead of vanishing (`[shell_runner] safe-mode: diag panel docked right (576x720 at x=704)`). Athena: flash current `--safe` image, boot, photograph the panel and/or read the stick with read-bootlog.ps1. **VERIFIED end-to-end on Athena 3× (2026-06-10): NVMe-ESP BOOTLOG.TXT captured and extracted with `read-bootlog.ps1 -Disk 0` each round — the logs drove five xHCI fixes + the gpu::init hang root-cause.** Hardened same day (ce48492/4a36820): per-tier + Tier-8 death-window checkpoint flushes (a HANG now pins the failing init), marker-inclusive final flush (a good boot's log ends with the success marker), procfs snapshot made COM1-only (was evicting the transcript from the ring), once-only best-effort flush in the #DF handler. Stick-resident copy still pending the stick enumerating (multi-controller xHCI).
- [ ] Verify bootloader 0.11 handles real GOP framebuffer modes (1080p/4K)
- [x] Verify `bootloader_api::info::BootInfo` real-iron MemoryMap parsed without panic — **PROVEN on Athena (BOOTLOG round 4, 2026-06-10):** the kernel consumed the real UEFI `BootInfo` (memory map + physical-offset + framebuffer) and the NUMA-aware buddy allocator came up `Node 0, 15843 MiB managed` (impossible without the iron memory map parsed cleanly), reaching `[ OS ] System successfully booted.` with 0 panics.

### 1.4 ACPI

- [x] RSDP / RSDT / XSDT parse

- [x] Fail-soft AML execution: `acpi_full::apply_platform_bringup` audits `_PIC`, `_OSI`, `_REG` calls; failures logged but kernel continues. Verified on QEMU DSDT. Exposes `/proc/athena/acpi`.
- [x] `_PIC(1)` AML call before enabling IOAPIC routing (mode switch from PIC to APIC) — safe invocation in `apply_platform_bringup`.
- [x] `_OSI("Windows 2020")` returns 1 (every laptop DSDT branches on it) - explicitly overridden using native method intercept.
- [x] `_OSI("Linux")` returns 0 (some DSDTs misbehave when Linux replies 1) - explicitly overridden using native method intercept.
- [x] AML method invocation logged so we can audit what fired during boot — `[acpi] Platform bring-up audit: N method(s) invoked` summary + per-method audit trail. QEMU proof: serial.log line 210.
- [x] DSDT executes to completion without panic on Athena's real tables — **IRON-CONFIRMED (photo, 2026-06-12): `acpi namespace init: 1637 objects` + `\_SB_.PCI0.RP01 registered` on the Beelink — namespace POPULATED on real firmware (was 0 devices for four rounds); full-log _PRT/EC evaluation detail pending netlog retrieval.** — **ROOT-CAUSED AND FIXED OFF-TARGET (2026-06-12): four parser bugs in the `aml` crate, not our ACPI layer.** The user dumped Athena's 40 raw tables to `firmware/acpi/athena-beelink-elitemini/` (DSDT + 22 SSDTs); the embed harness + the new host probe (`tools/aml_probe` — parses the REAL tables with the kernel's exact parser in milliseconds, `RUST_LOG=trace` gives a full parse trail) reproduced the empty namespace locally. The `aml` crate (0.16.4) is now VENDORED at `components/vendored/aml` via `[patch.crates-io]` with four fixes: (1) **IndexField (0x5B 0x86) unimplemented** — 4 in the DSDT; first one aborted the whole table (the `UnexpectedByte(91)`); implemented with real index/data access semantics (+ BankField 0x87, 42 across the SSDTs, with bank-select-then-access semantics); (2) **else-less `If` at the end of a term-list slice aborted the table** — `opcode()` returned a fatal `UnexpectedEndOfStream` on empty input where `choice!` needed a soft `WrongParser` to fall through DefIfElse's optional-else probe (Athena: `If(_OSI("Windows 2015"))` at the tail of `If(CondRefOf(\_OSI))`); (3) **field offsets/widths stream-validated as package lengths** — AMD's fabric-config Field skips 5.3 Mbit (`Offset(0xA3078)`) which is a raw bit count, not a stream-bounded PkgLength → switched field elements to `raw_pkg_length()`; (4) **load-time expression opcodes missing** — AMD computes OperationRegion offsets with `Add(AGRB, Or(ShiftLeft(DerefOf(Index(ADAT, n)))))`; implemented Subtract/Multiply/NAnd/Or/NOr/XOr/Mod/Not/SizeOf/DerefOf/Index. **Result: all 23 AML tables parse — namespace 159 devices / 2818 values (was 0)**; vendored crate's own suite 27/27. `[~]` pending the iron flash: expect `ACPI full subsystem initialized (37 tables, N devices)` with N≈159 and _PIC/_PRT/EC methods now resolving on Athena.
- [x] SSDT loading + dependency order
- [x] PCIe ECAM modernized discovery (MCFG -> AMD MSR -> Quirk) — `pcie::init` tries multiple sources; Zen 4 quirk (1022:14e8) added; safer `AtomicU64` base in `pci.rs`.
- [x] PCIe ECAM quirks for AMD Zen 4 host bridge
- [x] FADT register fields populated (PM1_EVT_BLK, GPE0_BLK) — `Fadt::parse` favors X-GAS (64-bit) fields; `GpeBlock` supports MMIO; `/proc/athena/acpi` reports source.
- [x] ACPI shutdown support (S5 soft-off) via `SYS_ATHENA_SHUTDOWN` (120) — requires `Cap::System { Rights::WRITE }`.
- [x] Embedded Controller (EC) at port 0x62/0x66 with `_REG` evaluation — `acpi_full::discover_ec` scans for `PNP0C09`; parses `_CRS` for ports and `_GPE` for bit; evaluates `_REG(3, 1)`.
- [x] GPE dispatcher: parse `_Lxx`/`_Exx` from `\_GPE`, dispatch on raise — SCI interrupt wired (IRQ 9 -> vector 0xF0); interrupt-driven GPE dispatch; power button handler logs and shuts down. Verified on QEMU DSDT.
- [x] DSDT `_PRT` packages parsed for PCI IRQ routing on real boards — `pci_irq::route_all_devices` active; hybrid internal/external evaluation survives QEMU and modern DSDTs. Verified: 128 entries parsed in QEMU. **IRON-CONFIRMED (full bootlog 2026-06-11T23:31): `\_PIC -> Integer(0)` evaluates and `[pci] Routing table: 84 entries parsed from _PRT` (17 _PRT methods, 20 at PCI0 root + 4 per GP bridge) on the Beelink — after the method-runtime opcodes (Acquire/Release/Sleep/Stall/Wait, commit e9e1e06) and the scan moving to the aml_context namespace.**
