### 1.5 Storage discovery

- [x] NVMe driver reads sector 0 on QEMU emulated controller
- [x] NVMe Identify Controller against Samsung 980 / WD SN770 / Crucial P3 — log real model; IEEE OUI parsing; model string trimming.
- [x] Tolerate Identify Namespace failures (skip + continue) — each inactive/errored NSID logged + skipped; bail after 16 consecutive misses; summary `[nvme] namespace scan: N active, M inactive, E errored`
- [x] Multi-namespace handling (pick lowest numbered with bootable signature) — `NvmeBlockDevice { nsid }` now per-NSID (was hardcoded to NSID 1); picker probes sector 0 of every active NSID, classifies as `GPT` / `MBR` / `AthFS` / `blank` / `unknown`, picks lowest with known signature, fallback to first active NSID. Logs `[nvme] nsid N: sector 0 = SIG` + `[nvme] boot disk candidate: nsid X (signature Y)`. Only registers as `ACTIVE_BLOCK_DEVICE` if no other driver claimed the slot first.
- [x] Admin queue depth negotiated, not hardcoded — derived as `min(MQES, page_capacity)` per ring (SQ 64 / page, CQ 256 / page); boot logs `[nvme] admin queue depths negotiated: SQ=N (page-cap S, mqes M), CQ=N (page-cap C, mqes M)`. CQ now 4× larger than the old hardcoded 64.
- [~] I/O queue per CPU — nvme.rs: init_per_cpu_queues() creates SQ+CQ per CPU at QIDs 5..8; submit_on_cpu() routes by cpu_id; QEMU verified 2026-06-02
- [x] NVMe controller reset on init (some firmware leaves bad state) — entry state logged; if `CC.EN && CSTS.RDY`, issue Normal Shutdown (CC.SHN=01b), wait for CSTS.SHST=complete, then clear CC.EN+SHN and wait for CSTS.RDY=0; bail with `BlockError::HardwareFailure` if RDY stuck high. QEMU proof: `[nvme] entry state: CC=0x460001 CSTS=0x1 (EN=true RDY=true CFS=false)` → `[nvme] normal shutdown completed cleanly` → `[nvme] reset OK`.
- [~] **NVMe WRITE fails on Athena — root cause found (photo #4, 2026-06-09): phantom-full submission queues.** The device reports its SQ consumption point in every completion (`sq_head`, NVMe §4.6) but the driver never applied it — `sq.head` stayed 0 forever, so `is_full()` went permanently true after `entries-1` commands and every later submit returned `QueueFull` silently (pre-poll, which is why the SCT/SC diagnostics never fired). Same bug class as the xHCI phantom-full transfer rings. On Athena NVMe is the ACTIVE boot device and absorbs all AthFS/FAT boot reads, so qid 1's accounting filled before the first bootlog write (lba 23024 % 4 → qid 1); on QEMU the active device is virtio and NVMe traffic never reaches the threshold. Fix: `poll_io_completion` + `poll_admin_completion` now credit `cpl.sq_head` back to the SQ. Also `write_sector` logs the concrete `BlockError` variant on failure (panel-visible). QEMU regression PASS. **CONFIRMED on Athena (photo #5): `[bootlog-persist] flush OK (full, early region locked) … on active block device` — the NVMe ESP write now succeeds, so `BOOTLOG.TXT` is readable on the internal disk via `scripts/read-bootlog.ps1 -Disk 0`.**
- [~] AHCI driver: detect, init, sector read smoketest — QEMU `ahci`+`ide-hd` LBA0 (`[ahci] smoketest PASS`); Athena TBD
- [~] AHCI quirks for AMD chipset SATA — `ahci.rs`: **BIOS/OS ownership handoff** (BOHC, AHCI spec 10.6.3) added to `AhciController::init()` — on real AMD FCH/SBxx boards UEFI/SMM owns the SATA HBA until the OS claims it (`CAP2.BOH` → set `BOHC.OOS`, wait `BOS` clears + `BB` clears), without which ports/writes wedge under SMM. `AhciQuirks::from_pci` flags AMD (0x1022) + legacy ATI (0x1002) and logs the AMD bring-up path. **A full `GHC.HR` HBA reset was tried and REVERTED** — it wipes the firmware-established port signatures and `detect()` runs before the per-port COMRESET, so it regressed the QEMU smoketest to "no active port" (caught + fixed same session); the per-port COMRESET in `port_reset()` clears stale state safely. QEMU `--disk=smoketest` regression-clean: `[ahci] port 0: Ata device` → `smoketest PASS … marker=MATCH`, handoff no-ops (no BOH/SMM on QEMU). Real AMD-SATA proof pending a SATA drive on an AMD board (Athena boots from NVMe).
- [~] Boot disk discovery: enumerate, identify by partition table or AthFS magic — `storage_mount::discover_boot_disk()` probes ACTIVE_BLOCK_DEVICE, detects GPT/MBR/AthFS-raw, scans ESP+AthFS partitions; QEMU: `[storage] boot disk: virtio-blk gpt sectors=2048 esp=true athfs=false` 2026-06-01; Athena NVMe pending

### 1.6 Time

- [x] HPET probe + spin_wait_us
- [x] TSC calibration from HPET
- [x] CMOS RTC read + epoch derivation
- [x] TSC invariance check (CPUID 0x8000_0007 EDX bit 8) — logged at boot
- [~] Fall-back to HPET when TSC non-invariant (currently warns only) — `rtc::on_hpet_ready()` switches wall-clock delta to HPET; boot log `[rtc] wall clock source: HPET (TSC non-invariant; period … fs)` on QEMU when CPUID invariant bit clear
- [~] HPET absence tolerated (some BIOSes hide HPET → fall back to PIT) — `hpet::note_absent()` + `pit_spin_wait_us` / `pit_spin_wait_10ms`; early `apic::calibrate_tsc()` uses PIT not dummy spin; `spin_wait_us` chain: HPET → TSC → PIT
- [x] **Per-CPU TSC sync verified on AP bringup — PROVEN on Athena (2026-06-24, fix-list #4 / Phase 4.8).** Replaced the old async max-min reading (which sampled each core's TSC at a *different boot instant* and reported the elapsed time between samples — ~593M cycles — as fake "skew", WARNing on every boot) with a Linux-style **pairwise warp test** run in lockstep BSP↔each AP during serial bringup (`smp.rs` `tsc_warp_source`/`tsc_warp_target`/`tsc_warp_loop`, `lfence`-bracketed `rdtsc`). It detects genuine cross-core monotonicity violations (a sample reading lower than the partner's strictly-earlier sample) and is immune to the old timing artifact. **Athena KVM `-cpu host`, all 12 Zen4 cores: `max_warp=0 cycles over 11 pairing(s), 0 warp event(s) (OK)`** — the TSCs were perfectly synchronized all along; the WARN was a measurement bug. QEMU SMP=1 (0 pairings) + SMP=2 (max_warp=0) clean across 6 boots; the lockstep rendezvous completed in every boot (no new race). Smoketest now reports `tsc_max_warp=…`.
- [x] PIT fallback path tested — `hpet::run_boot_smoketest` exercises `pit_spin_wait_us(500)` with TSC delta; QEMU: `[hpet] smoketest: pit_fallback_us=500 … -> PASS`

Fix: unread DMI no longer implies QEMU; the Zen-4 CPU check now runs first (Athena → `amd-generic-desktop` with real-hardware behavior incl. Bochs-VBE scanout attach), and only a non-Zen4 CPU with unread DMI keeps the historical QEMU assumption (QEMU-UEFI display path preserved; QEMU regression: still `profile = qemu`). Proper fix later: read SMBIOS entry from the EFI config table (needs bootloader to pass it). **Photo #3 showed `profile = qemu` persisting: the placeholder PRODUCT string is literally "AthenaOS QEMU", so the ungated `matches_qemu()` claimed the unread-DMI default before the CPU check ran. Now the QEMU match is only trusted when the DMI was actually read.** Athena retest pending (expect `amd-generic-desktop`).
- [x] Per-quirk regression tests so removing one is detectable — `hardware_profile.rs` `run_quirk_regression()` asserts every `PROFILES` entry still carries its exact golden quirk set (`QUIRK_GOLDEN`), that no golden id was deleted, and that every quirk bit any profile uses has a `decode_quirks` entry (`QUIRK_DECODE_COVERAGE`). Removing/adding a quirk now trips a boot FAIL line naming the added/removed mask. Also replaced the hardcoded `actual_cpus = 4` stub with the real `smp::ONLINE_CPUS` count. QEMU proof: `[hwprof] quirk-regression: 7 profile(s), used_mask=0x0000005e -> PASS` + `[hwprof] smoketest: 2 CPUs online matches profile qemu expected range`.

## Phase 2 — Bare-metal useful (Tier 1)

Goal: you can type at the kernel, the kernel reaches the network, knows what's plugged in, and survives long enough to do something.

### 2.1 USB stack (the single highest-leverage Tier-1 item)

- [~] `xhci.rs` — full driver in `kernel/src/xhci.rs`; QEMU `qemu-xhci` + tablet proves init; Athena/real iron TBD
- [~] `usb_core.rs` skeleton
- [x] xHCI controller enumeration from PCIe (class 0x0C, subclass 0x03, prog_if 0x30) — QEMU: `[xhci] found controller at 00:05.0`
- [x] xHCI capability register parse + operational registers initialized — QEMU: `[xhci] initialized: 64 slots, 8 ports`
- [x] Device Context Base Address Array (DCBAA) allocated — frame-allocator DMA page
- [x] Command Ring + Event Ring set up — frame-allocator DMA pages + ERST
- [x] Port reset + speed detection — smoketest: `Port 5: Device connected (Speed ID: 3)`
- [x] Device address assignment (`Address Device` command) — smoketest: `Enable Slot -> slot 1`, `Address Device OK`
- [x] Get Device Descriptor for each enumerated device — QEMU smoketest: `idVendor=0627 idProduct=0001` (BSR=0, EP0 doorbell target 1, IDT setup TRB)
- [x] Interrupt mapping: xHCI MSI-X vector → IRQ → polled event ring (MSI-X table logged; HID uses polled interrupt IN)
- [x] USB HID class driver (boot keyboard subclass) — SET_CONFIGURATION + interrupt IN in `xhci.rs`; `dispatch_boot_report` now bridges to input queue + focused task key buffer + legacy keyboard IPC/scancode path (`[usb-hid] smoketest legacy bridge: ... -> PASS`)
- [~] USB HID **mouse** + boot-protocol robustness — `find_hid_keyboard_interrupt` now captures the interface protocol (1=kbd/2=mouse); bring-up registers the correct `InputDeviceType`, sends `SET_PROTOCOL(boot)` + `SET_IDLE(0)` for boot devices (real keyboards power up in REPORT protocol), and `service_hid_reports` routes mouse reports to the existing `dispatch_boot_mouse` (cursor move + buttons + wheel) instead of the keyboard parser — the live USB mouse was previously dropped. QEMU (`usb-mouse` port 3): `Configure Endpoint (interrupt IN, mouse)`, `armed 3 HID interrupt-IN endpoint(s)`, no EP0 stall.
- [~] **Report-protocol HID (non-boot gaming devices) via Redox's parser (2026-06-16)** — boot-protocol-only decoding left gaming mice/keyboards that omit the Boot Interface Subclass dead-or-misparsed. Harvested the HID report-descriptor parser Redox uses (`usbhidd`→`rehid`→**`hidreport`**) into a new `#![no_std]` crate `components/athhid` (wraps `hidreport`, host-KAT'd 8/8: mouse/keyboard extract, signed deltas, `kind()`, boot-report bridges). Wired into `xhci.rs`: `bring_up_hid_keyboard_with_config` gates on `boot_capable` (subclass 1 + boot protocol) — boot devices keep the **exact** iron-proven path (`hid_device==None`); report-only devices get their report descriptor fetched (`get_hid_report_descriptor`, interface GET_DESCRIPTOR 0x22) + parsed by athhid, stored in `DeviceSlot::hid_device`. `service_hid_reports` decodes those (`extract_mouse`/`extract_keyboard` → `to_boot_report()` bridge → existing dispatch — no new input plumbing). **QEMU proof:** `armed 3 HID` (no regression) + live `report-protocol device — parsed 74-byte report descriptor, kind=Mouse` (usb-tablet). No new warnings; THIRD_PARTY_LICENSES + REDOX_EXTRACTION_MAP updated. Iron retest pending (the Athena HP keyboard still can't use it — it fails all multi-packet control reads, so the report-descriptor fetch itself times out).
- [~] **Multi-interface HID binding (composite gaming peripherals) (2026-06-16)** — `find_hid_keyboard_interrupt` bound only the FIRST HID interface, so a composite device (the Athena Razer 1532:0098 is a MOUSE whose interface 0 is a keyboard/media interface, with the pointer on a later interface — confirmed: athhid parsed iface 0 as `kind=Keyboard`) had its mouse interface NEVER bound → dead cursor (user-confirmed "no cursor"). Replaced with `find_all_hid_interfaces` (one endpoint per HID interface) + `DeviceSlot::hid_interfaces: Vec<HidInterface>`; `bring_up_hid_keyboard_with_config` configures every interrupt endpoint (incremental Configure Endpoint, ascending ep_index so context-entries only grows) → one SET_CONFIGURATION → per-interface boot/report protocol + register + arm. `arm_hid_interrupts`/`service_hid_reports` iterate all interfaces, matching completions by endpoint id. Each interface independently chooses boot vs athhid report decode. Host-KAT: `find_all_hid_interfaces` composite kbd+mouse descriptor (kernel cfg-test). QEMU: `armed 3 HID` + `1 interface(s) configured` per device + report-protocol parse + `found 2 MSC` — **no regression** (single-interface = 1-element Vec, identical path). Iron retest pending (does binding the Razer's 2nd/mouse interface move the cursor?).
- [~] **Bare-metal HID doorbell fix** — `doorbell_target()` was gated on `qemu_doorbell_offset` (true in QEMU, false off-QEMU), returning the DCI (`ep_index+1`) only in QEMU and bare `ep_index` (DCI−1) on real hardware. So on Athena the interrupt-IN endpoint was never rung: the mouse enumerated via EP0 (lit up) then was never polled → suspended → LED off (observed on Athena). Now `doorbell_target` **always** returns the DCI (`ep_index+1`) — standard on QEMU and real HW; this is also the `Endpoint ID` in transfer events, so completion matching now works on bare metal too. QEMU unchanged (`target=3`, smoketests PASS); Athena live-input retest pending.
- [~] **Phantom-full transfer ring fix (2026-06-09)** — nothing ever advanced `TransferRing::dequeue_index` on completion, so after `segment_size − 2` TRBs `is_full()` reported a permanently-full ring and every later enqueue failed with `RingFull`. The bulk-IN endpoint takes 2 TRBs per MSC sector read → all USB storage I/O died after ~120 reads (this is what killed the bootlog FAT-chain walk); HID interrupt-IN endpoints would equally stop after ~254 reports (≈127 keystrokes — a candidate cause for "keyboard/mouse stop working"). Fix: `poll_events` now credits each Transfer Event back to its ring (`note_transfer_completion`: slot/DCI from the event TRB, dequeue index from the completed TRB's pointer) — covers bulk, interrupt, and control consumers in one funnel. QEMU proof: 1000+-read FAT16 chain walk completes (`[bootlog-persist] ready … 1024 clusters`). Athena retest pending.
- [~] **Athena root cause found (2026-06-09, photographed on-screen panel): xHCI invisible to the pre-ECAM PCI scan.** Tier 6 USB bring-up ran BEFORE Tier 7 activated ECAM from ACPI MCFG; the legacy port-0xCF8 scan (bus 0..=8) saw 31 devices with **zero** USB-class controllers, while the post-ECAM re-scan saw 45. So on Athena the kernel never found the xHCI at all — keyboard, mouse, AND the USB bootlog stick all dead from one ordering bug (QEMU was immune: its xHCI sits on bus 0). Fix: Tier-7 **late USB bring-up** in `main.rs` — after `pci::refresh()` with ECAM active, if `xhci::is_initialized()` is false, re-run `xhci::init()` + enumeration/HID-arm + `usb_msc::init()`, all before `bootlog_persist::init` so the USB stick is still preferred for the log. QEMU regression: late path correctly not triggered, all USB smoketests PASS. **CONFIRMED on Athena (photo, 2026-06-09 second boot):** late bring-up found 6 USB controllers (xHCI 1022:15b9/15ba/15c0/15c1 on buses c4/c6 + two prog_if=0x40 USB4 routers), initialized c4:00.3 (64 slots, 7 ports), and saw 4 connected devices + an already-enabled USB3 port 6.
- [~] **Athena port-reset timeout (photo #2, 2026-06-09): every `reset_port` timed out.** Root cause: a fixed 100k-spin wait that expires in single-digit ms on 4+ GHz cores while a USB2 root-port reset holds ≥50 ms (TDRSTR) before PRC — instant-reset QEMU always passed. Same fixed-spin bug in `wait_for_command` (Address Device runs a real SET_ADDRESS bus transaction). Fixes: `reset_port`/`power_on_port`/`wait_for_command` now use HPET wall-clock waits (800 ms / 20 ms / 100 ms), `reset_port` accepts PR-cleared+PED-set (PRC consumed via event path), and **skips the reset entirely when PED is already set** (firmware-enabled USB3 port 6 — resetting a working link would drop it; PP-masking avoids the RW1C PED-disable trap). QEMU regression PASS. **Confirmed reset fixed on Athena (photo #3): all 5 ports reach `Enable Slot`.**
- [~] **Athena 64-byte context support (photo #3, 2026-06-09): every `Address Device` failed with `CommandFailed(ParameterError)`.** Root cause: Athena's xHC sets HCCPARAMS1.CSZ=1 (64-byte context entries; the smoketest even printed `context_64=true`), but the driver always built input contexts in the 32-byte-entry layout (`setup_address_context_routed`'s `_context_size_64` parameter was accepted and ignored) — the controller read garbage at every 64-byte boundary. QEMU never caught it (CSZ=0). Fix: `DeviceSlot::expand_input_context_csz64()` rewrites the compact image in place to 64-byte stride (entry k: 32k→64k, upper halves zeroed, backwards copy), invoked before Address Device and centrally in `configure_endpoint_with_ptr`; all OUTPUT device-context endpoint reads (EP0 dequeue-cycle sync, HID post-config, `sync_ep_enqueue_from_hardware`, `reset_ep0_pipe`, EP0-MPS write) now go through the stride-aware `output_endpoint()` accessor (slot context at entry 0 is layout-identical in the first 32 bytes, so `out.slot` reads were already safe). QEMU regression (CSZ=0 path byte-identical) PASS. **Photo #4: `Address Device OK (port 1)` + `slot state Addressed` — CSZ fix confirmed on iron.**
- [~] **Athena control-transfer HCE — root cause found (photos #4+#5, 2026-06-09): chained control-stage TRBs.** After `Address Device OK`, the first EP0 control transfer halted the controller: photo #5's new diagnostic read `USBSTS=0x00001019` → **HCH=true, HCE=true, HSE=false** = internal data-structure inconsistency, NOT a rejected DMA. Cause: `submit_control_transfer` set the Chain bit on the Setup and Data stage TRBs, merging the three stages into one malformed mixed-stage TD. A control transfer is THREE independent TDs (xHCI §4.11.2.2); the Chain bit links TRBs only WITHIN a TD. AMD's xHC validates this and halts with HCE; QEMU (and the previous all-passing smoketests) tolerates it. Linux never chains control stages. Fix: each stage is now a single-TRB TD with Chain=0 (Status keeps IOC=1, so the event flow — one completion event — is unchanged on QEMU). QEMU regression PASS. **CONFIRMED on Athena (photo #6): device descriptor now reads `idVendor=2109 idProduct=2822` (a VIA Labs hub on root port 1) — the chain fix worked.** The controller then HCE-halts deeper, inside that hub's enumeration, before the keyboard/mouse ports (2/4/5) are reached — symptom: "mouse lights up (bus power) but the cursor never moves" (its interrupt-IN endpoint is never armed).
- [~] **Hubs enumerated last; skipped on bare metal when direct HID is up (2026-06-09).** Because a buggy root-port hub HCE-halts the whole xHC and a halt kills every already-armed endpoint, the smoketest now DEFERS hub enumeration until all direct devices are brought up, then skips the (controller-halting) hubs on real hardware IF ≥1 direct HID device came up — so the keyboard/mouse on direct ports arm while the controller is healthy and aren't sacrificed to a flaky hub. QEMU (which never halts on hubs and tests a keyboard-behind-hub) always enumerates them, preserving coverage. this makes direct-attached input work regardless. **NOTE: photo #7 with hubs deferred proved the HCE is NOT hub-related** — see next item.
- [~] **Athena xHC HCE root cause (photo #7, 2026-06-09): per-control-transfer EP0 reset.** With hubs deferred, the controller halted on port 2's `Enable Slot` — the FIRST command after port 1's descriptor read — with the same `USBSTS HCH+HCE, HSE=false`. The on-screen panel is curated/lossy and dropped the real halting line, but `event ring dequeue_idx=7` (4 PSC + Enable + Address + GetDescriptor = exactly 7 events) proved events stopped *inside* port 1's `get_descriptor`, in `reset_ep0_transfer_ring`. That helper issued a **Stop Endpoint + clear-ring + Set TR Dequeue on EP0 after every single control transfer** (an old QEMU-era "clean ring" crutch) — AMD's xHC HCE-halts on that aggressive reset; QEMU tolerated it. Fix: removed all 6 per-transfer `reset_ep0_transfer_ring` calls (get_descriptor, control_in_vec, control_out_nodata, MSC + HID + hub bring-up). The EP0 ring now advances naturally across control transfers (Setup/Data/Status enqueue in sequence; the Link TRB handles wrap), which is the standard xHCI flow. The function is kept for genuine EP0 error recovery only. Athena retest pending — **this is the systemic fix: every device's enumeration past the first control transfer was being sabotaged.** **CORRECTION (2026-06-09): removing the reset unconditionally broke QEMU** — QEMU's xHCI emulation NEEDS the per-transfer EP0 rewind (without it its 2nd control transfer never completes → `armed 0 HID`). So the rewind is now **gated to QEMU only** (`rewind_ep0_if_qemu`), detected reliably by the xHCI controller's PCI vendor (Red Hat `0x1b36`) since QEMU-TCG doesn't set the hypervisor CPUID bit. Bare metal (AMD `0x1022`) skips the rewind (natural ring advancement, no Stop-Endpoint halt); QEMU keeps it. QEMU restored: `host=QEMU`, `MSC bring-up OK`, `armed 3 HID`.
- [~] **USB 3.x SuperSpeed handling distinct from 2.x** — `xhci_desc.rs` now parses the **SuperSpeed Endpoint Companion descriptor** (type 0x30, USB 3.2 §9.6.7) that follows each bulk endpoint on SS+ devices, extracting `bMaxBurst`; `prepare_configure_msc_bulk` applies it to the bulk endpoint contexts so the xHC issues multi-packet bursts on SS links (was hardcoded burst 0). USB2 devices have no companion descriptor → burst 0 (unchanged). QEMU proof (qemu-xhci SuperSpeed usb-storage on port 4): `[xhci] MSC: … speed=SuperSpeed burst[in=15,out=15] mode=SuperSpeed(burst)` + `MSC bring-up OK`. (HighSpeed/USB2 MSC path logs `mode=USB2(no-burst)`.)
- [~] **Athena real-device enumeration hardening (BOOTLOG rounds 1-3, 2026-06-10; commits df9e163/5ea4b49/4a36820):** five spec-compliance bugs that QEMU tolerates and AMD's xHC rejects, each photographed/logged then fixed: (1) zero recovery timing — added USB 2.0 TRSTRCY 10 ms post-port-reset + 2 ms post-SET_ADDRESS; (2) a halted EP0 was never recovered (one stall = device dead forever) — added `recover_ep0` (Reset Endpoint DCI 1 + ring reset + Set TR Dequeue) with one-retry descriptor reads; (3) FullSpeed EP0 max-packet hardcoded 8 — added 8-byte-first read + Evaluate Context update (**verified on iron: `slot 2 FS EP0 max packet 8 -> 64`**); (4) hub descriptor type hardcoded 0x29 — USB3 hubs need 0x2A + SET_HUB_DEPTH (descriptor verified on iron; SET_HUB_DEPTH timed out on the VIA hub → EP0 recovery added); (5) interrupt-endpoint Interval written as raw bInterval — the field is a 2^I × 125 µs exponent (LS/FS legal range 3..=10) — **fix verified on iron: the user's Razer (1532:0098) fully enumerates and arms: `ConfigureEndpoint OK slot=2` → `armed 1 HID interrupt-IN endpoint(s)`**. OPEN: only the FIRST of Athena's four xHCI controllers (c4:00.3) is bound — devices on c4:00.4/c6:00.3/c6:00.4 port groups (incl. the boot stick, most likely) are invisible → multi-controller bring-up is the next 2.1 slice; the port-4 LowSpeed device still stalls GET_DESCRIPTOR after recovery+gentle-read; live HID input events at the desktop pending the post-e731c8d flash.
- [~] **Multi-controller xHCI bring-up (commit 73dcde1, 2026-06-10) — CODE-COMPLETE, iron-verify pending.** `init()` now binds EVERY xHCI function (first → `XHCI_CONTROLLER` primary, rest → `XHCI_SECONDARY` Vec); `run_boot_smoketest` runs the full enumeration sweep per controller; the HID input thread services all controllers; `UsbMscDevice` carries a `controller` index (slots are per-controller) and all bulk/control transfers route via `xhci::with_controller`. Closes the "keyboard only works in some ports / boot stick never appears as MSC" structural gap on Athena's 4-controller (AMD Phoenix) topology. cargo check clean; QEMU regression + Athena flash (`initialized (secondary #N)`, Razer in any port, stick as MSC) pending.
- [x] HID report parsing — boot protocol 8-byte keyboard format (`usb_hid.rs`)
- [x] Keyboard event delivery to `input` event queue (`push_event` KeyDown/KeyUp)
- [x] HID boot mouse parser — 3/4-byte report (`usb_hid::dispatch_boot_mouse`) with button-diff state machine + motion + wheel; smoketest 3 frames → 1 btn_down / 1 btn_up / 1 motion / 1 wheel → PASS
- [x] Mouse event delivery to compositor pointer — boot HID mouse reports now mirror PS/2 routing (`compositor::move_cursor`, focused task `push_mouse`, shell + IPC channel 2); verified in USB-HID smoketest bridge counters
- [~] USB MSC class driver (for install media on USB enclosures) — **now works end-to-end in QEMU**. `xhci::bring_up_msc` classifies the device from its config descriptor (`xhci_desc::find_msc_bulk`), configures BOTH bulk endpoints via Configure Endpoint (`prepare_configure_msc_bulk`), and SET_CONFIGURATION; `usb_msc.rs` then runs INQUIRY/READ_CAPACITY/READ(10) over the BOT protocol and registers a `BlockDevice`. Fixed two real bugs: the `ep_index` off-by-one (`ep_index_for` now uses `xhci_ep_index` = DCI−1) and a GET_MAX_LUN data-IN transfer with a null buffer that aborted QEMU. QEMU proof (16 MiB `usb-storage`): `[usb-msc] slot=1 … blocks=32768 bsize=512`, `[usb-msc] smoketest: msc_devices=1 … read0_ok=true sig_ok=true -> PASS` (sector-0 signature read back through the full CBW→data→CSW path). Real USB flash drive on Athena still pending hardware validation, but the driver is functionally complete.
- [~] USB hub support (boot from device behind hub) — `xhci.rs` `enumerate_hub()`: hub descriptor parse, per-port PORT_POWER/PORT_RESET, route-string + TT addressing (`address_device_routed`), recursion for nested hubs; QEMU `usb-hub` + keyboard behind it: `[usb-hub] slot 2 is a hub: 8 ports`, `downstream slot 3 ... HID behind hub: ... OK`, `armed 2 HID interrupt-IN endpoint(s)`; real hardware pending Athena. **MSC behind a hub now works (2026-06-11):** hub children get the FULL classification (UAC→MSC→HID via the shared `classify_and_bring_up`) instead of the old HID-only assumption that made a boot stick in a front (hub-routed) port permanently invisible; the bare-metal hub-skip policy now skips hubs only when direct HID **and** direct MSC are both already up (no stick visible ⇒ hubs are searched). QEMU regression: second `usb-storage` behind the hub at port 2.2 → `[usb-hub] USB Mass Storage: bulk endpoints configured + SET_CONFIGURATION OK (slot 7)` + `[usb-msc] found 2 MSC device(s)` + bootlog `READY`. Plus a one-photo `[usb-summary]` block at end of boot (controllers bound/failed, per-controller ports/slots, MSC/HID/hub counts, USB4-port warning, bootlog READY/NOT-READY) + `bootlog_persist::retry_if_not_ready()` end-of-boot rescan — the next Athena photo answers the stick question even if it still fails.

### 2.2 Real network drivers

- [~] Intel I225-V / I226-V (2.5 GbE) — **full `IgcDriver`** in `igc.rs`: Intel "advanced" 16-byte descriptors + per-queue enable (RXDCTL/TXDCTL), 64-entry RX/TX rings, RCTL/TCTL/SRRCTL(adv,2K,drop_en) config, MAC from RAL/RAH + address-valid filter, 2.5G link/speed detect, IOMMU-sandboxed DMA, full `NetDriver` trait; `igc::probe(&mut mgr)` registers it as eth{N}. With the Realtek r8169 driver this covers BOTH dominant 2.5 GbE NICs on modern gaming boards. QEMU regression-clean (QEMU has no igc emulation → probe finds none; boot + netdrv smoketest PASS). Data path **iron-verified, not QEMU-verifiable**; real-hardware RX/TX pending an I225/I226 board.
- [~] Intel I219 (mainstream laptops/desktops) — `net_drivers::probe_i219()` scans 15 PCI IDs (0x15B8..0x0D55), resets via CTRL bit 26, reads MAC from RAL/RAH, checks link; QEMU: `[i219] Intel I219 not found (expected on QEMU)`; real hardware pending
- [~] Realtek RTL8169 / RTL8168 / RTL8111 / RTL8125 — **real `RtlDriver` implemented** (`net_drivers.rs`, `probe_rtl`): the r8169 family over the shared "C+" 16-byte descriptor model (one driver for 1GbE 8169/8168/8111 + 2.5GbE 8125, as Linux does). Soft reset, MAC from IDR0-5, 64-desc RX/TX rings with OWN/EOR/FS/LS, RCR/TCR/CPCR(MULRW+DAC)/RMS/MTPS config, `Cfg9346` lock dance, `TPPoll` NPQ tx kick, PHYstatus link/speed (8125→Gbps2_5), IOMMU-sandboxed DMA, full `NetDriver` trait. Bound for 0x10EC:{8169,8168,8161,8125,8136}; MMIO from BAR2→BAR1→BAR0. QEMU regression-clean (probe finds no device — QEMU only emulates the ancient rtl8139; boot + netdrv smoketest PASS, virtio-net unaffected). Data path is **iron-verified, not QEMU-verifiable** (no r8169 emulation); real-hardware RX/TX + 8125 2.5G tuning pending a gaming board. **IRON PROGRESS (Athena photo, 2026-06-12): `net_init: wired ok` + `dhcp! net0: link up, broadcasting` — the RtlDriver binds the 8125, reads PHY link-up, and transmits DHCPDISCOVER on real silicon; lease/RX confirmation pending netlog retrieval.** **IRON TX CONFIRMED (netlog capture 2026-06-12): `[rtl] TX path LIVE: first descriptor consumed by NIC (dev 8125, doorbell 0x90)` — the 8125 doorbell fix works; the bootlog itself arrived over the LAN via these frames (73/73 netlog chunks at the listener). RX still dead (DHCP Selecting) — RX_FETCH_DFLT_8125 RxConfig fix landed, next boot verifies.** **IRON 2026-06-13 (`bootlog-2026-06-13T1844`): RX STILL dead — the RX_FETCH fix did NOT close it. New diagnostic: the chip enumerates as `[rtl8169] Found Realtek NIC 10ec:8125` (the unified RtlDriver claims it + does TX) while a SEPARATE `[net] ... -> rtl8125 (pending)` registration never activates — likely a double-bind / wrong-owner-for-RX. Live DHCP: `kick_discovery emitted=true` then `state=Selecting` after 64 ticks (no OFFER). Next: audit the 8125 RX descriptor ring (OWN-bit/RxConfig/RMS) under the RtlDriver and resolve the dual rtl8169/rtl8125 registration.** **RX FIXED ON IRON 2026-06-13 (`bootlog-2026-06-13T1921`): `[rtl] RX path LIVE: first frame received (141 bytes, dev 8125)`** — the localizer (`[rtl] RX armed: RCR=0x4002e70e CR=0x0c rx_desc_own=64/64 RE=true`) showed the ring was armed correctly all along; the act of READING BACK `RTL_RCR`/`RTL_CR` right after RX-enable flushed the posted MMIO write that turns the receiver on (posted-write-needs-readback, CLAUDE §10 class). The `rtl8125 (pending)` line was a red herring (informational registry entry). **RX is now `[x]` iron-proven.** DHCP-to-Bound was then blocked by a SECOND, separate bug (below).
- [x] Driver selection table: PCI vendor/device → which driver — `net_drivers::PCI_NET_TABLE` + boot log `[net] pci VVVV:DDDD @ BDF -> driver (status)`; `/proc/athena/network`
- [~] System-wide HWID → driver-package manifest (auto driver scan + install — step 1: Scan + Match) — `kernel/src/driver_manifest.rs` scans PCI (`scan_pci`) and matches every `(vendor,device,class,subclass)` to a driver package classified Builtin / LinuxKpi / None (`match_pci`, exact-ID overrides + class fallback). `required_linuxkpi_packages()` yields the per-machine install set the installer copies + the driver-manager daemon launches (each then `sys_claim_device`s). `/proc/athena/drivers` emits the hardware list + matched driver. ### 2.4 Power management

- [~] `power.rs`, `power_supply.rs`, `thermal.rs`, `cpufreq.rs` modules — fuel gauge proven by `power_supply::run_boot_smoketest`. - [~] Battery polling path now runs periodically from LAPIC timer tick (`power::on_timer_tick` → `battery::poll`); boot proof via `[power] telemetry: ...` and `/proc/athena/power`
- [~] AC adapter telemetry exposed via `/proc/athena/power` (`ac_connected` from battery/charging state); direct AML `_PSR` method polling still pending

- [~] Sleep button `_SLPB` — `power_events::check_sleep_button()` scans `\_SB.SLPB._STA` + GPE table for SLPB/SBTN; `notify_sleep_button_pressed()` latches for S3 entry; QEMU: not found (expected); Athena pending
- [~] `_PSV` (passive cooling) threshold → frequency clamp — `power_events::check_thermal_throttle()` + boot smoketest; QEMU: paths exercised (`thermal_zones=0` expected); Athena pending
- [~] `_CRT` (critical) threshold → emergency shutdown — `power_events::check_critical_temp()` + boot smoketest; QEMU: paths exercised; Athena pending
- [~] CPU P-state transitions (cpufreq governor) — `cpufreq::on_timer_tick()` reads per-CPU load, calls `apply_governor_decision()` via IA32_PERF_CTL every 100 ticks; QEMU: `[cpufreq] smoketest PASS`; real AMD/Intel hardware pending
- [x] CPU C-states (cpuidle entry/exit) — `cpuidle.rs`: detects C0/C1 from CPUID leaf 5, `enter_idle()` uses HLT, `enter_mwait()` for deeper states; QEMU: `[cpuidle] C-states: [C0, C1] -> PASS` 2026-06-01
- [~] **S3 suspend → RAM + REAL resume — FULL ROUND-TRIP QEMU-PROVEN (2026-07-02, opus; iron pending).** `suspend::enter_s3()` now runs the complete ACPI §16.1 cycle both ways: FACS firmware waking vector → the shared AP boot trampoline at 0x8000 (a FACS wake enters real mode exactly like a SIPI, so the same blob walks the woken BSP real→protected→long mode) → naked `s3_resume_entry` (restores GDTR/IDTR/CR4/CR3/CR0/segments off `SLEEP_SAVE_AREA` blobs) → setjmp/longjmp back into `enter_s3` via `s3_asm_sleep`/`s3_asm_resume_tail` → TR reload (busy-bit clear + ltr), syscall-MSR re-program (registers only — the per-CPU block keeps the live task's `kernel_stack_top`), x2APIC + LAPIC-timer re-init. APs are quiesce-parked pre-sleep (a RENDEZVOUS, not a blind INIT — each AP acks from its lock-free idle-loop top then cli-halts; an async INIT once stranded a heap lock and deadlocked the re-online) with their queued tasks migrated to CPU0, **and RE-ONLINED after the wake** (`smp::reonline_aps_after_resume` re-runs the full bring-up incl. a fresh tagged-CAS warp pairing; needed `hpet::reenable_after_resume` — the wake-side reset freezes the HPET counter and every spin-wait hung). Wake source: CMOS RTC alarm (+3 s, BCD-aware) + `PM1_EN.RTC_EN`. **Proof (hypervisor-gated smoketest in the deferred sweep, every QEMU boot): the guest REALLY suspends at SLP_EN and wakes via firmware — `[suspend] S3: WOKE via FACS trampoline (PM1_STS=0x8401, rtc_wake=true)` then `[suspend] S3 round-trip: slept_and_woke=true wake_rtc=true lapic_timer_live=true … -> PASS`, boots continue to `boot health 7/7` with 0 panics at SMP=1 (on-demand trampoline deploy), SMP=2 (aps_parked=1) and SMP=4 (aps_parked=3).** **Full-SMP restore proven: `aps_parked=1 aps_reonlined=1` (SMP=2) and `aps_parked=3 aps_reonlined=3` (SMP=4) `-> PASS`.** Iron half pending: real-hardware S3 is user-triggered (_SLPB/power menu — the smoketest never sleeps bare metal) + device re-resume (NVMe/xHCI/NIC callbacks). Commits `6e6c846` + `1e38701`.
- [ ] S0ix modern standby (Intel firmware-driven) — out of scope for initial release
- [x] D-state per device (suspend devices when system suspends) — `pci_pm.rs` (2026-06-12): boot-time registry of every PM-capable PCI function (cap 0x01, PMC D1/D2 support decoded, live PMCSR state), `set_state` with the W1C trap handled (PME_Status bit 15 masked on writes so a state change never eats a pending wake event), `suspend_all`/`resume_all` for the S3 path (bridges + display held back). QEMU proof: `[pci-pm] smoketest: state_encode=true pmcsr_w1c_mask=true live(0 dev)=true -> PASS` — encoding + write-mask math proven pure; QEMU's i440FX-class devices expose NO PM capability (explicitly logged), so the live PMCSR write+readback proves on Athena where every modern device has one. `/proc/athena/pci_pm`. Remaining: S3 itself (separate item) wiring suspend_all/resume_all, iron.
- [~] Battery low warning → safe shutdown at threshold — `power_events::check_battery_threshold()` reads capacity, calls `power_off()` at ≤5% while discharging; QEMU: no battery present; Athena pending
- [~] Display brightness control (ACPI `_BCM` or backlight class) — `power_events::set_brightness()` tries `\_SB.PCI0.GFX0.LCD._BCM` + fallbacks; QEMU: methods absent (expected); Athena GPU pending

### 2.5 GPU on real iron

- [x] No-acceleration baseline — GOP framebuffer + software rasterizer active; compositor blits software surfaces; login screen renders at boot
- [~] AMD GPU (Radeon 780M iGPU on Athena) — userspace Mesa via LinuxKPI host — host bridge ready (`docs/LINUXKPI_PHASE2.md`); Mesa/amdgpu daemon port pending
- [~] Intel GPU (UHD/Xe) — userspace Mesa via LinuxKPI host — host bridge ready; Mesa/i915 daemon port pending
- [ ] NVIDIA GPU — out of scope for 1.0 (nouveau/proprietary blob both expensive)
- [~] Mode set: change framebuffer resolution at runtime — `gpu::request_display_mode` + `framebuffer::set_mode` + compositor resize; QEMU: `[gpu] smoketest: SetMode 1024x768 OK`, `[fb] mode_set … count=1` (Bochs VBE on stdvga); Athena GOP/DRM pending
- [ ] Multi-monitor: independent framebuffers
- [~] VRR negotiation — compositor.rs: negotiate_vrr(48,144) registers 48-144Hz range; vrr_registered=true; pending GPU driver for actual modesetting
- [~] HDR metadata pipeline — compositor.rs: enable_hdr_pipeline(400,9) registers 400nit BT.2020; hdr_registered=true; pending GPU driver for 10/12-bit output
- [~] Hardware cursor (acceleration is otherwise irrelevant if cursor lags) — `virtio_gpu.rs` (2026-06-12): brought up the dedicated virtio-gpu **cursor queue** (queue index 1, its own split-virtqueue via `setup_queue`) carrying `UPDATE_CURSOR` (0x0300, binds a 64×64 cursor resource at a hotspot) + `MOVE_CURSOR` (0x0301, reposition only) — a separate plane so cursor motion never queues behind frame/scanout submission on the controlq. QEMU proof: `[vgpu] cursor smoketest: cursorq=present update_cursor=true move_cursor=true -> PASS` (cursor resource created on the controlq, both cursor-queue commands consumed off the used ring). Surfaced a real QEMU detail: virtio-gpu pushes cursor commands with len=0 and writes NO response header, so the submit timeout sentinel became `u32::MAX` and `submit_consumed` detects success by used-ring advance. `/proc/athena/virtio_gpu` reports `hw_cursor`. Remaining: repoint the compositor's software cursor onto this plane + the real amdgpu/i915 cursor on iron.

### 2.6 Audio

- [x] HDA detection — **Athena (BOOTLOG round 3, 2026-06-10): `[audio] found HDA controller at c4:00.1 BAR0=0xdc5c8000`, `GCAP=0x4001 out=4`** (QEMU has no HDA: `no HDA controller found` is the correct negative there)
- [x] Deterministic test-tone path wired (`audio::run_boot_smoketest` enqueues 440 Hz square wave into the real-time ring; boot proof: `[audio] test-tone smoketest: wrote_samples=... -> PASS`; `/proc/athena/audio` now reports test-tone counters)
- [x] HDA controller init on real iron — **Athena: `HDA controller initialised at BAR 0xdc5c8000` + SCHED_BODY audio thread spawned (2026-06-10)**
- [x] HDA codec enumeration — audio.rs discover_codec(); **Athena: `STATESTS=0x0001`, `codec 0 discovered` (2026-06-10)**
- [~] Pin complex / widget walking — audio.rs: output pin + DAC found in codec graph; Athena pending
- [x] PCM playback (test-tone stream engine) — audio.rs: stream descriptor + DMA buffer + fmt 0x4011; **Athena: `test-tone smoketest: wrote_samples=960 hda_playback=1 -> PASS` (2026-06-10) — the HDA stream ran on real silicon; audible-output confirmation (speakers/jack) still pending a human ear**
- [~] PCM capture — audio.rs: capture ring + mmio_read_capture_pcm(); Athena pending
- [~] DMA position reporting — audio.rs read_dma_position() reads SDLPIB; Athena pending
- [~] Concept §AthAudio: sub-3ms round-trip on certified hardware (measurement harness) — **the output-path INSTRUMENT lands (2026-07-02, `audio.rs`)**: `output_latency_snapshot()` = ring backlog ÷ 48 kHz = the wait a fresh sample faces before HDA DMA consumes it, exposed at `/proc/athena/audio` (`output_latency_us`) beside the existing wake-jitter (`<100 µs`, `/proc/athena/perf`) + underrun counters. FAIL-able smoketest (`[audio] output-latency instrument: backlog=480 frames @ 48000 Hz -> 10000us queued … -> PASS` — the just-queued 10 ms test tone; zero/absurd values FAIL). Remaining for `[x]`: read the steady-state number on iron + the capture-side half of true round-trip.
- [ ] Sound Open Firmware (SoF) DSP loading for newer Intel chips
- [~] USB audio class driver (DAC headphone amps) — `usb_audio.rs` UAC1/UAC2 descriptor parser (Format-Type-I PCM, terminal/endpoint walk) now wired into the **real** xHCI enumeration path: a device with an AUDIO-class interface is parsed via `usb_audio::parse_config` and its playback/capture streams logged (`xhci.rs` classifier — UAC checked before MSC/HID). **QEMU-VERIFIED end-to-end against a real device** (added `usb-audio` on an 8-port `qemu-xhci`): detection → **isochronous bring-up** → DATA transfer. `xhci.rs` now has the isoch transport: `prepare_configure_isoch_out` (EP type IsochOut + Max-ESIT-Payload/mult/interval/CErr=0), `set_interface` (SET_INTERFACE alt-1 to arm the stream), `submit_isoch_transfer` with the SIA (start-ASAP) bit, and `bring_up_audio` orchestrating Configure-Endpoint(isoch) → SET_CONFIGURATION → SET_INTERFACE → isoch TD. Boot log: `isoch_ep=0x1(idx1) mps=192` → **`isoch OUT transport OK: 192 bytes accepted by the DAC`** (the isoch transfer event came back — real data flow), MSC + HID regression-clean, synthetic smoketest still PASS. **This lands the isochronous TRANSPORT** (unlocks USB webcams etc. too). `play_test_tone` then streams a 440 Hz tone through a **multi-buffered isoch ring** (DEPTH=4, refill-on-completion) — the correct continuous-playback architecture. The ring-prime depth streams cleanly, BUT sustaining the stream past it stalls: an isochronous endpoint **STOPS when its ring underruns** (unlike interrupt EPs, which re-arm fine through the same `enqueue_transfer`), so re-arming a stopped isoch EP needs an explicit restart, not just a doorbell — boot log `streamed 4/32 frames … multi-buffered prime drained; sustained stream pends isoch underrun-restart`. Remaining for full playback: **isoch endpoint restart-on-underrun** (the open item; may also be a QEMU isoch-model limit — same TDs work on the prime), UAC2 clock/sample-rate control (SET_CUR), and capture (isoch IN). Still no regression: MSC + HID + boot clean.
- [ ] Bluetooth audio (after Bluetooth stack)
